601 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Falk


CASE NO. 97-1227


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


724 So. 2d 146; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 15351; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2697



December 9, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 11, 1998. Rehearing Denied February 10, 1999. Released for Publication February 10, 1999. Petition for Review Denied August 9, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1430.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Leonard E. Glick, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. F96-29813.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) that dismissed its prosecution of defendant attorney under Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(9) on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV, and Fla. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: A prosecution against defendant attorney for unlawful solicitation of clients involved in motor vehicle accidents in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(9) was dismissed on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the trial court was in error in granting the defendant's motion to dismiss predicated upon a finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(9) was unconstitutional on U.S. Const. amend. I grounds. The appellate court held that the record, including the information filed by the state, was insufficient to support such a finding. The court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(9) did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Fla. Const. art. I, § 2, where a rational basis existed for the disparate treatment of those who solicited motor vehicle claims. The appellate court reversed the dismissal predicated on First Amendment grounds and remanded with directions to permit the state to amend the information to specify what act or acts of defendant were alleged to have violated the statute. The appellate court reversed the dismissal as it pertained to the equal protection challenge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of a case against defendant attorney for unlawfully soliciting clients and remanded with directions to allow the state to specify, with particularity, which of defendant's acts were alleged to have violated the statute in question. The statute was constitutional under the equal protection clause, and the charges were insufficient to support a finding of its unconstitutionality on First Amendment grounds.

 

602 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Brunetti v. Saul


CASE NO. 98-0256


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


724 So. 2d 142; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 15038; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2619



December 2, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1999. Released for Publication January 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Catherine M. Brunson, Judge; L.T. Case No. CD 96-7845 FY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit (Florida) providing for visitation by appellee maternal grandparents of an out-of-wedlock child whose mother was dead, under Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01.


OVERVIEW: Appellee maternal grandparents were awarded visitation of a child who had been born out of wedlock, but whose mother had died. Appellant father had been actively involved in the child's life, and the child had lived with him since the mother's death. The court found that appellees were relying upon Fla. Stats. ch. 752.01(d), providing for grandparent visitation rights where children were born out of wedlock. Based on the reasoning that Fla. Stats. ch. 752.01(e) had been held unconstitutional in the case of a child born into a marriage where the mother was deceased, because the father had a right of privacy, the court held that it followed that the father of an out-of-wedlock child had that same right of privacy. Fla. Stats. ch. 752.01(d) was therefore also unconstitutional. Further, appellees could not rely upon grandparent visitation provided by Fla. Stats. ch. 61.13(1)(a) because that was applicable only where there was a pending paternity proceeding, which was not true in the instant case. The lower court's order was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order which provided for visitation by appellee maternal grandparents of an out-of-wedlock child whose mother was deceased. The applicable statute, Fla. Stats. ch. 752.01(d), violated the right of privacy of the appellant father and was therefore unconstitutional.

 

603 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Fuchs v. Robbins


CASE NOS. 98-275, 98-274


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


738 So. 2d 338; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 14667; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2529



November 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted En Banc June 30, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 9590. Released for Publication July 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Margarita Esquiroz, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 93-21009.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) adopting the general master's report upholding appellee property appraiser's full valuation of appellant's building, although it was not substantially completed at the beginning of the tax year. The general master had found Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042, which provided that no value should be placed on buildings not substantially complete, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property appraiser assessed the land and building of appellant taxpayer at its full value, although the building was not substantially completed. Appellant sought review by the value adjustment board, which reduced the valuation. Appellee brought an action in the lower court to defend his original assessment. The lower court appointed a general master hear the matter; his recommendation, adopted by the trial court, upheld the original assessment on the basis that Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042, which provided that no value be placed on a building not substantially completed, was unconstitutional. Appellant argued that appellee did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of a statute. The appellate court noted that, where appellant brought the operation of a statute into question, appellee, a constitutional officer, did, in defense, have standing to question the validity of the statute. However, Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042 was constitutional because it did not create an additional exemption in violation of Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4, but merely related to the timing of the valuation and assessment of incomplete improvements to real property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order upholding appellee property appraiser's full valuation of appellant's building. Because the building was not substantially completed, it should not have been assessed for that tax year, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042.

 

604 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Sarnoff


CASE NO. 97-4803


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


734 So. 2d 1054; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 14397; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2520



November 12, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Frederick B. Tygart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of motor vehicles sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), denying appellant's change of venue motion in appellees' class action suit alleging arbitrary application of Fla. Stat. ch. 325.214.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxpayers filed a class action lawsuit against appellant state department of motor vehicles, contending that the Clean Outdoor Air Law, Fla. Stat. ch. 325.214, was unconstitutional because appellant assessed automobile inspection fees from the drivers of six counties but placed the fees in a fund earmarked for use by the entire state. Appellant sought to use its home venue privilege to transfer venue. Appellees claimed that the "sword wielder exception" prevented the transfer because appellant mandated that each motorist pass emissions inspection tests each year and pay registration fees. The trial court denied the motion to transfer. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for grant of the motion. The fee assessment was not an action justifying the application of the "sword wielder exception" because appellant had not yet enforced the statute against violators. Appellant was entitled to home venue privilege because appellees sought a determination of their rights under ch. 325.214.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the change of venue motion and remanded for grant of the motion; because appellees sued to determine the constitutionality of a statute not yet enforced against offenders, appellant could assert home venue privilege.

 

605 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


O. C. v. State


CASE NO.: 97-3075


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


722 So. 2d 839; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 14041; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2465



November 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Bob Wattles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), convicting appellant of attempted aggravated battery to cause great bodily harm and misdemeanor battery, finding that appellant was to be considered a gang member in order to enhance the sentence under the Criminal Street Gang Prevention Act of 1996, Fla. Stat. ch. 874.04, and sentencing appellant.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution charged appellant juvenile with attempted aggravated battery to cause great bodily harm and misdemeanor battery. The prosecution moved under the Criminal Street Gang Prevention Act of 1996, Fla. Stat. ch. 874.04, to treat appellant as a gang member for sentence enhancement. Appellant alleged that ch. 874.04 was unconstitutional and moved to dismiss the enhancement motion, which the trial court denied. At the close of evidence, the trial court denied appellant's motion for acquittal upon the attempted aggravated battery charge. The court convicted appellant, found that appellant was a gang member, and enhanced the sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction as supported by the evidence but reversed the denial of appellant's motion to dismiss the enhancement request. The court held that ch. 874.04 was unconstitutional as no nexus was required between the criminal act and membership in a gang; chapter 874.04 thus improperly used non-criminal acts to enhance criminal sentencing. The court remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing; the law providing for sentence enhancement upon a finding that a defendant was a gang member was unconstitutional because the prosecution was not obliged to show any connection between membership and the charged crime.

 

606 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Young v. State


CASE NO. 97-4503


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


719 So. 2d 1010; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13884; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2457



November 4, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 20, 1998. Petition for Review Denied February 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 181.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Howard C. Berman, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-6618 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), sentencing him to 15 years in prison for robbery pursuant to the sentencing enhancements allowed by the Prison Releasee Reoffender Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082 (1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant committed a robbery less than one year after he was released from prison. The state sought an enhanced penalty for the robbery charge pursuant to the Prison Releasee Reoffender Act (Act), Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082 (1997), which provided enhanced penalties for certain offenses committed within three years of release from a state correctional facility. Appellant pleaded no contest and was sentenced to 15 years in prison, pursuant to enhancements under the Act. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the Act, claiming it was ambiguous because it did not specifically include prisoners released prior to its effective date, and that it violated the single subject requirement of Fla. Const. Art. III, § 6. On appeal, the court affirmed. The appellate court found that the all-inclusive language of the Act required no statutory interpretation and included appellant. Further, the statute did not violate the single subject requirement of the Florida Constitution. The court found no duplicity of subject matter because the preamble to the Act stated that its purpose was to impose stricter punishment on reoffenders, and each amended section of the statute dealt with reoffenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court sentencing appellant to 15 years' imprisonment for robbery pursuant to the sentencing enhancements allowed by Florida's Prison Releasee Reoffender Act where appellant committed robbery within three years of his release from incarceration for a prior crime and subsequently pled guilty to the robbery.

 

607 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Florida Rock Indus. v. Alachua County


CASE NO. 98-3104


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


721 So. 2d 741; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13809; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2437



October 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 5, 1998. Rehearing Denied December 11, 1998. Released for Publication December 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Alachua County. Frederick D. Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed an appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida), which, in an environmental action, entered judgment for the defendants.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The clean air ordinance committee of the county obtained a sufficient number of signatures from registered voters to submit a proposed ordinance to the county commission. The commission refused to adopt the ordinance and, in accordance with the county's charter, it was therefore ordered to be placed on the ballot at the next general election. The plaintiff brought an action which challenged the proposed ordinance, asserting standing on the basis of its construction of a facility in the county which would be impacted by the ordinance. The lower court entered judgment for the defendants. The court held that since it was possible that the ordinance could become an element of a pollution control program administered by the county and approved by the department of environmental protection, the plaintiff failed to establish that the ordinance was unconstitutional on its face and in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which entered judgment for the defendants, because the court found no error in the trial court's conclusion that the proposed ordinance was not a land development regulation.

 

608 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Gibson v. State


Case No. 97-03477


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


721 So. 2d 363; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13673; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2422



October 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Diana M. Allen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) for capital sexual battery and lewd and lascivious acts upon an 8-year-old victim, claiming his sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole was cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital battery and lewd and lascivious acts. His victim was 8 years old. First, a motion to suppress a statement was not preserved for appeal. Next, the court held there was no reversible error in the trial court's refusal to grant a motion for continuance based on an amendment to the information and on a last-minute change by the public defender's office in his legal representation. Last, defendant raised the issue, under Fla. Const. art. I, § 17 or U.S. Const. art. VIII or Art. XIV, of whether the legislature had the power to impose a mandatory sentence of life without possibility of parole for the crime of penile union with the vagina of a girl less than 12 years of age when a defendant had no prior criminal record. The court based its decision upon a proportionality analysis guided by objective criteria, including: the gravity of the offense and the harshness of the penalty, the sentences imposed on other criminals in the same jurisdiction, and the sentences imposed for commission of the same crime in other jurisdictions. The court held the punishment was neither unusual nor cruel and affirmed the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions of capital sexual battery and lewd and lascivious acts. Neither the conduct of law enforcement during pretrial interviews nor the events immediately preceding this trial resulted in preserved, reversible error. Moreover, a sentence of life with no possibility of parole was neither cruel nor unusual.

Henderson v. State


CASE NO. 97-2899


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 1121; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13677; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2414



October 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Okeechobee County; Dwight L. Geiger, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 93-333CFA and 93-334CFA.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for resentencing on the October 31, 1996 affidavit of violation of community control.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed judgment from Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Okeechobee County (Florida), which imposed 18 months of community control when defendant admitted possession of marijuana following five-year prison sentence, claiming that combined sentences violated maximum upon conviction for battery, escape from juvenile detention center, and grand theft.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of battery, escape from a juvenile detention center, and grand theft. After the trial court imposed 18 months of community control when defendant admitted possession of marijuana following a five-year prison sentence, defendant appealed, claiming that community control combined with the prison sentence to violated a five-year maximum. On appeal, the court stated that sentences which exceeded the maximum were considered void to the extent that they exceeded the statutory maximum. The court reversed sentence and remanded for resentencing because the court agreed with defendant that his sentence exceeded the maximum period for the felonies he committed, and that constituted an illegal sentence. While testing positive for marijuana may qualify as a substantive violation, it was not clear whether the trial court in this case would have imposed the sentences it did based solely upon the allegations in an affidavit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed sentence and remanded for resentencing because the court agreed with defendant that his sentence exceeded the maximum period for the felonies he committed. His sentence was, therefore, an illegal sentence.

611 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Beers v. Beers


CASE NO. 97-1059


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


724 So. 2d 109; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13553; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2370



October 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1999. Released for Publication February 11, 1999. Petition for Review Denied June 23, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 1211.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Seymour Benson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband and appellee former wife both challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida), which entered a judgment of dissolution. After appellant filed for dissolution, appellee filed a third-party amended counterpetition for dissolution, which joined appellant's adulterous lover as a party-defendant. Appellee received damages for that claim in a separate proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former husband filed a petition for dissolution of marriage. Appellee former wife filed a counterpetition, alleging that during the marriage appellant had depleted marital assets in furtherance of an adulterous relationship. Appellee later filed a third amended counterpetition for dissolution, joining appellant's lover as a party defendant. The trial court entered judgment against the lover and awarded damages to appellee in a separate proceeding. The court later entered a judgment of dissolution and divided the marital property. Both appellant and appellee challenged. The court found that the trial court was wrong when it construed Fla. Stat. ch. 61.075(1)(i) as a statute of limitation and thus declined to consider appellant's intentional dissipation of marital assets more than two years before his filing for dissolution, when it made its equitable distribution order. The court also found that because the judgment against the lover was appellee's separate property, it should not have been treated by the trial court as a marital asset. Among other findings, the order was thus reversed in part and remanded for a recalculation of the equitable distribution award.


OUTCOME: The judgment of dissolution and award of equitable distribution were affirmed and reversed in part. The court found that the trial court was wrong to have not considered appellant's intentional dissipation of marital assets more than two years before the dissolution filing. Also, a judgment that appellee received should not have been considered a marital asset. The case was remanded for recalculation of the equitable distribution award.

 

612 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


FCCI Fund (FEISCO) v. Cayce's Excavation, Inc.


CASE NO. 97-3315


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


726 So. 2d 778; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12911; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2337



October 15, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order entered by Judge of Compensation Claims Judith S. Nelson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance fund requested review of an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims (Florida) that awarded workers' compensation benefits to appellee claimant, who was working on a barge afloat on navigable waters when he was injured. The judge concluded that Florida had jurisdiction to enter the order.


OVERVIEW: Appellee claimant was injured in an accident on appellee employer's barge and filed for workers' compensation insurance from appellant insurance fund. The court awarded workers' compensation benefits to appellee claimant. On review, the appellate court reversed because it held that the judge of compensation claims did not have jurisdiction to enter an order awarding benefits. The court held that appellee claimant was covered by the Longshoremen's and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. §§ 901 et seq., because he was injured while engaged in maritime employment upon actual navigable waters. The court said that where LHWCA applied, Florida workers' compensation benefits were expressly precluded under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.09(2). The court noted that state workers' compensation laws typically did not extend beyond the water's edge. Although the boundaries of the "federal zone" were imprecise, the court found that appellee claimant was clearly injured while working on navigable waters and was within the LHWCA coverage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order entered by the judge because the deputy did not have jurisdiction to award workers' compensation benefits to appellee claimant, who was working on a barge afloat on navigable waters when he was injured. Appellee claimant was covered by the Longshoremen's and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act, which precluded coverage under Florida workers' compensation statutes.

 

613 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Department of Revenue v. Seminole Tribe


CASE NO. 98-1775


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 270; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12905; 23 Fla. L. Weekly 2318; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2318



October 14, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 2, 1998. Released for Publication December 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; John A. Miller, Judge; L.T. Case No. 98-2582 (12).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of revenue sought review of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which denied appellant's motion to transfer of venue in accordance with the home venue privilege in appellee Indian tribe's action for declaratory and injunctive relief following the loss of its certificate of exemption from state sales and use taxation on off-reservation purchases.


OVERVIEW: After losing its certificate of exemption from state sales and use taxation on off-reservation purchases, appellee Indian tribe sued appellant department of revenue for declaratory and injunctive relief. Appellant filed a motion to transfer venue in accordance with the home venue privilege. The circuit court denied the motion finding that the privilege was waived because the suit was brought under section Fla. Stat. ch. 72.011 which provides for circuit court jurisdiction over actions in which taxpayers contest either the assessment of certain specified taxes or the denial of a refund of those taxes and specifically permits venue in such actions to be in the county where the taxpayer resides or maintains its principal commercial domicile. Appellant sought review and the court reversed after explaining that the fact that appellee had to pay sales tax could not be construed as an assessment within the meaning of ch. 72.011 because there had been no assessment against appellee nor had appellee been denied a refund. Because the action did not fall within a statute waiving appellant's home venue privilege, appellant was entitled to have the case transferred as requested.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order denying appellant department of revenue's motion for transfer of venue. The fact that appellant had to pay sales tax was not an assessment for purposes of the statute by which appellant would have waived home venue privilege. Because the action did not fall within a statute waiving appellant's home venue privilege, appellant was entitled to have the case transferred as requested.

 

614 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Plain v. State


CASE NO. 98-0943


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 585; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12858; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2309



October 14, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1998. Petition for Review Denied February 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 174.
Review denied by Plain v. State, 727 So. 2d 909, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 174 (Fla., 1999)
Decision reached on appeal by Plain v. State, 761 So. 2d 1124, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 6028 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Plain v. State, 907 So. 2d 1177, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11733 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Plain v. State, 88 So. 3d 956, 2011 Fla. App. LEXIS 19473 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Plain v. State, 2014 Fla. App. LEXIS 9561 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 25, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; Marc A. Cianca, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-2302-CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida), which convicted appellant of burglary of a dwelling with a battery and aggravated battery, and sentenced appellant under the Prison Release Re-offender Act, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 775.082(8)(a) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's convictions of burglary of a dwelling with a battery and aggravated battery, appellant sought the court's review asserting, among other things, that the Prison Release Re-offender Act, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 775.082(8)(a) (1997) (the Act), was an ex post facto violation as applied to him. The court held that the Act provided for greater penalties for offenses committed within three years of release from a state correctional facility. Here, the Act increased the penalty for a crime committed by appellant after the Act, based on appellant's release from prison resulting from a conviction which occurred prior to the Act. As such, the situation was no different than a defendant receiving a stiffer sentence under a habitual offender law for a crime committed after the passage of the law, where the underlying convictions which gave the defendant habitual offender status occurred before the law was passed. In such circumstances, habitual offender laws did not constitute ex post facto law violations, and as a result, appellant's assertion was without merit. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's sentence was affirmed because the act under which he was sentenced, the Prison Release Re-offender Act (Act), did not constitute an ex post facto law violation as applied to him.

Williams v. Spears


CASE NO. 98-926


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


719 So. 2d 1236; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12461; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2276



October 7, 1998, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners asked the court to exercise its common law certiorari jurisdiction to declare Fla. Stat. § 752.01(1)(1) unconstitutional, after respondent filed a petition seeking grandparent visitation pursuant to the statute.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were the divorced natural parents of a child. Respondent was the child's grandmother. Respondent filed a petition seeking court-ordered grandparent visitation, pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 752.01(1)(b). The parents answered that they had a fundamental right to privacy and self determination, pursuant to the Florida Constitution. The parents brought a motion for summary judgment, which was denied. They then brought a motion to dismiss, which was denied. Petitioners asked the court to exercise its common law certiorari jurisdiction and declare that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to them. The court granted the writ, finding that the statute in dispute was unconstitutional as applied, and would likewise be unconstitutional in any application to divorced parents who are in agreement that a court should not order grandparent visitation.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' request a writ for common law certiorari, finding that the statute in dispute was unconstitutional as applied to respondent's request for grandparent visitation.

 

617 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. Clark Sand Co.


CASE NO. 97-3331


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


721 So. 2d 329; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12730; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,379; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2270



October 5, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1998. Released for Publication December 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Nancy Gilliam, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida), which granted summary judgment to appellee manufacturers in a product liability negligence action based on appellant's alleged workplace exposure to a disease-causing substance. A repealed statute of repose had barred appellant's claim.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the lower court's grant of summary judgment to appellees, manufacturers of sandblasting equipment, in appellant's products liability action. Appellant claimed to have contracted silicosis from exposure to silica dust while he was employed as a sandblaster. The lower court had found that appellant's action was barred by a repealed products liability statute of repose, which eliminated any cause of action based on fraud or products liability filed more than 12 years after the fraud was committed or after the product was sold to its original purchaser. The appellate court determined that at the time appellant had surgery to remove a lung, he did not know that his illness was caused by his exposure and was told otherwise by his doctors. The appellate court determined that manifestation of the injury occurred when appellant was on notice of the causal connection between his exposure and his injury and that the question of when he should reasonably have been on notice of the connection was one for the jury. The appellate court concluded that the issue was an issue of fact and that, therefore, the trial court's grant of summary judgment was improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee manufacturers in appellant's products liability action. The appellate court held that the issue of when appellant's illness manifested itself was an issue of fact and that a grant of summary judgment was, therefore, improper.

 

618 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Delta Cas. Co. v. Pinnacle Med., Inc.


CASE NOS. 97-1429, 97-1588 & 97-3093


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


721 So. 2d 321; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12425; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2233



October 2, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1998. Released for Publication December 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Non-Final Appeal from the County Court for Orange County, Stephan W. Carter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers in a consolidated appeal challenged the orders of the County Court for Orange County (Florida), which denied their motions to dismiss and compel arbitration and that declared a portion of Fla. Stat. ch. 627.736(5) (1995) to be unconstitutional as violative of Fla. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of appellant insurers' motions and held that the compelled arbitration clause in Fla. Stat. ch. 627.736(5) (1995) violated the state constitution. The statute compelled arbitration of disputes between medical providers and insureds concerning the medical benefits available under personal injury protection insurance. Appellee medical care providers had been assigned the policy rights of persons injured in car accidents, and appellants had denied their claims. The court found that the statute violated substantive due process rights under Fla. Const. art. I, § 9 because it denied appellees their Fla. Const. art. I § 21 right to redress wrongs in court based on who owned the claim. Appellants were not required to submit to arbitration of their claims against insureds, but insureds were required to do so. Therefore, the statute was discriminatory. Moreover, the statute penalized medical providers compelled to arbitration because it substituted the prevailing party standard for obtaining attorney's fees in place of Fla. Stat. ch. 627.428(1) (1995), which controlled fee awards in litigation between insurers and their insureds in court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the lower court's finding that a law requiring appellee medical providers to submit to arbitration violated their due process rights under the state constitution because their access to the courts was limited by who they were, not the type of claim that they had. The appellate court concluded that the attorney fee provision was similarly unconstitutional.

Nelson v. State


CASE NO. 97-3435


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


719 So. 2d 1230; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12422; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2241



October 1, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Kim Skievaski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appellant's habitual felony offender sentence vacated, and this case remanded for the appellant to be resentenced.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a habitual felony offender sentence imposed by the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida), after she was convicted of felony petit theft.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review, in a direct criminal appeal, challenging a habitual felony offender sentence for felony petit theft. The court found that the trial court erred in imposing a habitual felony offender sentence for appellant's theft because Fla. Stat. ch. 812.014 indicated that habitual felony offender sentence for felony petit theft was precluded. Because the sentence clearly failed to comport with the statutory limitation of ch. 812.014, the sentence was illegal and was remediable as fundamental error. Accordingly, the court vacated the habitual felony offender sentence and remanded the case for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Appellant's habitual felony offender sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing because the sentence failed to comport with statutory limitations and was, therefore, illegal.

 

620 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Ritchie v. State


CASE NO. 97-967


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 261; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12305; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2253



September 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 13, 1998. Released for Publication December 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Jack M. Schemer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction for the capital sexual battery of one of her sons in the Circuit Court, Duval County (Florida). Appellant contended the trial court erred by failing to make a statutorily sufficient, individualized determination of necessity that the child victim's testimony be presented at trial by means of his videotaped deposition, as opposed to his live, in-court testimony in the presence of appellant.


OVERVIEW: The jury found appellant guilty of capital sexual battery on the basis of videotaped testimony by her son. Fla. Stat. Ann. § 92.53(1) allowed the use of videotaped testimony where the court found that the child would suffer at least moderate emotional or mental harm due to the presence of defendant if required to testify in open court. However, the mere recitation that the child would suffer such harm was not sufficient in determining whether to allow such testimony and the lower court failed to state its findings as to pertinent facts in allowing the testimony. The error was not harmless because appellant's right of confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI had been violated and the case was remanded for the required determination. Appellant's assertion that evidence of similar sexual abuse by a sibling should not have been allowed was rejected because there was a relaxed standard of admissibility in the familial context for similar corroborating fact evidence where the charged and collateral offenses shared a unique combination of characteristics. However, on retrial the admissibility of such evidence was to be independently determined by the trial court.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for capital sexual battery was reversed and remanded because the trial court's failure to state its findings as to pertinent facts in allowing appellant's son's videotaped testimony was a violation of appellant's constitutional right of confrontation. On remand, the trial court was to independently redetermine whether appellant's other son's similar corroborating fact evidence should be admitted.

Chrysler Corp. v. Florida Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles


CASE NO. 97-3421


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 563; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 12294; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2249



September 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1998. Released for Publication December 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Charles D. McClure, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automobile manufacturer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) that granted a motion by appellee state department of highway safety to dismiss appellant's complaint for injunctive and declaratory relief in a challenge to the facial constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 320.641(3) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellant automobile manufacturer sought to amend its franchise agreement with dealers in Florida. A group of dealers opposed to the proposed amendment filed a complaint with appellee state department of highway safety. Appellee initiated administrative proceedings and, thereafter, appellant brought an action challenging the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 320.641(3) (1995). A motion by appellee to dismiss appellant's action was granted because of the pending administrative proceedings. Appellant contended that the trial court violated its due process rights by ruling on a constitutional claim without affording adequate notice and opportunity to be heard. The appellate court reversed part of the judgment and remanded the case, finding that the administrative action could have no effect on the constitutional issue and, thus, it was pointless to require the time and expense of full administrative proceedings. The appellate court also held that the facial constitutionality of a statute could not be decided in an administrative hearing. Dismissal of the as-applied challenge was affirmed, however, where appellant was required to exhaust its administrative remedies on the claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed part of a judgment that granted appellee state department of highway safety's motion to dismiss appellant automobile manufacturer's complaint for injunctive and declaratory relief in a challenge to a statute's facial constitutionality where further administrative proceedings could have no effect on the constitutional issue. The case was remanded. The dismissal of appellant's as-applied constitutional challenge was affirmed.

Wood v. State


CASE NO. 97-4900


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


717 So. 2d 617; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11949; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2200



September 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the County Court for Okaloosa County. William Frye, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the County Court for Okaloosa County (Florida) for driving a motor vehicle while his license was revoked, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(2)(a) (1995).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving a motor vehicle while his license was revoked, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(2)(a). A valid driver's license was required for the operation of a moped, which was what defendant was driving. The court's analysis of a recent decision supported the conclusion. Defendant waived his argument that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to the operation of mopeds because he raised the argument for the first time in his appellate reply brief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving a motor vehicle while license was revoked because a valid driver's license was required to operate a moped. Appellant's argument that the criminal statute was unconstitutional was not to be considered for the first time on appeal.

Koontz v. St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist.


CASE NO. 97-3285


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 560; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11843; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2157



September 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1998. Released for Publication December 7, 1998. Petition for Review Denied March 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 543.
Rehearing denied by, 11/19/1998
Review denied by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 729 So. 2d 394, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 543 (Fla., 1999)
Appeal dismissed by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 861 So. 2d 1267, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19248 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2003)
Dismissed by St. Johns River Water Mgmt. Dist. v. Koontz, 908 So. 2d 518, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9774 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Alice Blackwell White, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part and REMANDED for further action consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) upholding appellee's authority to designate a hydrological basin and determining that appellant's regulatory taking claim was not ripe.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned property zoned commercial in front and residential in the rear and subject to legislative land-use restrictions. The property was located on a tributary of a river in an area designated by appellee as part of a hydrologic basin. Appellant wanted to develop a portion of the property and sought a management and storage of surface waters permit from appellee. Appellee denied the request, and appellant sued, claiming that appellee had no legislative authority to create the basin because the legislation relied upon unconstitutionally delegated such authority and alternatively, he sued to establish a regulatory taking. The court agreed with the trial court that appellee had the authority to designate the hydrological basin under valid statutes. However, the court found that the trial court was incorrect in ruling that appellant's regulatory taking claim was not ripe. The court found that despite appellee's argument that there was a chance that a modified application might be approved, appellee had made a final decision on the only application before it, so there was final agency action, and the issue of whether there had been a taking was properly before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, holding that appellee had the authority to designate the hydrological basin under valid statutes, and reversed in part, holding that the issue of whether there had been a taking was properly before the trial court because there was final agency action in appellee's denial of appellant's application for a permit.

 

624 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirvin


CASE NO. 97-3266


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 893; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11770; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2173



September 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 5, 1998. Petition for Review Denied March 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 487.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the County Court of Franklin County. Van Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state of Florida, sought review of the judgment of the County Court of Franklin County (Florida), which found that appellees', fishermen who had been charged with violating Fla. Const. Art. X, § 16(b)(2), due process rights had been violated after it found Fla. Const. Art. X, §§ 16(b)(1), (b)(2), (c)(1), (c)(3), and (c)(5) to be unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellee fishermen were all individually charged with violating Fla. Const. Art. X, § 16(b)(2), for using nets in excess of 500 square feet in the nearshore and inshore waters of Florida. Appellees each subsequently filed virtually identical motions to dismiss, challenging the provision of Fla. Const. Art. X, §§ 16(b)(1), (b)(2), (c)(1), (c)(3), and (c)(5). After the cases were consolidated, the court below found the challenged provisions unconstitutionally vague in violation of appellee's rights to due process. The judgment of the court below was reversed on appeal because the court found that the language in the challenged constitutional provisions conveyed a sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct when measured by common understanding and practice. The court noted that on remand of the § 16(b)(1) charges, the state's evidence must include proof that the fishermen were using prohibited gill or entangling nets. For purposes of the § 16(b)(2) charges, the state had to include proof that the fishermen were using prohibited nets in waters three nautical miles seaward of the coastline or territorial sea base line in the Gulf of Mexico.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which found that certain statutory provisions in the Florida Constitution that placed limitations on marine net fishing were unconstitutionally vague, was reversed, and the action charging appellee fishermen with violations of the provisions was remanded, because the court found the language in the challenged provisions to have conveyed a sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct.

State v. Conner


CASE NO. 97-3283


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


717 So. 2d 179; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11771; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2172



September 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 5, 1998. Petition for Review Denied March 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Fla. LEXIS 486.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the County Court of Wakulla County. Jill Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the County Court of Wakulla County (Florida) granting appellee's motion to dismiss a charge against him for violation of Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 46-31.0035(2) which prohibited fishing in certain waters.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with violating Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 46-31.0035(2), which prohibited any person from operating or fishing in near shore and inshore Florida waters with a net or bag containing more than 500 square feet of mesh area. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss. The trial court later certified two questions. The court found that contrary to the trial court's determination and appellee's argument, Rule 46-31.0035(3)(b) did adequately apprise a person of the area in which fishing with a net containing more than 500 square feet of mesh area was prohibited. The court also found that contrary to the trial court's determination, the Marine Fisheries Commission did not exceed its rulemaking authority by using the term nautical mile instead of mile in Rule 46-31.0035 because common usage and understanding of the term mile, as used in the constitutional provision, was nautical mile.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment granting appellee's motion to dismiss the charge and held that the applicable rule adequately apprised a person of the area in which the act was prohibited and that the Marine Fisheries Commission did not exceed its rulemaking authority by using a certain term in the rule.

Golf Club v. City of Plantation


CASE NO. 97-0218


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


717 So. 2d 166; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11629; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2149



September 16, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 2, 1998.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Golf Club of Plantation, Inc. v. City of Plantation, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7066 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Arthur M. Birken, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-6095 (12).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which dismissed plaintiff's action against defendant city seeking damages based on a taking of property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose out of the city's refusal to allow a golf club to develop land. Citing zoning laws, the city denied the club's various requests to construct single-family dwellings on the property surrounding the golf course. The club, plaintiff, filed a complaint against the city seeking damages based on a taking without just compensation. The city brought a motion for summary judgment, and the court dismissed the action. Plaintiff appealed the dismissal of its takings claim based on the fifth amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, its due process takings claim, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and its claim for declaratory relief. The court found that the trial court erred in dismissing claims based on the fifth and 14th amendments, and reversed those claims, but affirmed the dismissal of the claim for declaratory relief finding plaintiff was foreclosed from seeking that remedy. The court found dismissal of the fifth amendment claim should have been without prejudice to allow plaintiff to amend its complaint to assert which particular application of the city's plan amounted to an as-applied taking of the property. As to the 14th amendment claim, there were factual determinations in dispute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the complaint based on U.S. Const. amend. V, and XIV, but affirmed the dismissal of the claim for declaratory relief, finding it was not an appropriate remedy.

Sebring Airport Auth. v. McIntyre


CASE NO. 97-02707


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 296; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11526; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2097



September 11, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Highlands County; J. Dale Durrance, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, airport authority, raceway, and State challenged the declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court for Highlands County (Florida), which granted summary judgment for appellees, property appraiser and tax authority, for properly denying a tax exemption under Fla. Stat. ch. 196.012(6), which was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raceway applied for an ad valorem tax exemption under Fla. Stat. ch. 196.199. When appellee property appraiser denied the exemption, appellants, airport authority, raceway, and State, sought a declaratory judgment. All parties filed for summary judgment, which the trial court granted for appellees, property appraiser and tax authority. On appeal, the court affirmed the determination that a 1994 amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 196.012(6) was unconstitutional. The disputed property was used as a for-profit racetrack. It fell within ch. 196.012(6), which was an impermissible attempt by the legislature to create additional tax exemptions not authorized by Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3. The classes of municipal property potentially exempt from ad valorem taxation included property used predominantly for educational, literary, scientific, religious or charitable purposes, economic development, renewable energy sources, and historic preservation. The constitution did not authorize the legislature, through enactment of general laws, to provide for municipal exemptions from ad valorem taxation for a sports facility operated on a for-profit basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory ruling and grant of summary judgment for appellees, property appraiser and tax authority. Appellants, airport authority, raceway, and State, were not entitled to an ad valorem tax exemption for a profit-based raceway, as the statute under which the exemption was sought was unconstitutional.

Romano v. State


CASE NO. 97-1940


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 283; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11503; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2094



September 9, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Virginia Gay Broome, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-4336 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a ruling from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted him of sexual battery and sentenced him to 13 years incarceration.


OVERVIEW: In April 1996, appellant committed the offense of sexual battery. Appellant was convicted of the crime and sentenced to 13 years incarceration. Appellant sought review. The court found that there was no improper substantive modification by the division of statutory revision in 1993 because in 1992 the legislature did not intend that sexual battery require any force or violence beyond the force or violence inherent in the accomplishment of penetration or union as those terms were defined in Fla. Stat. ch. 794.005. In addition, the court found that even if the division improperly modified the sexual battery statute in publishing session law chapter 93-156 in Fla. Stat. ch. 795.011(5), the error was cured in 1995 when the legislature adopted chapter 795.011(5) as the official law. The court declined to review appellant's alleged error regarding his sentence because he failed to preserve said error for review by not objecting to the scoresheet or moving to correct his sentence in the trial court pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b). The court found that appellant might be entitled to postconviction relief pursuant to rule 3.800(b) or to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence without prejudice to appellant filing a motion for postconviction relief in the trial court because appellant failed to preserve his alleged error regarding the sentence for review.

Heggs v. State


Case No. 96-05252


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 263; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 11265; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2053



September 4, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Oliver L. Green, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant filed an appeal from judgment of Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which sentenced him to prison under Florida's 1995 sentencing guidelines, contending such guidelines were unconstitutional because the enacting legislation, 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 184, violated single subject rule of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to prison for armed robbery under Florida's 1995 sentencing guidelines. He appealed contending that the 1995 sentencing guidelines were unconstitutional because the enacting legislation, 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 184, violated the single subject rule contained in Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The court concluded that the resolution of this issue would have a great effect on the proper administration of justice throughout the state and therefore, on its own motion, it certified that the issue required immediate resolution by the Florida Supreme Court under Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(5). Chapter 184 contained civil provisions addressing domestic violence injunctions as well as the challenged sentencing guidelines. These provisions were not logically connected and there was no legislative statement of intent to implement comprehensive legislation to solve a crisis. However, the court declined to declare that the 1995 sentencing guidelines were unconstitutional because such a decision would impact the sentences of a large number of defendants.


OUTCOME: The court certified the issue of guidelines' constitutionality to Florida Supreme Court. While the enacting legislation appeared to violate the single subject rule by combining civil and criminal provisions that were not logically connected, a declaration that the guidelines were unconstitutional would impact sentences of a large number of defendants.

State v. Coyle


CASE NO. 96-04073


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 218; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9685; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1820



July 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1998. Released for Publication October 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court for Hillsborough County; Gregory P. Holder, County Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed the order of the County Court for Hillsborough County, (Florida) dismissing charges against defendants for open and gross lewd and lascivious behavior in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 798.02.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were performing their own unique form of entertainment on the stage of a licensed adult club. Defendants were arrested by two undercover police officers. Defendants were charged with second-degree misdemeanors for open and gross lewd and lascivious behavior in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 798.02. Defendants moved to consolidate and to dismiss the charges, alleging that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss. Plaintiff state appealed. The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings, holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 798.02 was not unconstitutionally vague because, in light of the common understanding of the terms and the applicable case law discussing and defining them, the statute gave adequate notice of the conduct sought to be prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the charges against defendants for lewd and lascivious behavior and remanded for further proceedings, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because, in light of the common understanding of the terms and the applicable case law discussing and defining them, the statute gave adequate notice of the conduct sought to be prohibited.

 

635 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Keough v. State


CASE NO. 96-3347


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


714 So. 2d 666; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9706; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1809



July 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, Tonya Rainwater, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his Brevard County Circuit Court (Florida) conviction for aggravated fleeing and eluding in contravention of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction for aggravated fleeing and eluding in contravention of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2), arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because there was no definition of "high speed" and because "causes the law enforcement officer to engage" was not explained. Additionally, defendant argued that the statute denied him due process because it assigned criminal liability for actions of a law enforcement officer. The court of appeals affirmed defendant's conviction. The evidence showed that during an investigatory stop by deputies, defendant raced his car out of the open gate of an otherwise enclosed water treatment plant compound, and fishtailed his way past one of the deputies, who testified that he would have been hit if he had not moved out of the way of defendant's car. A chase ensued that involved speeds as high as 118 m.p.h., and which ended 40 miles later after "stop sticks" deflated defendant's tires, causing him to fail to negotiate a turn, hit a pole, and land in a river. Based on those facts, the court held that defendant failed to show that the statute was constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated fleeing and eluding was affirmed because, under the facts of the case, defendant failed to demonstrate that the statute prohibiting such conduct was unconstitutionally vague or denied him due process.

 

636 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Whalen v. Prosser


Case No. 97-03165


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


719 So. 2d 2; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9497; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1812



July 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 9, 1998. Released for Publication October 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; James R. Case, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, estate beneficiaries, challenged an order of the Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) which dismissed their complaint for intentional interference with an expectancy of inheritance against appellees, estate holder's relatives. Appellants argued the circuit court erred because appellees exercised undue influence by causing an incompetent estate holder to reverse the primary beneficiaries by revising the estate planning documents.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, estate beneficiaries, expected to be the estate holder's primary beneficiaries. Appellees, estate holder's relatives, then lacked the status of estate beneficiaries. Appellees caused the estate holder to relocate near them and induced her to execute new estate planning documents drafted by appellees' attorney. Appellants filed a complaint against appellees which alleged intentional interference with an expectancy of inheritance before the estate holder's decease. Appellees filed a motion to dismiss with prejudice which the circuit court granted. Appellants challenged that decision by arguing appellees exercised undue influence because they caused the estate holder to move near them and to execute new estate planning documents drafted by their attorney when estate holder was incompetent. The court noted that no evidence of the estate holder's incapacity existed, which indicated that no undue influence occurred in her change of estate planning documents. The court ruled that appellants' expectancy interest afforded no cause of action. The court refused to apply this tort theory because the estate holder remained alive. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court which dismissed the complaint for intentional interference with an expectancy of inheritance filed by appellants, estate beneficiaries, against appellees, estate holder's relatives. The court ruled that this tort did not apply while the estate holder was alive and when appellants had a mere expectancy interest and found no undue influence in her revision of the estate planning documents.

Ocasio v. McGlothin


CASE NO. 98-891


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


719 So. 2d 918; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9551; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1751



July 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Clarification Granted October 28, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 13694. Review Dismissed December 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2617.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Jennifer D. Bailey, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-21863.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the non-final order of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) that upheld the constitutionality of the grandparent visitation statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a), (d), and which awarded appellee grandmother visitation rights, in an action initiated by appellee to obtain visitation rights to the child of appellant, an unwed mother.


OVERVIEW: Appellee grandmother sought visitation rights with the child of the deceased father, her son. Appellant mother challenged the constitutionality of the grandparent visitation statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a), (d). The court affirmed the order allowing visitation and upholding the constitutionality under ch. 752.01(1)(a), which permitted appellee visitation as the mother of a deceased, unwed parent. The court was bound by stare decisis to adhere to its prior decision finding the provision constitutional, but certified the issue for appeal based upon a conflict with another district court of appeal. The court found ch. 752.01(1)(d) facially unconstitutional and reversed that portion of the order granting visitation. The court agreed with the dissent in the case providing stare decisis on ch. 752.01(1)(a) that the provision interfered with rights protected in Fla. Const. art. I, § 23 and the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court certified the issues surrounding ch. 752.01(1)(d) for it was an issue of great public importance.


OUTCOME: The portion of the order granting visitation because appellee was the grandparent related through a deceased parent was affirmed because the court was bound by stare decisis, but the remaining portion of the order permitting visitation was reversed because the court found that forcing visitation violated the appellant's rights. The court certified the issues for appeal to the supreme court.

Department of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation v. Calder Race Course, Inc.


CASE NO. 97-2704


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


724 So. 2d 100; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9584; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1795



July 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 15, 1998. Released for Publication February 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Division of Administrative Hearings. Administrative Law Judge Mary Clark.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, challenged an order of the Division of Administrative Hearings (Florida), in favor of appellees, pari-mutuel wagering entities. The order invalidated a rule as unauthorized by Fla. Stat. ch. 550.0251 and held its promulgation improperly exercised delegated legislative authority of the Administrative Procedures Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 120.52(8) (Supp. 1996), ch. 120.536(1) (Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, issued Fla. Admin. Code R. 61D-2.002. Appellees, pari-mutuel wagering entities, contested the rule before an administrative law judge of the Division of Administrative Hearings. Appellees argued that the rule was not authorized by Fla. Stat. 550.0251 and its promulgation by appellant was an invalid exercise of delegated legislative authority under the Administrative Procedures Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 120.52(8) (Supp. 1996) and ch. 120.536(1) (Supp. 1996). Appellees argued the rule's allowance of warrantless searches by appellant violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The judge issued an order invalidating the rule. Appellant challenged that determination by arguing the rule followed ch. 550.0251, was promulgated pursuant to ch. 120.52(8) and ch. 120.536(1), and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court disagreed with appellant and affirmed the judge because ch. 550.0251 did not authorize the rule, the promulgation of which was an invalid exercise of delegated legislative authority under ch. 120.52(8) and ch. 120.536(1) and which violated U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed for appellees, pari-mutuel wagering entities, the Division of Administrative Hearing judge's order invalidating the contested rule promulgated by appellants, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, because it was unauthorized by the department's enabling act, it was an improper exercise of delegated legislative authority under the Administrative Procedures Act, and violated the U.S. Constitution's Fourth Amendment.

 

640 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Laboo v. State


CASE NO. 97-2128


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


715 So. 2d 1034; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9479; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1784



July 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Jack Schemer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for workers' compensation fraud, grand theft, and perjury, from the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), contending that prosecutorial comments constituted fundamental error, conviction for both workers' compensation fraud under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.105 and grand theft under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.014 was a double jeopardy violation, and it was error not to allow the jury to decide the issue of materiality.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of workers' compensation fraud, grand theft, and perjury. On appeal, appellant complained of a number of improper prosecutorial comments made during closing argument in rebuttal to defense counsel's initial closing argument. He conceded that no objections to these comments were raised below, but he asserted that the comments constituted fundamental error. The court affirmed, holding that when viewed in the context of all the evidence presented and the initial arguments by defense counsel, any comments by the prosecutor which may not have been proper were not so egregious as to have impaired the ability of the jurors to decide the case based on the evidence. Appellant further contended that conviction for both workers' compensation fraud under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.105 and grand theft under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.014 was a double jeopardy violation. The court held that the plain reading of Fla. Stat. ch. 440.105(5) evidenced the legislature's intent to allow a conviction for workers' compensation fraud and any other applicable crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for workers' compensation fraud, grand theft, and perjury because the three issues he raised were not preserved for appeal and did not constitute fundamental error.

 

641 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Rice


Case No. 97-702


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


716 So. 2d 807; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9420; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1739



July 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 28, 1998. Review Denied December 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2607.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, J. Preston Silvernail, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condominium unit owner sought review from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) summary judgment for appellees husband and wife, arguing that the lower court erroneously concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 718.107 (1993) prevented the previous owner of appellees' unit from conveying use of the attached garage to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Upon purchasing a condominium unit with an assigned garage and finding that appellant condominium unit owner was using the garage in question based on the purported conveyance of the garage from the previous owner of their unit, appellees husband and wife sought arbitration to enforce their claim on the garage. After an arbitration decision in appellees' favor, appellant filed suit, and the lower court entered summary judgment for appellees based on Fla. Stat. ch. 718.107 (1993). Appellant sought review. The court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 718.107(2) (1993) restrained the conveyance of all common elements appurtenant to a living unit, such that the garage in question could not have been conveyed to appellant. Further, the court held that even under appellant's own theory that the conveyance merely granted a license to appellant to use the garage, such a license was automatically extinguished upon sale or conveyance of the property in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that the statutory scheme made explicit the prohibition of conveyances of common elements such as the garage in question except insofar as they were conveyed with the sale of their attached unit to the new unit owner.

State v. A.C.


CASE NOS. 98-1038, 98-1039, 98-1123 & 98-1128


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


714 So. 2d 617; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9082; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1700



July 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 14, 1998. Petition for Review Denied November 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2353.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated petitions for writs of certiorari to the Circuit Court of the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Karen L. Martin & Hubert R. Lindsey, Judges; L.T. Case Nos. CJ 96-3928 JL, CJ 94-2191JL, CJ 96-6087JL, CJ 97-4422JL CJ 94-537JM, CJ 94-4452JM, CJ 94-7242JM, CJ 95-6944JM, CJ 96-8502JM, CJ 97-4605JM, CJ 92-6617JM, CJ 92-7191JM, CJ 93-3906JM, CJ 93-4970JM, CJ 94-6866JM & CJ 95-7418JM.



DISPOSITION: Petitions for writ of certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the state sought review of several decisions from the Palm Beach County Circuit Court (Florida) that denied motions to transfer respondent juveniles to adult court.


OVERVIEW: The court consolidated four petitions with identical issues for writ of certiorari. In each, the state had sought review of trial court decisions which denied motions to transfer respondent juveniles to adult court and found that Fla. Stat. ch. 985.227(3) violated the constitutional provisions prohibiting ex post facto laws. The state contended that the statute did not violate the ex post facto prohibition. The court quashed the trial court's denials of the motions to transfer and found that Fla. Stat. ch. 985.227(3) was constitutional because the prohibition against ex post facto laws did not apply to procedural matters. Furthermore, the court's jurisdiction was not implicated, and transfers from juvenile court to adult court did not affect a substantial substantive right of the accused.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the denials of the motions to transfer respondent juveniles to adult court and found that the transfer statute did not violate constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws.
