Goosen v. Walker


CASE NO. 97-4459


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


714 So. 2d 1149; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 9084; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1712



July 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; Burton C. Conner, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-425 DV 20.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbor challenged a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida), which enjoined him from photographing or videotaping appellee neighbors, or from pretending to engage in such conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant neighbor, who did not get along with appellee neighbors, was enjoined from photographing or videotaping appellees or pretending to do so. He argued that the injunction was unconstitutional because it violated U.S. Const. amend. I. On review, the appellate court noted that the testimony showed that appellant had videotaped appellees on two to four occasions during the preceding four months when appellees were in their own yard or an adjoining area. Thus, the appellate court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support the finding implicit in the injunction that appellant's conduct constituted stalking pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 784.048(2). In regard to appellant's arguments that his conduct was constitutionally protected, the appellate court cited a precedent case standing for the proposition that conduct which amounted to stalking was not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. Thus, based on the foregoing precedent, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's injunction prohibiting appellant's photographing or videotaping of appellees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's injunction prohibiting appellant neighbor from photographing, videotaping, or pretending to photograph or videotape appellee neighbors. The appellate court held that precedent established that conduct which amounted to stalking was not constitutionally protected.

Ladd v. State

COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida), which convicted him of use of a child in a sexual performance, promoting a sexual performance by a child, and attempted possession of a videotape depicting a sexual performance by a child, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071 (1995).

Ortega v. State


CASE NO. 97-0494


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 833; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 8094; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1617



July 8, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Roger B. Colton, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-9336.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which declared appellant to be a sexual predator under the Florida Sexual Predator's Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21-23.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed the state's motion to have him declared a sexual predator was unconstitutional as an ex post facto violation. The registration requirement of the 1995 Florida Sexual Predator's Act (Act), Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21-23, which the stated contended was applicable to appellant, was contained in the statute as it existed at the time of appellant's crime. Requiring appellant to register was not an ex post facto violation because even though the 1993 Act was repealed the registration requirement remained when provisions of the statute were reenacted. Registration requirements of sexual predator acts were generally regarded as regulatory and not punishment, and thus not subject to the prohibition against ex post facto laws. The community modification provisions of the sexual predator statute were not applied to appellant and therefore the court did not reach the issue of whether those provisions were more than regulatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision to declare appellant a sexual predator, finding the requirement that appellant register as a sexual predator did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws because the registration requirement existed at the time of appellant's crime, despite the fact that the sexual predator statute had been repealed earlier.

Mizrahi v. N. Miami Med. Ctr.


CASE NO. 97-353


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 826; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 8137; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1624



July 8, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Jon I. Gordon, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-21486.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing and Grant of Clarification for Withdrawn Opinion of January 28, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 599.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment for the appellees affirmed. Rehearing denied; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surviving children moved for a rehearing and/or clarification on an earlier opinion of their appeal of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which granted summary judgment for appellee hospital and physicians based on Fla. Stat. ch. 768.21(1995) in appellants' wrongful death suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were the surviving adult children of decedent, who died, allegedly as a result of the medical malpractice of one or more of appellee medical center or appellee physicians. Appellants brought a wrongful death suit against appellees. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees based on Fla. Stat. ch. 768.21 (1995). On appeal, appellants contended that ch. 768.21(8) was unconstitutional, as violative of the equal protection clause of both the federal and Florida constitutions. The court found that because the right to wrongful death damages was not a fundamental right, and those in appellants' position were not a suspect class, ch. 768.21(8) would be unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection only if the challenged classification bore no rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. The court found that the statute's disparate treatment of medical malpractice wrongful deaths did bear a rational relationship to the legitimate state interest of ensuring the accessibility of medical care to state residents by curtailing the skyrocketing medical malpractice insurance premiums in the state. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant surviving children's motion for a rehearing was denied, however the court granted appellants' motion for clarification. The judgment, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital and physicians, was affirmed because the statutory provision cited by the trial court was constitutional.

State v. Cunningham


Case No. 97-03010


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 1221; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 7549; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1573



June 26, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 27, 1998. Petition for Review Denied November 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2340.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Anthony Rondolino, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which held Fla. Stat. ch. 794.05 (1996) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: State challenged the trial court's order holding Fla. Stat. ch. 794.05 (1996) unconstitutional on privacy grounds. The statute prohibited sexual activity between an adult 24 years of age or older and a 16 or 17 year old minor. The court reversed and remanded because the statute furthered a compelling state interest by protecting minors from harmful sexual conduct and possible sexual exploitation by adults. The court held that this state interest clearly outweighed any right a minor might have in consenting to this type of exploitation. Finally, the court held that the statute employed the least intrusive means in order to accomplish the state's goal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding of unconstitutionality because the statute furthered a compelling state interest by the least intrusive means in that it prohibited sexual activity between minor children and adults of an age likely to be more exploitative of such children.

Wilburn v. State


CASE NO. 97-1041


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


763 So. 2d 353; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 7500; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1544



June 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1998. Petition for Review Denied November 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2322.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Howard C. Berman, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-191 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nurse sought review of the orders of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), that entered judgment convicting appellant of attempted sexual battery of a mentally defective person and sentenced appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nurse worked in the Alzheimer's disease unit of a nursing facility. While on duty, appellant attempted to engage in oral sex with one of the patients under her care. The patient was diagnosed with organic brain syndrome. His memory and judgment centers were greatly damaged, and, as a result of his brain dysfunction, he demonstrated overtly sexual conduct. Appellant was charged with attempted sexual battery of a mentally defective person under Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(4)(e). At trial, appellant did not challenge the vagueness of ch. 794.011(4)(e). Instead, appellant contended that appellee prosecution failed to prove that the sexual activity was nonconsensual. After trial, appellant was convicted and sentenced. On review, appellant claimed ch. 794.011(4)(e) was unconstitutional because the term "mentally defective," as defined in ch. 794.011(1)(b), failed a vagueness challenge. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence because the evidence appellee presented at trial demonstrated appellant's conduct fell within the conduct that ch. 794.011(4)(e) proscribed, and appellant was provided with adequate notice that her conduct was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of conviction and sentencing because the evidence presented at trial clearly showed that appellant nurse's conduct fell squarely within the conduct which the statute proscribed, and appellant was provided with adequate notice that her conduct was illegal.

Tuttle's Design-Build v. Caple


CASE NO. 97-3068


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 1213; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 7521; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1526



June 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Alan Postman, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 97-14980.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which awarded plaintiff mortgagees' interest payments pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 702.10(2) during the pendency of plaintiffs' foreclosure proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the trial court's order awarding plaintiff mortgagees interest payments during the pendency of parties' foreclosure proceedings, defendant mortgagor argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 702.10(2), the statute pursuant to which the interest payments were ordered, was unconstitutional. Reviewing the state law at issue, the court noted that the law required defendant either show cause why payments on the mortgage should not be made during the pendency of foreclosure proceedings or vacate the property at issue. The court held that, as the statute deprived defendant of property, it was required to comply with due process provisions. However, the court held that the statute failed to provide for a creditor bond to protect defendant from mistaken repossession or payment. Thus, the court held the statute was unconstitutional. The court also held the statute's provisions requiring defendant post an excessive bond to stay the payments unconstitutionally regulated matters of practice and procedure and improperly conflicted with procedural rules regarding bonds established by the state's supreme court. Thus, the court reversed the judgment awarding interest payments and remanded.


OUTCOME: The award of interest payments in plaintiff mortgagees' foreclosure action against defendant mortgagor was reversed and the case was remanded, as the statute pursuant to which the award was made was unconstitutional.

 

653 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Bryant v. State


Case No. 97-00443


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 781; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 6646; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1429



June 12, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Robert B. Bennett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Arguing that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 893.13(1)(d)(1995) was unconstitutionally vague, that the trial court failed to inquire after his motion to discharge court-appointed attorney, and failed to determine whether he knew the consequences of habitualization before entering his pleas, appellant sought review from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida), which entered a final judgment after entering no contest pleas to the sale of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a final judgment after entering no contest pleas to the sale of cocaine and the sale of cocaine within 200 feet of a public park pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 893.13(1)(d)(1995). The court rejected his argument that § 893.13(1)(d) was unconstitutionally vague. The court applied the general rule of giving legislation its plain and ordinary meaning, and determined that the term "public park" was not impermissibly vague. However, the court reversed the judgment against him because it found that the record supported that the trial court failed to make a proper inquiry upon his motion to discharge his attorney and also failed to determine whether he was aware of the consequences of the habitualization. The court reasoned that appellant's plea was therefore involuntary, and remanded the case to give him the opportunity to withdraw his plea and to proceed to trial if he desired.


OUTCOME: Although the court disagreed with appellant's contention that the phrase "public park" was unconstitutionally vague, the court reversed the judgment because the record supported that the trial court failed to make a proper inquiry upon his motion to discharge his attorney and to determine whether he was aware of the consequences of the habitualization.

 

654 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Seminole County v. M. G. Invs.


CASE NO. 97-2385


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


714 So. 2d 1066; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 6655; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1450



June 12, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1998. Released for Publication August 13, 1998. Petition for Review Denied November 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2334.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Thomas G. Freeman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida), which awarded appellee property owner attorney fees following a condemnation proceeding pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 73.092(1)(a)(1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellant county argued that the trial court erred in construing Fla. Stat. § 73.092(1)(a)(1995), a provision awarding attorney fees in eminent domain proceedings on the basis of benefits received for the client when the "defendant" hires an attorney. Specifically, appellant contended, the trial court's designation of the mortgagee, the prior landowner and the recipient of judgment proceeds -- rather than appellee, the current owner -- as the statutory defendant was improper for purposes of calculating benefits acquired for the client and in awarding appellee attorney fees. Because there was no difference between the final judgment and appellant's first written offer to appellee, appellant asserted, the benefits were zero and no attorney fees were required. The court disagreed, ruling that a "reasonable attorney's fee for the defendant's attorney," in § 73.11, referred to compensation due appellee, the property owner. The mortgagee did not have an interest in the mortgaged property, the court ruled, but only a chose in action creating a lien. The court concluded that the fee award satisfied the constitutional provision that appellee owner receive full compensation for a taking.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed awarding appellee property owner attorney fees following a condemnation proceeding in which the mortgagee was the judgment recipient, because the statutory fee authorized for "defendant's attorney" was construed as compensation due appellee for a taking.

Linder v. State


CASE NO. 97-597


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


711 So. 2d 1340; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 6636; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1391



June 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Ronald Dresnick, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-39971.

Original Opinion of April 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 5475.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing denied. *

* Although appointed appellate counsel was previously allowed to withdraw pursuant to Anders v. California, 386 U.S. 738, 18 L. Ed. 2d 493, 87 S. Ct. 1396 (1967), we reappoint counsel for further proceedings on the certified conflict.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant moved for rehearing after the court rejected his appeal of the trial court's judgment convicting him of aggravated battery and sentencing him as a violent career criminal pursuant to 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 182.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated battery and was sentenced as a violent career criminal pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(4)(c) (1995). He appealed, but the court rejected his appeal on the identical single subject challenge to 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 182. When appellant moved for rehearing, the court denied his motion but certified its decision as being in direct conflict with the second district court of appeal. The second district court of appeal had held 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 182 to be unconstitutional for violation of the single subject requirement of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6, and had invalidated a violent career criminal sentence on that basis. The effect of the second district court of appeal's ruling was to rule out a violent career criminal disposition for crimes committed between October 1, 1995 and May 24, 1997. Appellant committed the crime on December 30, 1995, and thus he would have fallen into the class entitled to relief if this case had proceeded in the second district.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's motion for rehearing after it had denied his appeal because it found the single subject part of the violent career criminal statute did not render that statute unconstitutional. The court also recognized direct conflict with a decision from the second district court of appeal and certified the case on that basis.

Chiles v. State Emples. Attys. Guild


CASE NO. 97-2359


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


714 So. 2d 502; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 6140; 158 L.R.R.M. 2025; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1348



June 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied July 13, 1998. Released for Publication July 29, 1998. Second Correction October 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Nikki Ann Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governor challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which found that state employees who worked as attorneys had a fundamental right to collectively bargain that was unconstitutionally infringed upon by Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(3)(j) (1997). Appellee labor union brought a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee labor union sought declaratory relief against state officials for whom appellant governor was substituted. The trial court ruled that state employees who worked as attorneys had a fundamental right to collectively bargain which was unconstitutionally infringed by Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(3)(j) (1997). The trial court found that appellant had a compelling interest in the lawyer-client relationship between the state and the attorneys it employed but that a complete ban on collective bargaining by state-employed lawyers was not necessary to protect that interest. The court affirmed because Fla. Const. art. I, § 6 provided public employees with the right to bargain collectively, and that the right was fundamental. The court found that the state had presented no evidence to support its position that government employed attorneys would abandon their ethical obligations if permitted to join a union and that it did not prove that a blanket ban on collective bargaining by government attorneys was the least onerous means of protecting the attorney-client relationship between the lawyers and the public entities which employed them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the statutory limit on state-employed attorneys' collective bargaining rights was unconstitutional.

Powell v. City of Delray Beach


CASE NO. 97-3020


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


711 So. 2d 1307; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 8848; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1339



June 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] DECISION WITHOUT PUBLISHED OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 1, 1998. Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Frederick A. Hazouri, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 95-9396 AO.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit of Palm Beach County (Florida), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city and held that appellants had to pave an alley adjacent to their apartment building.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowners applied for a permit to build a duplex. Appellee city required that appellants pave the alleyway adjacent to their property in order to obtain the permit. Appellants brought an action contesting the paving requirement, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court reversed the trial court's order, holding that the paving requirement in Delray Beach, Fla., Land Development Reg. § 5.3.1(E)(2) did not apply to situations where homeowners were allowed to back directly into alleyways. The court found that the trial court had construed the statute to express intentions which did not appear. The court reasoned that the trial court attempted to use a definition of an alley to get around the "backing into alleyways" exception defined in Delray Beach, Fla., Land Development Reg. § 6.1.4(A)(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment to appellee city, holding that the trial court erred when it imposed a paving requirement on appellant homeowners, because the paving requirement did not apply to situations where homeowners were allowed to back directly into alleyways.

Plante v. Department of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation, Div. of Pari-Mutuel Wagering


CASE NO. 97-4480


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


716 So. 2d 790; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 8850; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1338



June 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: DECISION WITHOUT PUBLISHED OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearning Granted August 12, 1998. As Corrected August 13, 1998. Released for Publication August 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering; L.T. Case No. 93-70511.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant veterinarian sought review of a decision of appellee State of Florida, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering (division), which, on remand to impose a new penalty, sentenced the veterinarian to the same one-year suspension that had been imposed prior to the first appeal, but reduced the amount of the fine.


OVERVIEW: The division found that the veterinarian had violated a statute and a rule by drugging a racehorse in order to affect the race's outcome. On appeal, the court affirmed the violation of the statute, but reversed the violation of the rule, which was unconstitutional, and remanded for a new penalty. On remand, the division imposed the same one-year suspension, but reduced the amount of the fine. The veterinarian appealed, contending that the division erred in striking his memorandum and attachments citing the division's precedents reflecting that lighted penalties had been imposed in other horse drugging cases. In reversing and remanding, the court held that (1) the veterinarian was entitled to rely on precedents and it was error to strike that portion of the veterinarian's submission; (2) it was not error to strike the other information submitted by the veterinarian, which showed that after he was found in violation, the division had liberalized its policy on prosecuting the use of sodium bicarbonate on horses; and (3) the other information constituted new evidence and there was no authorization for an agency to reopen an administrative evidentiary hearing once it had been concluded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded solely for the division's consideration of the precedents submitted by the veterinarian and reconsideration of the penalty imposed for the veterinarian's violation of a statute by giving a racehorse medication or drugs in order to affect the outcome of a race.

DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus issued; writ of prohibition issued; conviction and sentence quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus and a writ of prohibition, and appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which convicted him of indirect criminal contempt under the Marchman Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 397.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the writ of habeas corpus and quashed defendant's conviction and sentence because his conviction was void. The court held that the order to show cause failed to specify the acts defendant allegedly committed in violating the order directing him to complete a substance abuse program. The court also granted the writ of prohibition to prohibit the lower court from enforcing or otherwise attempting to exercise jurisdiction pursuant to its order committing defendant for involuntary substance abuse treatment.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of habeas corpus and quashed defendant's conviction because the lower court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to order defendant to a substance abuse program. The court issued a writ of prohibition to prevent the lower court from further exercising jurisdiction.

McCann v. State


CASE NO. 96-3596


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


711 So. 2d 1290; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 5944; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1293



May 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 6, 1998. Released for Publication July 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Howard M. Zeidwig, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-3321 CF10A.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR CORRECTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which convicted appellant of attempting to procure a person under the age of 18 for prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempting to procure a person under the age of 18 for prostitution. On appeal, the instant court stated that the test for sufficiency of the evidence was whether a rational trier of fact could have found proof of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the evidence met the test. Further, contrary to appellant's contention, the court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 796.03 (1993) was not unconstitutionally vague. While it was true that the term "procure" may mean to act as a "pimp" and not necessarily procure the person for oneself, it was also clear that "procure" may mean persuading, inducing, or prevailing upon the person to do something sexual for oneself. A reading of the statute reflected both definitions as being criminal conduct. This was especially true in light of the fact that the intent behind the statute was the state's compelling interest in protecting underage people from being sexually abused or exploited. The court held that the judgment should be affirmed, but the court remanded the case for correction because the charge against appellant was a third-degree felony and not a second-degree felony.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted appellant of attempting to procure a person under the age of 18 for prostitution, but the court remanded the judgment for correction. The evidence met the test of sufficiency and the statute under which appellant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague. However, the charge against appellant was a third degree felony and not a second degree felony.

State v. Keirn


CASE NO. 96-4001


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


720 So. 2d 1085; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 5044; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1144



May 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert Carney, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-8218 CF.



DISPOSITION: Section 322.34(1)(c) constitutional, trial court's order of dismissal reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecution challenged an order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) that granted appellee's motion to dismiss charges of driving while his license was suspended in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c), arguing that the circuit court erred in concluding that that statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power in violation of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with felony driving under a suspended license in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c) (1995), which declared a first or second conviction of driving with a suspended license to be a misdemeanor and a third conviction to be a felony. He moved to dismiss, and the circuit court granted the motion after concluding that the statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to the judiciary because Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c) required an adjudication of guilt for the conduct to be punishable as a felony and because Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01 allowed it to withhold an adjudication of guilt; as such, the circuit court reasoned that it had the unbridled discretion to make appellee's conduct a felony or a misdemeanor by simply exercising its discretion regarding the adjudication of guilt. Appellant prosecution sought review. In reversing, the appellate court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c), was not unconstitutional. A conviction under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34 occurred after a final disposition of a case as a result of a trial or plea without regard to the court's decision on adjudication of defendant.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order of dismissal was reversed, as state statute was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to the judiciary. A conviction occurred after a final disposition of a case as a result of a trial or plea without regard to the circuit court's decision on adjudication of defendant.

 

663 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp. v. Ballard


CASE NOS. 97-1514 and 97-1684


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


739 So. 2d 603; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 4725; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,236; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1077



April 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Moses Baker, Jr., Judge; L.T. Case No. 93-10817 AD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a manufacturer of an asbestos product, sought review of the judgment from the 15th Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida) upon a jury verdict for appellee, a non-Florida resident who was injured by the product in states other than Florida. Appellant claimed that Florida was forum non conveniens under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.061(a) (1997), and that the punitive damages were excessive under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.73(1) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a non-Florida resident, was injured by exposure to an asbestos-containing product on job sites in states other than Florida, but sued appellant, the manufacturer of that product, in Florida. Appellant's motion to dismiss the case based on forum non conveniens was dismissed by the trial court. A jury awarded appellee compensatory and punitive damages. On appeal, the court held that under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.061(a) (1997), the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's forum non conveniens motion, because appellant waited three years after the complaint was filed before filing its motion, and the case was ready for trial. Because appellant agreed to have the jury decide the issue of punitive damages, and because the facts rebutted the presumption of Fla. Stat. ch. 768.73(1) (1993) that a punitive damage award over three times the amount of compensatory damages was excessive, the court found that the amount was proper. However, because the punitive damage award was greater than similar awards, the court affirmed the judgment, but certified the question of whether the amount of the punitive damages was excessive to the state supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee, a non-resident injured in other states by an asbestos product manufactured by appellant, but certified the question of whether the amount of punitive damages was excessive, because appellant's three-year delay in seeking to dismiss the complaint based on forum non conveniens made the denial of its motion proper, and the facts made the amount of the damages, although unusually high, proper.

Arias v. Department of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation, Div. of Real Estate


CASE NO. 97-576


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 655; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 4333; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1026



April 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1998. Released for Publication June 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the State of Florida, Department of Business and Professional Regulation, Florida Real Estate Commission. LOWER TRIBUNAL. NO. 96-81648.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate agent sought review of a final order, by appellee Department of Business and Professional Regulation, Division of Real Estate (Florida), finding appellant had violated Fla. Stat. ch. 475.25(1)(b) (1995), suspending appellant's real estate license for two years, sentencing appellant to one year of probation, and fining her $ 1,000. Appellant argued that appellee Department did not have penalty guidelines in place.


OVERVIEW: After appellee Department of Business and Professional Regulation found that appellant real estate agent had violated Fla. Stat. ch. 475.25(1)(b) (1995) for allegedly facilitating racial discrimination, appellee suspended appellant's real estate license. Appellant sought review. The court held that appellee failed to comply with Fla. Stat. ch. 455.2273 (1997), requiring appellee to have in place guidelines for disciplinary actions and the imposition of related penalties. Therefore, the total lack of enforcement guidelines left appellant in a predicament ripe for arbitrary and erratic enforcement and provided no standards governed by the legislature as to constitute a judicially reviewable discretion. The court held that, absent the requisite guidelines, the appellee's order must be reversed. Appellant was entitled to notice of all matters that appellee would consider including the likely range of the penalty to be imposed against her. Further, any future action to create and apply penalty guidelines would constitute an improper ex post factor application of the law against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court held that appellee Department of Business and Professional Regulation's order should be reversed. The court held that appellant real estate agent, subject to disciplinary hearing, was entitled to notice of all the matters that appellee would consider against her, including the likely range of the penalty to be imposed.

COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Okaloosa County (Florida) holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.155(8)(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.155(8)(a) was unconstitutional as contrary to Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4(c). Appellant argued that holding the statute at issue unconstitutional would result in inequitable taxation. The court disagreed and reasoned that other types of non-homestead residential and commercial property were excluded from the homestead assessment tax cap.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court finding the statute at issue unconstitutional because the statute included provisions that expressly altered the state's constitution regarding homestead taxation.

Hearndon v. Graham


CASE NO. 92-3842


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 87; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 3754; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1039



April 14, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the circuit court for Alachua County. Stephan P. Mickle, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 26, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1898.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant stepdaughter sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida), which dismissed her complaint with prejudice against appellee stepfather for sexual abuse because the four-year statute of limitations under Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(3)(o) (1987) had run.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stepdaughter contended that the trial court should have applied the doctrine of delayed discovery of an injury to toll the four-year statute of limitations, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(3)(o) (1987), in her action against appellee stepfather for the sexual abuse he committed upon her from the age of eight until she was 15. According to appellant she suffered from traumatic amnesia or a related syndrome, which explained the delay in commencing the action. Neither party brought to the attention of the trial court Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(7) (1993), which permitted the commencement of an abuse action within seven years after the abused person reached the age of majority, or within four years of leaving the dependency of abuser, or within four years from the time of discovery by the injured party of both the injury and the casual relationship between the injury and the abuse, whichever occurred later. The court held that in light of the fact that the trial court was unaware of the amendment, it properly dismissed appellant's case, but certified the question of whether the doctrine of delayed discover could be applied to toll the statute of limitations because of traumatic amnesia.


OUTCOME: The court held that appellant stepdaughter was precluded by the statute of limitations from maintaining a suit against appellee stepfather for sexual abuse committed when she was between the ages of eight and 15. However, because the court realized that there could be more than one way to interpret the case law applicable to tolling the statute of limitations, the court certified the question.

E.P.H. v. Wright

Davis v. State


CASE NO. 97-996


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 635; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 3412; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 880



April 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, A. Thomas Mihok, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) convicting him of possession of cocaine. Appellant claimed on appeal that the noise ordinance he was violating when he was stopped by an off-duty policeman was unconstitutionally vague and violated his right to free expression, and was thus an illegal stop.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by an off-duty policeman for violating a noise ordinance. Appellant consented to a search of his vehicle, where cocaine was discovered. Appellant was convicted for possession of cocaine. On appeal, appellant argued that the cocaine was illegally seized because the ordinance that he was violating when he was stopped was unconstitutionally vague and violated his right to free expression. The court of appeals affirmed the conviction, holding that the noise ordinance was neither vague nor an illegal restraint of free expression, therefore the stop was legal. The court further held that because the search was consensual, the conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed appellant's conviction, holding the noise ordinance was neither unconstitutionally vague nor an unconstitutional restraint on appellant's right to free expression. The court further held that violation of the noise ordinance was sufficient grounds for a traffic stop, therefore the stop was legal and the ensuing search was consensual.

 

670 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Dade County v. Hernandez


CASE NO. 96-3524


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


708 So. 2d 1008; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 3134; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 847



April 1, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 6, 1998. Released for Publication May 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Petition for Certiorari to the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court for Dade County, Murray Goldman, Barbara S. Levenson, and Joel H. Brown, Judges. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-286 AP.



DISPOSITION: Appellate division's opinion quashed with directions to remand the case to the Dade County Court for a trial on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought review by certiorari of a decision of the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) which reversed a hearing officer's decision regarding a county animal control violation. Petitioner contended that the appellate division was without jurisdiction to review the hearing officer's decision.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner county issued a citation to respondent for failing to vaccinate his dog against rabies that year, in violation of the Dade County, Fla., Code § 5-7. Although contested by respondent, the citation was upheld by a county hearing officer. Respondent appealed the hearing officer's decision to the appellate division of the circuit court. The appellate division heard the appeal, rejecting petitioner's argument that the appeal was properly for the county court's consideration, and not that of the appellate division of the circuit court. The appellate division reversed the hearing officer's decision and dismissed respondent's citation. Thereafter, petitioner county sought review by certiorari, on the ground that the appellate division was without jurisdiction to review the hearing officer's decision. The reviewing court quashed the appellate division's decision and remanded the case to the county court for a trial on the merits. The court ruled that petitioner's procedure with regard to challenges of animal control citations, which called for appeals of the hearing officer's decision by trial de novo in the county court, was constitutional and should have been followed.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court quashed the appellate division's decision and remanded the case to the county court for a trial on the merits. The court ruled that the appellate division lacked jurisdiction over the matter, because petitioner's procedure with regard to challenges of animal control citations called for appeals of the hearing officer's decision by trial de novo in the county court.

Conner v. State


Case No. 96-03016


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


709 So. 2d 170; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2960; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 843



March 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; E. Randolph Bentley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; certain probation conditions stricken.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) for the offenses of armed burglary of a dwelling, armed robbery, and armed kidnapping, on the grounds that the hearsay exception for elderly and disabled adults found in Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(24) (1995) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial for armed burglary of a dwelling, armed robbery, and armed kidnapping, appellee state notified appellant of its intent to admit statements of the victim, an elderly man who had died prior to trial, under the Elderly Person or Disabled Adult hearsay exception of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(24) (1995). Appellant moved to have the statute declared unconstitutional on claims that the statute offended the confrontation clause of U.S. Const. amend. XI and that its application denied due process guaranteed by U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and Fla. Const. art. 1, § 9. The trial court refused to declare the statute unconstitutional and appellant entered a nolo contrendre plea and preserved the right to challenge his conviction on this ground. The appellate court held that it could not rule on the statute's constitutionality as applied because the trial court did not make full findings. The court found, however, that the trial court entered findings that the victim met the definition of elderly person, that he was unavailable, and that the statements were corroborated. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because he did not point to any grave deficiencies in the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because he failed to point to any grave deficiencies in the statute or its application that would cause the court to be concerned with constitutional questions. The court also held that it could not rule on the constitutionality of the statute because the trial court did not make full findings.

O'Brien v. Florida Birth-Related Neurological Injury Compensation Ass'n


CASE NO. 97-1035


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 51; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2649; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 748



March 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Division of Administrative Services; L.T. Case No. 96-1823N.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review from a decision of the Division of Administrative Services (Florida), which found that their son's death was not compensable under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 766.33 (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, as personal representatives of the estate of their son, brought an action under the Florida Birth-Related Neurological Injury Compensation Plan pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 766.33 (1995). At the start of the administrative hearing appellants' counsel asked the judge whether a report had been prepared pursuant to § 766.308. The judge responded that he was not in possession of such a report and had no information about it. Appellants made no objection to proceeding in the absence of the report, but on appeal they argued that it was error to proceed given the lack of review by a medical advisory panel. Appellee responded that there was no fundamental error and that appellants were required to object in the trial court. The court agreed with appellees and affirmed the judgment. The court reasoned that appellants' failure to object during the hearing constituted a waiver, and that fundamental error had to be equivalent to a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The finding of the administrative agency was affirmed because appellants' failure to object to the lack of review by a medical advisory panel constituted a waiver.

Nylen v. State


CASE NO. 97-00160


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 409; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2624; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 786



March 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Dennis P. Maloney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) convicting appellant and sentencing him for violating Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2) by fleeing to elude a law enforcement officer. Appellant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for fleeing to elude a law enforcement officer in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2). Appellant asserted that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2) was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the statute was constitutional as applied to appellant's case because appellant led law enforcement officers on a chase at speeds of up to 100 miles per hour for ten to fifteen minutes. The court struck the trial court's imposition of certain costs because the costs were discretionary and the trial court did not pronounce the imposition of the costs at sentencing. Appellant, however, was required to pay court costs as a condition of his order of probation.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed on the ground that the applicable statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of appellant's case where appellant led officers on a high speed chase for ten to fifteen minutes. The court struck the trial court's imposition of certain discretionary costs because the trial court did not pronounce them at sentencing. Appellant was required to pay court costs as a condition of his probation.

Paedae v. Escambia County


CASE NO. 97-2567


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


709 So. 2d 575; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2411; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 698



March 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1998. Released for Publication June 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Nickolas Geeker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida) which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee in an action for damages brought pursuant to section 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state law.


OVERVIEW: Appellants received title to a parcel of land and planned to sell parcels for single-family dwellings, including mobile homes. A purchaser was denied a mobile home permit because appellee county took the position that the mobile homes were not allowed in the areas under its comprehensive plan. Appellants filed suit seeking damages, declaratory relief, and injunctive relief for failure to follow comprehensive plan and zoning ordinances. The lower court found mobile homes to be a permitted use and enjoined appellee from enforcing its interpretation. Appellants filed an amended complaint alleging a civil rights claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging a claim of inverse condemnation against appellee and seeking other supplemental state relief. On appeal, the court affirmed summary judgment in appellee's favor. The court held that appellants had neither a federal nor state cause of action for damages, and appellee's action in regard to its interpretation of the comprehensive plan and refusal to issue a permit to appellants was a governmental function, which was protected by sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee county was affirmed because appellants had neither a federal nor state cause of action for damages, and appellee's actions in regard to its interpretation of the comprehensive plan were governmental functions protected by sovereign immunity.

 

675 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


Case No. 96-02517


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


708 So. 2d 315; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2424; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 713



March 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1998. Released for Publication April 16, 1998. Rehearing Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Fla. LEXIS 521. Released for Publication March 8, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Claudia R. Isom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of robbery with a firearm and aggravated battery, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) to sentence her as a violent career criminal under Fla. Laws ch. 95-182. Defendant claimed that her sentence was illegal because ch. 95-182 was unconstitutional as violating the single subject requirement of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery with a firearm, aggravated battery, and being a felon in possession of a firearm. The court sentenced defendant under Fla. Laws ch. 95-182 as a violent career criminal to life imprisonment on the first two counts and at least 30 years imprisonment on the third count. Defendant appealed her sentence, claiming that ch. 95-182 was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject requirement of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The appellate court held that ch. 95-182 was unconstitutional and reversed defendant's sentence. Art. III, § 6 provided that every law shall embrace but one subject. Various sections of ch. 95-182 dealt with sentencing procedures for violent career criminals, civil aspects of domestic violence, substantive and procedural rules regulating private damages actions brought by victims of domestic abuse, and procedural duties of the court clerk and sheriff regarding the filing and enforcement of domestic violence injunctions. Ch. 95-182 joined together criminal and civil subjects that had no natural or logical connection. As a result, it was unconstitutional, and defendant could not be sentenced according to its guidelines.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed a trial court's decision to sentence defendant, convicted of robbery with a firearm and aggravated battery, to life imprisonment as a violent career criminal. The appellate court explained that the violent career criminal statute joined together criminal and civil subjects that had no natural or logical connections. As a result, it was unconstitutional, and defendant could not be sentenced according to its guidelines.

Ayres v. State


CASE NO. 97-654


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


708 So. 2d 318; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2431; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 723



March 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.850 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, C. McFerrin Smith, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida) denying his motion for post-conviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with exploitation of the elderly under Fla. Stat. ch. 415.111(5) and pled no contest to the charge. At a hearing, the public defender moved to withdraw appellant's plea because Fla. Stat. ch. 415.111(5) had been declared unconstitutional. The state refused to stipulate to an oral motion because the hearing had been set to resolve disputed issues concerning restitution, and the attorney for the state said he needed time to research the issue. The trial court stayed the restitution issue, pending filing of a written motion to withdraw the plea. Two years later, appellant filed a written motion for post-conviction relief, seeking to withdraw his plea. The trial court denied the motion because it was found to be untimely. On appeal, the court reversed and held the written motion could be viewed as supplemental to or an amendment to his oral motion, which the court found to be timely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court to dismiss appellant's motion for post-conviction relief as untimely. The court reasoned that the motion was an amendment to his oral motion to withdraw his plea that was timely filed.

Gardens Country Club v. Palm Beach County


CASE NOS. 96-1165 and 96-4189


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


712 So. 2d 398; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 2270; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 682



March 11, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 16, 1998. Released for Publication April 16, 1998. Petition for Review Denied September 9, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1809.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Thomas E. Sholts, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 89-4494 AG.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant country club sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which granted summary judgment to appellee county in appellant's complaint for inverse condemnation and for violation of its due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled, on appellant country club's complaint for inverse condemnation, that the claim was ripe for review, that there had been no total temporary taking by appellee county of appellant's property, and that appellant's vested right to develop the property in connection with the then-existing comprehensive plan did not rise to the level of a constitutionally protected property interest. Explaining, the court ruled that because appellee refused to consider appellant's application for rezoning under the applicable 1980 plan, in view of appellee's mandate that development plans satisfy an incipient comprehensive plan, it would have been futile for appellant to file another application under the incipient plan. However, appellee's action in enacting an ordinance that would refuse to certify applications inconsistent with the incipient plan did not constitute a partial taking, as appellant was not deprived of a substantially economic beneficial use of the property. Because there was a plausible basis for appellee to pass the ordinance, so as to bar development inconsistent with the incipient plan, appellant suffered no deprivation of a constitutionally protected interest.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed granting summary judgment to appellee county in appellant country club's complaint for inverse condemnation and for violation of its due process rights, because no total temporary taking by appellee of appellant's property had occurred and because appellant's vested right to develop its property in connection with then-existing comprehensive plan did not rise to level of constitutionally protected property interest.

D.L.B. v. State


CASE NO. 96-01814


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 844; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1894; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 592



February 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 11, 1998. Released for Publication March 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Edgar Hinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Sentence remanded for clarification. Written disposition order must be corrected to conform to the court's oral announcement that the Crimes Compensation Trust Fund fine would be waived.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) judgment adjudicating him delinquent after he disrupted a school function and committed the offense of affray, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 870.01(1) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was found delinquent after disrupting a school function and committing the offense of affray, fighting in a public place to the terror of the people. Defendant then appealed, challenging the affray statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 870.01(1) (1995), as unconstitutionally vague, and arguing various other errors. The court held that the term affray was defined with sufficient definiteness that the statute was not impermissibly vague. Further, the court held that the lower court had not been required to ask for a second restrictiveness level recommendation after rejecting the first one, but found that the lower court's failure to distinguish between defendant's two offenses in pronouncing sentence and failure to specify the term of community control or maximum term of commitment required remand for clarification. Finally, the court held that the lower court's oral pronouncement that a fine would be waived required that the fine be struck on remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the statute was constitutional but that the vagueness of the sentencing required clarification, and finding that the lower court's failure to conform its imposition of a fine to its earlier oral pronouncement required that the fine be struck.

Floyd v. State


CASE NO. 96-4571


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 833; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1886; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 651



February 26, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Kenneth L. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida), in which the court entered judgment sentencing appellant pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.001(5) to a term that exceeded the statutory maximum.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence and driving with a suspended license. The trial court imposed a sentence pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.001(5) that exceeded the statutory maximum sentence. Appellant challenged his sentence asserting that section 921.001(5) was unconstitutional because it failed to give adequate notice of the possible penalties. The appeals court affirmed appellant's sentence. According to the appeals court, although section 921.001(5) allowed for the imposition of sentence that exceeded the statutory maximum, the section was still valid. In finding section 921.001(5) constitutional, the appeals court held that section 921.001(5) stood for the unremarkable proposition that the sentencing guidelines could trump the statutory maximum otherwise set by law. The appeals court held that a maximum sentence could be determined in any case simply by completing a sentencing guidelines score sheet, as such, section 921.001(5) provided adequate notice of the potential penalties for an offense.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed appellant's sentence which exceed the statutory maximum because the sentencing guidelines provided adequate notice of the possible penalties.

 

680 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


McElrath v. Burley


CASE NO. 97-1210


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 836; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1901; 73 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P45,314; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 647



February 26, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. F. E. Steinmeyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, in his capacity as Executive Director of the Florida Commission on Human Relations, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which held unconstitutional a portion of the Florida Civil Rights Act of 1992, Fla. Stat. ch. 760.11(7), in appellee employee's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employee filed a sexual discrimination claim with the state commission on human relations (the commission). When the claim was denied pursuant to a no-cause finding, appellee did not file an administrative complaint under Fla. Stat. ch. 760.11(7) to challenge the ruling. Instead, appellee filed a declaratory judgment action against appellant, executive director of the commission, seeking to have ch. 760.11(7) declared unconstitutional. The trial court held that ch. 760.11(7) was unconstitutional, but the appellate court reversed and remanded the judgment. The court held that ch. 760.11(7) was not unconstitutional as an improper restriction of the right of access to the courts. Appellee had no constitutional right of access for her discrimination claim because it was not a common law claim. The court also found that the claim was insufficient to support an equal protection violation. The statute did not contain any classification, which discriminated between charging parties. Further, any alleged disparate treatment was rationally related to the permissible governmental purpose of avoiding court docket congestion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded an order that held unconstitutional a portion of the Florida Civil Rights Act in appellee employee's declaratory judgment action. The procedure for filing an administrative complaint to challenge a no-cause finding was not unconstitutional where it did not improperly restrict appellee employee's right of access to the courts and did not violate equal protection and due process rights.

Russo v. Persico


CASE NO. 97-4216


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


706 So. 2d 933; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1824; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 567



February 25, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Lawrence L. Korda, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-1756(41)(91).



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), granting visitation rights under Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a) to appellees, the maternal grandparents of appellant's daughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a father whose deceased wife's parents successfully obtained visitation rights with appellant's four-year-old daughter under Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a), challenged the constitutionality of trial court's order granting visitation. On review, the appellate court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a) unconstitutionally infringed on appellant's fundamental right to his raise his child free from interference by the government as protected by the privacy provision in Fla. Const. art. 1, § 23. The statute was flawed because it required the trial court to award reasonable visitation rights merely upon a showing of the best interest of the child without a prior showing that demonstrable harm would result if appellees could not visit with the child. Noting conflict with other state appellate courts, the appeals court ruled in favor of appellant, quashed the trial court's order, and certified the question for review by the state's highest court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting appellee grandparents visitation rights as to their granddaughter, appellant's daughter, because a state statute mandated such visitation based only upon the best interest of the child and did not require an initial showing of demonstrable harm and because the statute violated appellant's privacy rights as guaranteed by the state constitution.

Nelson v. Department of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation


CASE NO.: 97-1249


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 378; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1527; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 535

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 10, 1998. Released for Publication March 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative Appeal from the Department of Business and Professional Regulation.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate broker sought review of the order from appellee, the Florida Department of Business and Professional Regulation, finding appellant guilty of violating Fla. Stat. ch. 475.25(1)(f), fining him, and placing him on probation after appellant had pleaded nolo contendere to charges of battery and criminal mischief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant real estate broker pleaded nolo contendere to charges of battery and criminal mischief filed against him after he set off a smoke bomb at an agency's offices as a political protest over agency actions. Appellee business and professional regulation department found appellant guilty of violating Fla. Stat. ch. 475.25(f)(1) because he had been found guilty of a crime directly relating to the activities of a licensed real estate salesperson or involving moral turpitude or fraudulent or dishonest dealings. Appellee fined appellant and placed him on probation. On appeal, the court reversed appellee's decision. Appellant's misdemeanors of battery and criminal mischief did not show a baseness or depravity in appellant that impugned his ability to deal fairly with the public to the extent that suspension of his broker's license was warranted.

State v. Presidential Women's Ctr.


CASE NO. 97-2577


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


707 So. 2d 1145; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1372; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 491



February 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Clarification Granted April 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 3849. Released for Publication April 15, 1998.
Clarified by, Opinion replaced by, in part State v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 3849 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Apr. 15, 1998)
Appeal after remand at Crist v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15011 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Kathleen Kroll, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 97-5796 AG.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a non-final order from the Circuit Court of Palm Beach County, which granted appellee abortion clinics a temporary injunction enjoining enforcement of the Women's Right to Know Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 390.0111 (1997), on constitutional grounds pending a final hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellee abortion clinics brought suit against appellant state to have the Women's Right to Know Act (Act), Fla. Stat. ch. 390.0111 (1997), declared unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions. The trial court temporarily enjoined enforcement of the Act on constitutional grounds pending a final hearing. Appellant sought review of the non-final order. Affirming, the court held that the right of privacy under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23 afforded a greater protection than the right of privacy under the federal constitution and demanded the compelling state interest standard. Under established authority, the court held, the state did not have a compelling interest in the health of a pregnant woman during the first trimester, or in a fetus before it was viable. The court also reminded that laws regulating a woman's right to terminate her pregnancy were subject to the strict scrutiny test of constitutionality. Focusing on the Act's informed consent provisions, Fla. Stat. ch. 390.0111(3)(a)1 (1997), the court concluded that appellees had sufficiently established a substantial likelihood of prevailing on the merits to support the temporary injunction.


OUTCOME: Finding that appellee abortion clinics had sufficiently established a substantial likelihood of prevailing on the merits of their constitutional challenges to the Women's Right to Know Act (Act), the court affirmed the trial court's order temporarily enjoining appellant state from enforcing Act, pending a final hearing.

Brooks v. Watchtower Bible & Tract Soc'y


CASE NO. 97-4167


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT

February 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Kenneth A. Marra, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 97-009440 AB.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of the Circuit Court of the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), enjoining appellants from holding a referendum to repeal an ordinance passed by the city commission that authorized the sale of municipal property to appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged an order of the trial court that enjoined the holding of a city referendum to repeal an ordinance passed by the city commission authorizing the sale of a 72-acre tract of municipal land that included an auditorium to appellees. In granting the injunction, the trial court considered the charter provision providing for a referendum but determined that under case law it did not apply to administrative ordinances. The appellate court held that the ordinance was the proper subject of the referendum under the Florida Constitution, state statutes, and the city charter and code. In addition, the court perceived no conflict with any Florida statute in the provision for the disposition of municipal property by ordinance. Therefore, the court reversed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed because appellants were entitled to hold a referendum to repeal an ordinance that authorized the sale of municipal property to appellees. The ordinance was the proper subject of the referendum under the Florida Constitution, state statutes, and the city charter and code.

Murphy v. International Robotics Sys.


CASE NO. 97-0388


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 587; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1155; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 447



February 11, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1998. Released for Publication March 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward H. Fine, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 94-5321AI.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), and argued that defendants' counsel had made an improper closing argument.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower court's decision in a civil case. Counsel for defendants had made improper remarks during closing argument, stating among other things that if plaintiffs were awarded damages, they would be accessories to tax fraud. Counsel for plaintiffs did not make a contemporaneous objection. Although the other courts of appeal of the state found that such remarks constituted fundamental error going to the merits of the action, the court disagreed that a new trial was necessary. Generally, it was necessary to make contemporaneous objections at the time the remarks were made. The state bar still investigated and disciplined attorneys who made unethical arguments and the court still reported such statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court decision, because unethical remarks by defendants' counsel during closing arguments did not constitute fundamental error that went to the merits of the action, and plaintiffs had not objected to the remarks.

 

686 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Love PGI Partners, LP v. Schultz


CASE NO. 96-1973


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


706 So. 2d 887; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 920; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 417



February 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1998. Released for Publication April 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Citrus County, Patricia Thomas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partners sought review of the final judgments rendered against them by the Circuit Court for Citrus County (Florida) concerning appellee property appraiser's denial of appellants' claims for agricultural classification for certain lands.


OVERVIEW: Appellant partners owned land that appellee property appraiser found to be ineligible for agriculture classification for tax purposes. Before the court was whether there was substantial competent evidence to determine that appellants' use of part of their lands for forestry by natural regeneration was not bona fide. Also before the court was whether cattle-grazing operations conducted on part of one of appellants' property could not qualify for an agricultural classification. The judgment of the lower court was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the lower court finding that denied agricultural classification for the natural woodlands. The court found there was insufficient evidence of any actual forestry operations on the lands in question. The court reversed the lower court finding that denied appellants' agricultural classification for the parcel of land where cattle grazed. The court found that the appropriateness of agricultural classification of land for ad valorem tax purposes depended on the general statutory laws of Florida, not a county code.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the portion of the lower court judgment that denied an agricultural classification for the natural woodlands appellant partners owned. The court reversed the portion of the lower court judgment that denied an agricultural classification for a fenced-in area where cattle grazed.
