Spence v. Stewart


CASE NO. 96-4162


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


705 So. 2d 996; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 910; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 405



February 4, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; J. Leonard Fleet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-685 (42).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother challenged an order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which denied her request to establish visitation rights with her grandson and declared Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(d) (1995) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother brought a paternity action against the father of her out of wedlock child. Appellant grandmother intervened and sought visitation rights. Appellant's motion did not refer to a specific statutory provision. The trial court sua sponte declared that Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(d) (1995), which provided visitation rights to grandparents of out of wedlock children, was an unconstitutional violation of the right to privacy and denied appellant's request for visitation. The court reversed and remanded because matters involving custody and visitation in paternity actions should be based on the best interest of the child as in dissolution proceedings, and Fla. Stat. ch. 61.13(2)(b)(2)(c) (1995) provided for grandparental visitation in a dissolution proceeding if such visitation was in the child's best interest. The court held that by bringing their dispute to court, the parents had abandoned their right of familial privacy and an award of grandparental visitation did not violate their rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied appellant grandmother's request to establish visitation rights with her grandson and remanded because Florida law provided that courts could award grandparental visitation rights if such visitation was in the child's best interest.

Optiplan, Inc. v. School Bd.


CASE NO. 96-1016


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


710 So. 2d 569; 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 626; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 331



January 28, 1998, Opinion Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Division of Administrative Hearings, School Board of Broward County; DOAH Case No. 95-4560BID and RFP No. 96-29S

At appellant's request, appellee school board referred the case to an administrative hearing officer. At the beginning of the hearing, appellant moved to amend its pleadings. Appellant sought judicial review. The court reversed the order and remanded the matter. It held that the hearing officer had the authority to allow an amendment of the bid protest and that the amendment should have been allowed.

Waites v. State


CASE NO. 96-2178


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


702 So. 2d 1373; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 14516; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 148



December 31, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward A. Garrison, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 95-10296 CFA02, 90-016602 CFA02, 90-016603 CFA02, 91-012774 CFA02, 91-013278 CFA02, 91-13726 CFA02, 92-008134 CFA02 and 92-008648 CFA02.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Clarification for Withdrawn Opinion of November 19, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13124.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a judgment from Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted and sentenced him for operating a motor vehicle without having a driver's license, as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 322.03(3)(b), in a careless and negligent manner resulting in the death of another human being in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(3)(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant drove a truck owned and maintained by his employer. At the end of a work day, appellant, while driving through a busy intersection, collided with an automobile, killing the driver of another automobile. At the time of the collision, appellant possessed a chauffeur's license, which was not the appropriate license for operating the truck. At appellant's trial, testimony was presented that the department of motor vehicle extensively advertised the new license classifications. Notification was mailed to all chauffeur's license holders. The scheme appeared on the back of all licenses, and appellant's license was re-issued while the new classifications were in effect. Appellant was found guilty. On appeal, the court stated that to be charged under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(3)(b), appellant's license had to be suspended, canceled, or revoked because of some wrongdoing. Appellant's negligence in operating the vehicle could only enhance some willful act. The court held that the prosecution failed to met its burden of proving that appellant knew of his license's invalidity. Therefore, the judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that convicted and sentenced appellant for violation of motor vehicle laws was reversed and remanded because appellant's actions were not willful, but negligent, and the prosecution failed to show that appellant knew that his license was invalid.

 

692 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Mancini v. Personalized Air Conditioning & Heating


CASE NO. 97-1525


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


702 So. 2d 1376; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 14539; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 85



December 31, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Cynthia G. Angelos, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-062 CA.



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED; REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a part-time newspaper columnist, filed a petition for writ of certiorari from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida). Defendant claimed that plaintiff corporation was required to give her pre-suit notice under Fla. Stat. ch. 770.01 (1995) prior to filing a libel action against her and that plaintiff failed to comply with this statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought a libel action for statements contained in two of defendant's newspaper columns. Plaintiff claimed that the publications were libelous because defendant allegedly implied that plaintiff was the same corporation as a defunct and discredited corporation. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss asserting that plaintiff failed to comply with the statutory notice requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 770.01 (1995), which defendant claimed was a condition precedent to plaintiff's libel action. Plaintiff claimed that this statute did not apply to defendant because she was a part-time columnist and was not newspaper entity. The legal question posed by defendant's petition for writ of certiorari was whether a columnist for a local newspaper was entitled to pre-suit notice pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 770.01 (1995) before plaintiff could file its libel action. The court determined that the plain language of the statute made no distinction between suits against the newspaper itself and the individuals who wrote for it. The court held that defendant fell within the statutory protection and that defendant was entitled to pre-suit notice before plaintiff could maintain its libel action.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's petition for writ of certiorari and quashed the order denying defendant's motion to dismiss. The court held that defendant, a part-time newspaper columnist, was entitled to pre-suit notice prior to the filing of a libel action so that defendant could print a retraction of any errors before she had to defend against a libel action.

 

693 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gloster


CASE NO. 96-4559


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


703 So. 2d 1174; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 14566; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 32



December 18, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 9, 1998. Released for Publication January 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Kenneth L. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order by the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida), which dismissed an information charging appellee with a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c) (1995) on the ground that it unconstitutionally delegated legislative power to the judiciary.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state charged appellee with driving a motor vehicle with a suspended or revoked license under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1)(c) (1995) when he had previous convictions for driving violations. The trial court dismissed the charge on the basis that the statute unconstitutionally delegated legislative power to the judiciary to determine whether the charge was a misdemeanor or a felony. Appellant contended that the trial court's order was based upon flawed reasoning. The court, in agreement, reversed and remanded the case. Under the statutory scheme, treating a violation of ch. 322.34(1)(c) as a misdemeanor was not an available alternative. A person whose adjudication was withheld pending completion of probation was not a convicted person. If probation was revoked, adjudication of guilt as to the offense was required. Thus, ch. 322.34(1)(c) did not involve an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, because the trial court erred in finding that appellant state's criminal charges against appellee stemmed from an unconstitutional statute.

 

694 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Hooper v. State


CASE NO. 96-3068


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


703 So. 2d 1143; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13658; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 2762



December 10, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 20, 1998. Released for Publication January 20, 1998. Petition for Review Denied May 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Sheldon Shapiro, Judge; L.T. Case No. 95-1552CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which convicted him of robbery with a firearm, theft of a motor vehicle, and aggravated fleeing and eluding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery with a firearm, theft of a motor vehicle, and aggravated fleeing and eluding. On appeal, defendant argued that after the robbery took place, the state supreme court made a substantive change in the standard jury instruction on principals, making it easier for the state to obtain a conviction, and that the trial court's use of the new instruction was an ex post facto law violation. The appellate court held that the use of the new instruction, which enabled the state to establish guilt without two elements contained in the prior instruction, was an ex post facto violation. Nevertheless, the court affirmed the conviction, finding that the use of the new instruction was harmless error. The state presented extensive evidence, and its primary position was that defendant was a substantial participant in the crimes, not merely a principal. Besides defendant's confession, there was other overwhelming evidence of his guilt as an active participant, not as a principal, which led the court to conclude that the use of the new instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of robbery with a firearm, theft of a motor vehicle, and aggravated fleeing and eluding. Although the trial court's use of a new jury instruction on principals constituted an ex post facto violation, the error was harmless because the state presented extensive evidence that defendant was a substantial participant in the crimes, and not merely a principal.

D.P. v. State


CASE NO. 96-3289


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


705 So. 2d 593; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13883; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2744



December 10, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 4, 1998. Released for Publication March 4, 1998. Petition for Review Denied May 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 964.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Thomas K. Peterson, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-12851.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged his adjudication of delinquency by the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) under the county's comprehensive anti-graffiti ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile challenged his adjudication of delinquency under the county's anti-graffiti ordinance which forbid the sale to minors of spray paint and jumbo markers. He alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it violated his due process rights as it imposed a criminal penalty without requiring the state to show criminal intent. Appellant reasoned that these objects had legitimate household uses, so it was impermissible to criminalize simple possession of ordinary household goods. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance passed constitutional muster because it did not place an outright ban on the possession of these objects by minors; rather it allowed minors to possess them on public property if accompanied by an adult or on private property with the owner's consent. Also, there were instances where public interest required the prohibition of innocent acts in order to secure enforcement of the laws against evil acts. The court then held that it was permissible for the court to treat minors differently from adults. Finally, the court maintained that the possession of spray paint and jumbo markers did not implicate a fundamental right.


OUTCOME: The adjudication of delinquency was affirmed because the anti-graffiti ordinance under which appellant juvenile was prosecuted was constitutional and enforceable.

Sharper Image Corp. v. Department of Revenue


CASE NO. 96-3734


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


704 So. 2d 657; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13647; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2766



December 8, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 16 1998. Released for Publication March 4 1998. Certiorari Denied March 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1889.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Leon County, William Gary, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant out-of-state corporation sought review of the order from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) that granted appellee state department of revenue's motion for summary judgment on appellant's complaint challenging a use tax assessment on it catalogs under Fla. Stat. ch. 212,05(1)(b), ch. 212.06(1)(a), and ch. 212.06(6) (1987), and claiming that the religious exemption of Fla. Stat. ch. 212,06(9) (1987) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant out-of-state corporation sent product catalogs to Florida customers. Appellee state department of revenue assessed a use tax on the catalogs in addition to the sales tax on the mail order sales. Appellant filed an action challenging the assessment, and the trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that because the catalogs were items of tangible property that were distributed in Florida, they were subject to the use tax under Fla. Stat. ch. 212.05(1)(b), ch. 212.06(1)(a), and ch. 212.06(6) (1987) whether or not a customer purchased anything from the catalogs. The court held that even if the newspaper and religious exemptions to the use tax under Fla. Stat. ch. 212,08(7)(w) (Supp. 1988) and 212.06(9) (1987) were unconstitutional, under Fla. Stat. ch. 212.21 (1987), appellant's remedy was to abolish the exemption, not the assessment. Therefore, the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting appellee state department of revenue's motion for summary judgment on appellant out-of-state corporation's complaint challenging a use tax assessment on its catalogs, because the catalogs were distributed in Florida and thus expressly subject to the tax, and state law required appellant to pay the tax whether or not the religious exemption was unconstitutional.

Waites v. State


CASE NO. 96-2178


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13124; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2628



November 19, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Clarification Granted on December 31, Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 14516.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward A. Garrison, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 95-10296 CFA02, 90-016602 CFA02, 90-016603 CFA02, 91-012774 CFA02, 91-013278 CFA02, 91-13726 CFA02, 92-008134 CFA02 and 92-008648 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS THAT APPELLANT BE DISCHARGED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), convicting him of operating a motor vehicle without a driver's license and operating in a careless and negligent manner resulting in the death of another, violations of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.03(3)(b) and 322.34(3)(a), respectively, and revoking his probation on seven prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle without a driver's license and operating in a careless and negligent manner resulting in the death of another, violations of Fla. Stat. chs. 322.03(3)(b) and 322.34(3)(a). As a result of those convictions, appellant had his probation revoked on seven prior felony convictions. The court reversed the convictions of appellant and remanded the matter with instructions that appellant be discharged, finding that the offense under ch. 322.34(3)(a) did not impose strict criminal liability and that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant violated the statute willfully. The court determined that there was no clear legislative intent to impose strict criminal liability under the statute and concluded that in order to convict appellant under the statute, the state would have had to prove appellant willfully failed to have the proper driver's license. The court found that the failure to establish the requisite mens rea required that appellant be acquitted of the offense, and with the acquittal, the probation revocation resulting from the conviction was also reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions of appellant for operating a motor vehicle without a driver's license and operating in a careless and negligent manner resulting in the death of another, finding that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant acted willfully. The court determined that the statute did not impose strict criminal liability and that the state had the burden of establishing mens rea.

 

699 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Halifax Hosp. Medical Ctr. v. News-Journal Corp.


CASE NO. 96-3115


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 434; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 12765; 26 Media L. Rep. 1189; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2587



November 14, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Released for Publication December 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, John V. Doyle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED but withhold mandate pending review by the supreme court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida), which determined that the exemption to Fla. Const. art. I, § 24(a) contained in Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3035(4), which permitted the hospital's governing board meetings to be closed when strategic plan were discussed, was unconstitutional in that it was broader than necessary to accomplish the stated purpose of the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee news media challenged the constitutionality of the exemption provided for in Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3035(4) (1995), which provided that portions of appellant public hospital's governing board meetings be closed when confidential contracts or strategic plans were discussed. Fla. Const. art. I, § 24(a) provided for open meetings, but the legislature was authorized to provide exemptions if such law stated with specificity the public necessity justifying the exemption and such exemption was no broader than necessary to accomplish the stated purpose of the law. The trial court found the exemption to Fla. Const. art. I, § 24(a) contained in the statute was unconstitutional. To determine if the exemption was no broader than necessary, the court looked to the exemption and its duration. There was no statutory limit of what could be discussed during closed portion of meeting. There was no definition of, and therefore no limitation on what could be included in a strategic plan. The court held that at the very least, the term "strategic plan" should have been defined. Thus, the court affirmed the trial court's decision; however, it also certified the question to the supreme court.


OUTCOME: While the court affirmed the trial court's decision that the exemption provided for by statute, which permitted appellant hospital to close its governing board meetings to appellee news media when strategic plans were discussed, was unconstitutional, it also certified the question to the supreme court because it was a critical issue of statewide concern.

Pohlmann v. Pohlmann


Case No. 96-1709 & 96-2476


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


703 So. 2d 1121; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 12761; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2592



November 14, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 2, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Newman D. Brock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband challenged the final judgment of the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida) denying modification of his child support obligations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former husband's and appellee former wife's final judgment of dissolution provided that appellant would pay child support and 100 percent of medical expenses not covered by insurance. Appellant petitioned for modification of child support alleging that there had been a substantial change in his financial circumstances warranting a downward modification of his obligation. Appellant also contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 61.30(12) was unconstitutional. The trial court found that there was no substantial change in circumstances which would justify a reduction in the former husband's child support obligations and that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court agreed that the statute was constitutional as it furthered a legitimate state interest, assuring that noncustodial parents continued to support children from their first marriage notwithstanding their obligation to support subsequently born children. The court agreed there was no substantial change warranting a reduction in child support but remanded the matter for the trial court to consider a reduction in child support for the extended visitation granted to appellant.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant former husband modification of his child support obligation was affirmed in part as there was no substantial change in circumstances warranting reduction and was reversed regarding reduction in medical expense reimbursement paid by appellant. Further the matter was remanded for the lower court to consider a reduction in support for the extended visitation granted appellant.

Parham v. Balis


CASE NO. 96-03037


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


704 So. 2d 623; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 12716; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2613



November 12, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1998. Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Daniel E. Gallagher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order dismissing amended complaint reversed and remanded for further proceedings. Question certified as one of great public importance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the Circuit Court of Hillsborough County (Florida), dismissing his medical malpractice complaint with prejudice because it was untimely filed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a medical malpractice action against appellees, physicians and institute, for a medical procedure that took place on December 18, 1990. Appellant alleged he discovered the negligence in December 1993 and on December 16, 1994, appellant filed a petition under Fla. Stat. ch. 766.104(2) for an automatic 90-day extension of the two-year statute of limitations. In March 1995, appellant served notice of his intent to initiate litigation and on April 17, 1995, appellant served an amended notice adding appellee institute. Appellant's initial complaint was filed in July 1995, and an amended complaint adding appellee physician was filed in September 1995. The lower court dismissed the amended complaint with prejudice and held that appellant's amended action was barred because appellant was required to file suit by January 29, 1995. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the order holding that the 90-day extension and the notice of intent to initiate malpractice litigation under Fla. Stat. chs. 766.104(2) and 766.106(4) extended the statute of limitation and the statute of repose. The court also certified the question for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order that dismissed appellant's complaint with prejudice holding that appellant's statutory extension and a notice of intent to initiate malpractice litigation had extended the statute of limitation and the statute of repose.

Gassner v. Bechtel Constr. & Indus. Indem.


CASE NO.: 96-2006


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


702 So. 2d 548; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 12686; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2581



November 10, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1997. Released for Publication January 5, 1998. Petition for Review Denied May 12, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 931.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of Judge of Compensation Claims Melanie Jacobson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of Judge of Compensation Claims (Florida) dismissing his petition for workers' compensation benefits, including payment of medical and pharmaceutical bills and attorney's fees and costs, for lack of jurisdiction because of a collective bargaining agreement and pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 440.211.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought workers' compensation benefits including payment of medical and pharmaceutical bills and attorney's fees and costs. The Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) dismissed his petition on the grounds that his exclusive remedy for benefits not already furnished was under a collective bargaining agreement (CBA), which established an alternative dispute resolution (ADR) system. Appellant challenged the ruling. The court affirmed. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.211(2)(1995) the JCC lacked jurisdiction over compensation claims when the CBA met the statutory criteria. The JCC viewed the jurisdictional issue correctly in considering only the narrow question: whether the CBA supplanted provisions of ch. 440 that would otherwise apply to appellant's claim, in the posture she found the case when the jurisdictional determination had to be made. The court refused to disturb her determination that the CBA's established ADR system was intended to supplant chs. 440.25 and 440.271 whenever litigation would otherwise be required to establish entitlement to or the amount of an attorney's fee that an employer allegedly owed an employee's attorney.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that the Judge of Compensation lacked jurisdiction to act on appellant's petition for benefits by virtue of a collective bargaining agreement and in conformity with a state statute.

 

703 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


J.D.L.R. v. State


CASE NO. 96-0592


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 626; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 12256; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2531



November 5, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Steve Levine, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-3412.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Dade County (Florida), challenging his adjudication of delinquency and the denial of his motion to dismiss the charge of carrying a weapon on school grounds based on his contention that the knife he was carrying was a common pocketknife, excepted under Fla. Stat. ch. 790.115(2) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was arrested for carrying a weapon on school grounds in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.115(2) (1995). Defendant moved to dismiss the charge on the grounds that the knife he was carrying was a common pocketknife, which was excepted from the definition of weapon under the statute. The trial court denied the motion and, based on observations that the knife had weapon-like characteristics, permitted the state to argue that the knife was a weapon. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion and the trial court's subsequent adjudication of defendant as delinquent. The court affirmed, concluding that the knife did not fall within the definition of common pocketknife. Although the knife was a pocketknife, it had distinctive features that were not characteristic of a typical, ordinary, pocketknife but were characteristic of a weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant juvenile's adjudication as delinquent and the denial of his motion to dismiss the charge of carrying a weapon on school grounds, holding that the knife carried by defendant fell within the statutory definition of weapon because of features that were not typical, ordinary, or frequently occurring in pocketknives.

Appellant specifically challenged the imposition of a condition in his standard probation order prohibiting him from possessing any drugs not prescribed by a physician.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced for a home invasion robbery. Appellant's sentence consisted of 72 months imprisonment followed by five years' probation. The court therefore affirmed appellant's conviction and sentencing, with the exception of striking the investigative cost.

Frear v. State


CASE NO. 96-4048


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Florida) for possession of a firearm by a violent career criminal, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.235(1) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with possession of a firearm by a violent career criminal, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.235(1) (1995). Appellant filed a motion to dismiss the charge on the basis that the statute was unconstitutional because it was susceptible to arbitrary and capricious application and was impermissibly vague, The trial court denied appellant's motion and the appellate court affirmed. The appellate court held that the statute was not susceptible to arbitrary and capricious application even though prosecutors could have charged appellant under another statute. The court ruled that the statute was not vague because a person of common intelligence and understanding could have understood what conduct was prohibited and because ch. 775.084(1)(c) provided a clear definition of what constituted a violent career criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a violent career criminal and the court held that the statute under which appellant was charged was not susceptible to arbitrary and capricious application and was not impermissibly vague.

Watkins v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida) that convicted him of two marijuana offenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for two marijuana offenses. Appellant sought review of his convictions, contending that the inclusion of cannabis as a schedule I during in Fla. Stat. ch. 893.03(1) (1993) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed appellant's convictions. The court found that the Florida Supreme Court had held that the placement of cannabis in schedule I of the list of controlled substances was constitutional. The Florida Supreme Court held that there continued to be expert opinion supporting the reasons which had prompted the legislature to enact the statute and that this was sufficient to constitute a continuing rational basis for the act. The court held that the record before it contained expert testimony sufficient to satisfy it that there continued to be a rational basis for the inclusion of cannabis under schedule I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that convicted appellant of two marijuana offenses. The court held that the record contained expert testimony sufficient to satisfy it that there continued to be a rational bases for the inclusion of cannabis under schedule I.

 

707 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Poulos v. Martin County


CASE NO. 96-2853


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


700 So. 2d 163; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11558; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2395



October 15, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Cynthia G. Angelos, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-126-CA.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), which held that a certain development decision by defendant county sought by defendant developer was consistent with the county's comprehensive plan. Plaintiffs' action was brought pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 163.3215 (1995), and the trial court applied an appellate standard of review to defendant county's actions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' action was filed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 163.3215 (1995) and sought a declaratory judgment that a development action taken by defendant county was inconsistent with the comprehensive plan. Defendant developer was permitted to intervene and the trial court granted its motion to review the action of the county in its appellate capacity rather than by conducting a trial de novo. The trial court upheld defendant county's action and plaintiffs appealed. The court reversed, holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 163.3215 (1995) provided for a trial de novo in the trial court. Construing the statute to provide for review by writ of certiorari would be contrary to rules of appellate procedure which required that petitions for review must be filed within 30 days of the order to be reviewed. In contrast, Fla. Stat. ch. 163.3215 (1995) contained a pre-suit filing requirement, requiring the challenging party to file a complaint with the local government before filing a lawsuit. This meant that the suit in circuit court would be filed up to 90 days after the issuance of the development order, which would be contrary to the 30-day requirement of Fla. R. App. P. 9.100(c)(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a trial de novo because the statute authorizing plaintiffs' suit provided for a trial de novo in cases challenging actions of local governments. If the statute were to be construed as providing only for appellate review by the trial court it would be contrary to the rules of appellate procedure.

Travis v. State


CASE NO. 96-2925


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


700 So. 2d 104; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11441; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2349



October 7, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Nancy Gilliam, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida) convicting appellant upon a plea of nolo contendere to aggravated fleeing and eluding, resisting arrest without violence, and driving with a suspended license. Appellant asserted that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2), prohibiting fleeing and eluding an officer, was unconstitutionally vague on its face because it did not provide adequate notice of proscribed conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was spotted by a police officer driving the wrong way down a one-way street with his car headlights off. The officer attempted to stop appellant with his police cruiser, but appellant maneuvered around the cruiser. The officer pursued appellant down several streets at high speeds, but appellant refused to yield until he wrecked his car. Appellant fled on foot, but was apprehended by police. Appellant was charged with aggravated fleeing and eluding, resisting arrest without violence, and driving with a suspended license. Appellant moved to dismiss the fleeing and eluding charge on constitutional grounds, which was denied. Appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere, preserving his right to appeal. On appeal, the court affirmed judgment convicting appellant because Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2), which prohibited fleeing and eluding a police officer, was constitutional on its face because it gave fair notice of the conduct proscribed. The court held that consideration of the facts as applied to determining the facial validity of the statute was appropriate, because Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2) did not purport to regulate any constitutionally protected activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment convicting appellant of aggravated fleeing and eluding, resisting arrest without violence, and driving with a suspended license, because the statute prohibiting fleeing and eluding a police officer was constitutional on its face because it gave fair notice of the conduct proscribed.

Stewart v. Price


CASE NO.: 95-996


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


718 So. 2d 205; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11439; 23 Fla. L. Weekly D 1800



October 7, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Gadsden County. N. Sander Sauls, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant representatives challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Gadsden County (Florida), which ruled for appellee doctor in the medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant representatives pursued a suit against appellee doctor for negligent diagnosis and treatment, intentional misrepresentation, concealment of the condition of the deceased, and negligent care and treatment of cirrhosis. They also challenged the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 768.21(8) (1991). By the time of trial, the only issue remaining for the jury was the claim of medical malpractice. The trial court prohibited testimony by a witness on the standard of care for internists, finding that the witness was a general practitioner, not an expert as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 766.102(2)(b) (1991). On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case for a new trial. The witness met the criteria for a specialist in internal medicine under the statute, so the trial court erred in precluding his testimony. Appellants failed to show, however that ch. 768.21(8) (1991) was unconstitutional because it provided that adult children could not recover damages in wrongful death actions stemming from medical malpractice. The statute did not deny federal and state constitutional guarantees of equal protection of the laws and due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial. The trial court erred in excluding testimony by a witness on the grounds he was not an expert, as he qualified as a specialist in internal medicine under the expert witness statute.

The court also held that the state was in the same position as any creditor as to the applicability of the homestead provisions.

Bradenton Group v. Department of Legal Affairs


CASE NO. 96-2661 and 96-2979


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 1170; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11137; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2320



October 3, 1997, Opinion Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Non-Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, R. James Stroker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporations challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which held that appellee State of Florida was entitled to a temporary injunction against appellants preventing them from conducting any bingo operations or spending any money in their bank accounts. Appellee state of Florida challenged the trial court's ruling requiring it to post a bond during appellate review.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State of Florida charged appellants corporations with operating illegal bingo operations and violating state gambling laws. Appellee state of Florida filed a motion with the trial court to impose a temporary injunction against appellants from operating bingo operations and freezing their bank accounts. The trial judge refused to lift the injunction but ordered appellee to post the bond. Both parties challenged the ruling. The court held that appellee was entitled to a temporary injunction against appellants, because their actions constituted serious violations of the law, and certified a legal question to the state supreme court. The court also upheld the trial judge's order for the bond, stating that the law permitted appellants to recover damages from appellee if they won their case and therefore the bond requirement was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that appellee was entitled to a temporary injunction preventing appellants from conducting bingo operations or spending any money from their bank account. Appellants were entitled to have appellee post a bond for any damages appellants incurred during the judicial proceedings.

Casterline v. State

COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) that revoked appellant's probation and entered an order enhancing appellant's conditions of his probation a few years after appellant pleaded guilty to two counts of sexual performance by a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to two counts of sexual performance by a child and was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment followed by 15 years' probation. Seven years later, appellant was arrested for aggravated assault with a knife sharpener upon a minor. The court reversed and remanded, holding that a court could not change an order of probation by enhancing the terms absent proof of a violation; and challenges to improper enhancement of the terms of probation could be raised in a motion for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order modifying appellant's probation. The court held that challenges to improper enhancement of the terms of probation could be raised in a motion for postconviction relief; and there was no proof of a violation under the original probation order.

VIVEROS v. STATE


CASE NOS. 96-0861, and 96-1294


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


699 So. 2d 822; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11146; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2303



October 1, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; John G. Ferris, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 92-21833 CFC, 92-24200 CFC, 93-1560 CF, 93-1579 CF, 93-3678 CF, and 94-14967 CF.



DISPOSITION: Reversed appellant's conviction for armed burglary with a firearm in case number 96-1294 and remand for a new trial. Affirmed conviction for aggravated assault with a firearm. In case number 96-0861, reversed appellant's conviction on count V in case number 92-24200, thereby mooting the subsequent revocation of probation and resulting prison sentence on this count. Affirmed as to other probation revocations.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for the 17th Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which convicted him for armed burglary with a firearm, aggravated assault with a firearm, and revoked his probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried for attempted second-degree murder with a firearm, armed burglary with a firearm, shooting into an occupied building, and carrying a concealed firearm. He was convicted of the lesser offense of aggravated assault with a firearm, armed burglary with a firearm, and shooting into an occupied building. He was acquitted on the second attempted murder charge and on carrying a concealed firearm. Appellant was sentenced to concurrent violent habitual offender sentences, and his probation was revoked. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case. Appellant's conviction for armed burglary with a firearm was reversed because the jury instruction relied on a circular definition of burglary. The court affirmed the aggravated assault conviction as a lesser-included offense, as there was sufficient evidence to support a conviction on the greater offense of attempted second-degree murder with a firearm. The court found that appellant's seven year probation sentence was improperly imposed, as he was not charged with the underlying offense, but the court affirmed revocation of appellant's probation with respect to other offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case. The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated assault and revocation of probation. It remanded for a new trial on armed burglary, as the offense was improperly described in a jury instruction.

State v. Sobieck


CASE NO. 96-875


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 96; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10873; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2257



September 26, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1997. Released for Publication November 26, 1997. Petition for Review Denied February 27, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Fla. LEXIS 455.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Cynthia K. Mackinnon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of orders from the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which dismissed nine counts of an amended criminal information filed against appellee, holding that an earlier proceeding in a civil suit constituted a prior penalty and thus barred prosecution of the criminal counts because they were premised on the same conduct involved in the civil case.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with one violation of Florida' RICO statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 895.03(3), 895.0202(3), 895(4) (1995), based on six predicate incidents involving resale of tickets in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 817.36(2)(a). The trial court found that § 817.36 was constitutional, and dismissed nine counts of the criminal information on double jeopardy grounds. On review, the court found statutes like § 817.36 were designed to prevent unfair cornering of the market and limit opportunities to manipulate prices; therefore, this was legitimate area in which the state could impose economic regulations. Further, the court found that appellee had been punished in a prior civil forfeiture proceedings based on the RICO statute. However, that forfeiture proceeding did not impose punishment in the sense of implicating the double jeopardy clause. Rather, such forfeiture proceedings were viewed as independent of any factually related criminal action. Accordingly, the trial court's orders, which dismissed nine counts of the information, were reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The orders, which dismissed nine counts of an amended criminal information filed against appellee, were reversed and remanded because appellee's prior civil forfeiture proceeding did not impose punishment in the way that implicated the double jeopardy clause.

Fletcher v. State


CASE NO. 96-3075


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


699 So. 2d 346; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10844; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2264



September 26, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hernando County, John W. Springstead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their designation as sexual predators under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (Supp. 1996), entered in the Circuit Court for Hernando County (Florida), asserting that the statute was an unconstitutional ex post facto law and that the trial court had no jurisdiction to label them as sexual predators because the declaration modified their sentences more the 60 days after imposition in violation of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800.


OVERVIEW: Appellants had been separately convicted of various sex offenses prior to the enactment of the Florida Sexual Predators Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (Supp. 1996). Subsequent to enactment, the state successfully invoked the provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21(4)(a)(2) to have the appellants classified as sexual predators. The appellants sought review, asserting that ch. 775.21 violated the constitutional prohibition against the enactment of ex post facto laws and that the trial court had no jurisdiction to label them as sexual predators because the declaration modified their sentences more the 60 days after imposition in violation of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800. The reviewing court affirmed, holding that the statute violated neither the ex post facto clause nor Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800 because the designation was neither a sentence nor a punishment but merely a status resulting from their convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' designation as sexual predators, holding that the statute was not a violation of the ex post facto clause or the rules of criminal procedure because the designation sexual predator was neither a sentence nor a punishment but simply a status resulting from the conviction of certain crimes.

Raulerson v. State


CASE NO. 97-710


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


699 So. 2d 339; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10865; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2267



September 26, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Carven D. Angel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his judgment and sentence from the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida) for felony driving while license suspended, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(1) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving while his license was suspended, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34 (1995). The state prosecuted the offense as a felony because defendant had three prior convictions for the same offense. Defendant moved to dismiss the charge, contending that ch. 322.34(1) was unconstitutional because it allowed the trial court to determine whether the offense was a misdemeanor or felony. The trial court denied his motion. Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere, and trial court adjudicated him as guilty of the felony offense. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, concluding the statute was constitutional. The dispositive issue was whether defendant's violation of ch. 322.34(1) was a conviction when the sentencing court decided to withhold an adjudication of guilt instead of entering a judgment against defendant. The court determined it was, therefore defendant's argument failed because all his prior violations of the statute counted in determining whether the violation was a felony. One may be convicted without being adjudicated guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment and sentence for felony driving while license suspended because the challenged statute was constitutional.

Von Eiff v. Azicri


CASE NO. 96-3273


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


699 So. 2d 772; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10595; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2176



September 17, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Bernard S. Shapiro, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 94-27837.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father and mother appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which granted visitation rights to appellees, the maternal grandparents of appellant husband's biological daughter.


OVERVIEW: The judgment of the lower court granting visitation rights to appellee maternal grandparents was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded upon the appeal of the judgment by appellants, the biological father and the adoptive mother of the child at issue. On appeal, the court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(a) (1995) satisfied the requirements of the Fla. Const. The court found that allowing limited visitation to grandparents after a parent has died promoted a compelling state interest in protecting the emotional well being of children. The court further found that appellees were entitled to visitation pursuant to the above statute but that the scope of the visitation order was overly broad. The court found that allowing appellees to take an active role in the child's religious education overstepped the bounds of the court's discretion. Thus, the court affirmed the lower court's order permitting visitation by appellees because it was in the child's best interests. However, the court reversed and remanded the case to the lower court for reconsideration of the extent and scope of what constituted reasonable visitation under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court granting visitation rights to appellee maternal grandparents was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded to the lower court. The appellate court found that visitation by appellees was in the best interests of the child. However, the appellate court concluded that the lower court's original visitation order was overly broad.

 

719 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Irizarry


CASE NO. 96-3234


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


698 So. 2d 912; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10015; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2075



September 3, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the County Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Susan Lubitz, Judge; L.T. Case No. 9620674TCA02.



DISPOSITION: Question as involving a matter of great public importance certified by the county court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecution sought review of a non-final order of the County Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida) denying appellant's motion in limine to introduce into evidence results of appellee's breath test at appellee's criminal trial for driving under the influence of alcohol. Appellant asserted that the breath test results were admissible, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1934(5) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was arrested and charged with driving under the influence of alcohol. Appellant prosecution filed a motion in limine to introduce into evidence a breath test result affidavit prepared pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1934(5) (1995). Appellant's motion was denied, and appellant sought review of the non-final order. The court reversed judgment and granted appellant's motion in limine to introduce a breath test result affidavit, because a breath test result affidavit was admissible in evidence without further proof of maintenance of the intoxilyzer as an exception to the hearsay rule for public records and reports, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1934(5). The court held that in implementing Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1934(5), the Department of Law Enforcement promulgated administrative rules under Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 11D-8.005 and 11D.8.006, requiring an annual inspection of breath test instruments for accuracy and alcohol-free reading, monthly inspection, and a breath test log of every breath test, maintained monthly by a technician.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of appellant prosecution and granted appellant's motion in limine to introduce a breath test result affidavit into evidence at appellee's criminal trial for driving under the influence of alcohol, because a breath test result affidavit was admissible in evidence without further proof of maintenance of the intoxilyzer as an exception to the hearsay rule for public records and reports.

Miller v. State


CASE NO. 96-4247


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 586; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 9030; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1960



August 7, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication August 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. L. Ralph Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant challenged his conviction and sentence in the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), asserting that a good-faith argument could be made that reversible error occurred below. The prosecution moved to dismiss under Fla. Stat. ch. 924.051.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant initially entered a plea of no contest to a charge of escape in exchange for a negotiated guidelines sentence and did not preserve any issues for appeal. Defendant subsequently filed an Anders brief asserting that a good-faith argument could be made that reversible error occurred below. The prosecution then moved to dismiss under Fla. Stat. ch. 924.051. On appeal, the court dismissed criminal defendant's action, holding that a review of the record failed to disclose reversible error. The court held that it had a duty not to grant the prosecutions motion under chapter 924.051 and to review the record to determine if any of the four Robinson error issues existed. However, a review of the record did not disclose error.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed criminal defendant's appeal, holding that a review of the record failed to disclose reversible error and that the appellant had failed to preserve any issues for appeal.

 

722 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Coastal Petroleum v. Chiles


CASE NO. 96-3035


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 619; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8821; 138 Oil & Gas Rep. 293; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 2548



November 5, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected on Grant of Rehearing and Denial of Certification November 5, 1997. Released for Publication November 21, 1997. Certiorari Denied June 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4300.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Philip Padovano, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petroleum corporation challenged the final judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), that granted appellee state boards summary judgment in appellant's action for relief pursuant to inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant petroleum corporation had an option for leases of certain state-owned land off the coast of Florida. Appellant and the state entered into an agreement in which appellant retained only the most offshore portion of the original area to which the leases pertained and retained residual royalty interest in near shore portions until 2016. The settlement required appellant to continue to pay rents on areas where it retained an active interest, to comply with environmental regulations in effect at the time of drilling, to release all interests to the state in the year 2016, and to not interfere in any state land use decisions. The state legislature passed Fla. Stat. ch. 377.242 (1990), prohibiting further oil exploration and leases in the near shore area. Appellant filed an action in which it sought compensation for the alleged taking of its royalty interests. The court affirmed the trial court and held that appellant's interest in the properties was too speculative to be protected through the means of inverse condemnation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court in determining that because appellant petroleum corporation had no reasonable expectation that the state would lease certain lands and could not force the state to lease the lands, legislation prohibiting further exploration and drilling did not constitute inverse condemnation.

 

723 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


F.Y.I. Adventures v. City of Ocala


CASE NO. 96-697


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


698 So. 2d 583; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8819; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1875



August 1, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1997. Released for Publication September 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Carven D. Angel, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on grant of rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of January 10, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 104.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida) that granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment in appellant's declaratory judgment action that challenged the city ordinance that regulated bingo in the city limits because it conflicted with Fla. Stat. ch. 849.0931.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation leased real property and then subleased the premises for a fixed rental amount to charitable organizations for the conduct and play of bingo games. Appellant filed a declaratory judgment action against appellee city and challenged the ordinance that regulated the play and conduct of bingo games in the city limits because it conflicted with Fla. Stat. ch. 849.0931 and on various constitutional grounds. The circuit court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that although the ordinance went further than the statute in the regulation of bingo, the ordinance did not conflict with the statute. There were no provisions in the statute that indicated the legislature intended that bingo be uniform across the state. Thus, the court found that the constitutional challenges to the ordinance were without merit and the ordinance was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the circuit court that granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment in appellant corporation's declaratory judgment action that challenged the city ordinance, holding that the city ordinance was not in conflict with state law. Although the ordinance placed greater regulations on bingo, it was not in conflict with the state law nor was the ordinance unconstitutional.

Florida Dep't of Revenue v. Hardy


CASE NO. 96-2983


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 954; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8807; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1879



August 1, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Non-Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Linda A. Gloeckner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED; CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the department of revenue and various other agencies and officers, sought review of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which denied their motion to transfer venue in appellees' class action suit seeking, inter alia, a refund of fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed a class action suit against appellants, the department of revenue and other various state agencies and officers, seeking to have Fla. Stat. ch. 328.03(7) (1995) declared unconstitutional and further seeking a refund of fees they paid pursuant to that chapter. The trial court denied appellants' motion to dismiss the complaint and their alternative motion to transfer venue. On appeal, the court reversed and held the trial court abused its discretion by denying appellants' motion to transfer and the sword wielder exception was inapplicable because appellant department of revenue issued no notice or warrant to appellees and thus no official action had been taken on the part of appellants other than the filing of motions in response to appellees' suit. Thus, the court vacated the order denying the change of venue, remanded to the lower court with instructions to transfer the cause to the another circuit court pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.060(b).


OUTCOME: The court held the trial court abused its discretion by denying a motion to transfer venue filed by appellants, the department of revenue and various other agencies and officers, because the sword wielder exception was inapplicable to the facts of the case. The court vacated the order denying change of venue and remanded with instructions to transfer the cause to another circuit.

St. Mary's Hosp. v. Phillipe


CASE NOS. 96-2321, 96-2971 and 96-3320


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


699 So. 2d 1017; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8584; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1853



July 30, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing and Rehearing En Banc Denied October 22, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 11887. Released for Publication October 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the State of Florida, Division of Administrative Hearings;. L.T. Case No. 95-5118MA and from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward H. Fine, L.T. Case No. 96-6343 AI.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, hospital and health services corporation, challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which held that defendants were not entitled to a stay before enforcement of an arbitration award for plaintiffs, family members of deceased, for medical malpractice, and that the arbitrator did not err in awarding each plaintiff an award rather than as a class.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, family members of a deceased, sued defendants, hospital and health services corporation, for committing malpractice when the deceased gave birth. Both parties elected to arbitrate, and the arbitrator awarded each plaintiff an award for economic and non-economic damages, attorneys fees, and ordered that payment be made equally over 10 years. Defendants sought a stay of the award during their appeal, and a trial judge refused, and upheld the award. Defendants challenged the ruling, arguing that the arbitrator could only make one award to the entire class of plaintiffs, rather than to each plaintiff, and that economic damages were not permitted. The court held that defendants were not entitled to a stay while they appealed, because the purpose of arbitration was to pay in a quick manner. The court also determined that the arbitrator overstepped his bounds when he awarded each plaintiff an award for malpractice, rather than give one award to the entire class. The court upheld the award of non-economic damages, attorneys fees, and payment over 10 years, stating that the arbitrator's decision complied with the law on these issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed in part the decision of the lower court and held that plaintiffs as a class were entitled to only one award for medical malpractice, but that plaintiffs were entitled to non-economic damages, attorneys fees, and payment over a 10 year period. The court also concluded that defendants were not entitled to a stay before plaintiffs could enforce the arbitration award.

Community Blood Ctrs. v. Damiano


CASE NO. 96-3642


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 948; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 9004; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1858



July 30, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 16, 1997. Released for Publication September 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court of the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; John T. Luzzo, Judge; L.T. Case No. 92-17513 (07).



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner blood bank requested a writ of certiorari following an order of the trial court (Florida), which denied petitioner's motion to dismiss a malpractice complaint brought by respondents, a patient and her family.


OVERVIEW: Respondent patient received a blood transfusion after giving birth to twins. Respondent patient was later diagnosed with AIDS. The malpractice complaint filed by respondents, patient and her family, named the obstetrician and petitioner blood bank as defendants. Several years after respondents had filed their lawsuit, petitioner filed a motion to dismiss the complaint based on respondents' noncompliance with Fla. Stat. ch. 766.106, the medical malpractice presuit requirements. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss. Petitioner argued that although the medical malpractice statute of limitations did not apply to actions against blood banks, respondents nevertheless were bound to comply with the presuit requirements. The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of certiorari because, without a clear expression of legislative intent to the contrary, the court interpreted the applicable statutes as excluding blood banks from the malpractice presuit requirements in actions against them as suppliers of contaminated blood, where they had not rendered any treatment or care.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner blood bank's request for a writ of certiorari because petitioner was not a health care provider for the purpose of requiring respondents, patient and her family, to comply with the medical malpractice presuit requirements. Therefore, the trial court correctly denied petitioner's motion to dismiss.

 

727 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Department of Labor & Employment Sec. v. Lindquist


Consolidated Case No. 97-01091, Case No. 97-01071


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


698 So. 2d 299; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8389; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1784



July 23, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 27, 1997. Released for Publication September 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from nonfinal orders of the Circuit Court for Lee County; Lynn Gerald, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state agency, in two consolidated cases, sought review of the orders from the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida) that denied its motion to change the venue to its home county on the complaints of appellees, commercial fishermen who gave their nets to appellant in exchange for a promise for certain sum of money pursuant to the buy back program of Fla. Stat. ch. 370.0805 (1995), but received less than the promised amount.


OVERVIEW: Appellees in two consolidated cases were commercial fishermen who were subject to Fla. Const. art. X, §§ 16(a) and 16(b)(1)-(2), which limited the type of nets that could be used in fishing. Therefore, pursuant to the net buy-back program of Fla. Stat. ch. 370.0805 (1995), appellees met with employees of appellant, a state agency, in appellees' county and agreed to sell appellant their nets for a specified sum. Appellant took the nets, but sent vouchers for lesser amount. Appellees sued appellant in their county, and the trial court denied appellant's motion to have the cases transferred to appellant's home county. On appeal, the court held that appellant's right to have the cases heard in its county was limited by the sword wielder doctrine. Because ch. 370.0805 (1995) indicated that the nets remained appellees' property until appellant paid for them, appellees' property rights in the nets were protected by Fla. Const. art. I, § 9. Because appellant went to appellees' county to take the nets, and because the complaint alleged that appellant violated their constitutional right to their property, the sword wielder doctrine applied. Therefore, the court affirmed the orders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders denying appellant state agency's motion to change the venue of appellee fishermen's consolidated cases to appellant's home county, because the allegations that appellant went to appellees' county, took their nets pursuant to a statute, then broke its promise to pay an agreed upon amount, thus violating appellees' constitutional rights to their property, made the sword wielder doctrine applicable.

Shapiro v. State


CASE NO. 96-0141


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


696 So. 2d 1321; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8402; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1772



July 23, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 15, 1997. Review Denied October 30, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1887.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; James I. Cohn, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-9688 CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant psychotherapist sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), that convicted him of sexual misconduct by a psychotherapist, a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 491.0112 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant psychotherapist was charged under Fla. Stat. ch. 491.0112(4)(b) (1993), which prohibited sexual misconduct by means of a therapeutic deception, which was defined to mean a representation to the client that sexual contact by the psychotherapist was consistent with or part of the client's treatment. The lower court convicted appellant, and he sought review. The court found the trial court properly denied appellant's motion for judgment of acquittal because the evidence demonstrated a prima facie case that appellant used therapeutic deception to convince the female victim to engage in sexual conduct. The court found testimony from a former patient was properly admitted into testimony as a prior act. Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(a) allowed evidence of other crimes, wrongs, or acts to be admissible when it was relevant to prove a material fact in issue, such as proof of motive, opportunity, or intent. Because the testimony from the former patient was admitted to prove a common scheme, it was relevant. The court found Fla. Stat. ch. 491.0112 (1993) was not overbroad because there was not an absolute fundamental constitutional right to engage in any type of sexual behavior.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that convicted appellant of sexual misconduct by a psychotherapist was affirmed because the evidence demonstrated a prima facie case that appellant used therapeutic deception to convince the female victim to engage in sexual conduct. The testimony of a former patient was properly admitted into evidence to prove appellant's intent.
