St. John Medical Plans v. Gutman


CASE NO. 96-1800


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


696 So. 2d 1294; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8161; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1717



July 16, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Robbie M. Barr, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-22930.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, medical center, medical plan, and individual, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) that dismissed in part appellants' complaint that alleged appellee senator misused his position as a state senator when he received an inappropriate fee, and breached public trust.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, medical center, medical plan, and individual, filed suit against appellee senator. The suit alleged appellee misused his position as a state senator when he received an inappropriate fee, and breached public trust. Appellants filed suit, asserting that they had standing based on Fla. Const. art. II, § 8(c). The court found appellants did not have standing based on Fla. Const. art. II, § 8(c), because it was not self-executing and it could not have been implemented without some manner of recovery being established by legislative enactment. The court noted that Fla. Const. art. II, § 8(c), provided standing in the state of Florida, not individual citizens. The court found that appellants did not have standing under Fla. Stat. ch. 112.3175 (1995) because appellants admitted they had no special injury, therefore, they did not have standing under that section. The court certified a question to the state supreme court to determine whether Fla. Const. art. II, § 8(c), by itself without legislative enactment gave an individual citizen standing.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that dismissed appellants' complaint that alleged appellee senator misused his position as a state senator when he received an inappropriate fee and breached public trust was affirmed because appellants did not have standing.

 

730 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Avatar Dev. Corp.


CASE NO. 96-1639


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 561; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8166; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1740



July 16, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1997. Released for Publication August 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert F. Diaz, Judge; L.T. Case No. 9528814MM10A&B.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant state appealed from an order of the County Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) that dismissed the criminal misdemeanor filed against appellee corporation and appellee vice president and based upon the purported noncompliance with permits issued by the Department of Environmental Protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation and vice president obtained a permit to conduct a dredge and fill operation. Appellee was required to notify the state before commencement of the work and place safety measures into effect before the work. Appellees failed to comply with the requirements. Appellant prosecutor charged appellees with two misdemeanor violations of Fla. Stat. ch. 403.161(1)(b) (1995). The trial court dismissed the information and found Fla. Stat. ch. 403.161(1)(b) (1995) was unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded because in order for the court to declare a legislative delegation of power invalid, the court was required to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the duty conferred was a power that was exclusively legislative. The authority to make administrative rules was not a delegation of legislative power, nor were such rules raised from an administrative to a legislative character because the violation was a public offense. The court found that the state administrative agency was subject to express legislative control and guidance. Fla. Stat. ch. 403.161(1)(b) (1995) was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to an administrative agency.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court was reversed because the legislature did not unconstitutionally delegate legislative authority to a state agency. The agency was subject to express legislative control and guidance, and it was the state's public policy to preserve and protect the water.

 

731 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. R.R.


CASE NO. 96-1445


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 181; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 8151; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1719



July 16, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a non-final order of the Circuit Court for Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-9353.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecutor appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) that granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Based on a tip, two officers conducted surveillance of an abandoned house. They approached defendant, who was sitting on the porch. When the officers approached defendant, he dropped two clear plastic bags that contained drugs. Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance. Defendant filed a motion to suppress, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant pled no contest to the charge. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing on the motion to suppress, and the lower court suppressed the evidence. The court reversed because the police officer's encounter with defendant was consensual, because a reasonable person would have felt free to disregard the police and go about their business. A consensual encounter did not require the police to have a reasonable suspicion of any improper conduct before conversation was initiated. The court reversed because the presence of the police officers on the porch where defendant was sitting was no different than a consensual encounter and the police did not even have time to speak before defendant voluntarily dropped the bags of drugs. Because there was no coercion, the court improperly granted defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence was reversed because the presence of the police officers on the porch where defendant was sitting was no different than a consensual encounter and the police did not even have time to speak before defendant voluntarily dropped the bags of drugs.

 

732 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


Case No. 95-02169


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


698 So. 2d 555; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 7870; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1711



July 11, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Brandt C. Downey, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which convicted him of robbery with a deadly weapon, attempted robbery with a deadly weapon, trespass with a dangerous weapon, aggravated battery with a deadly weapon, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon and simple assault, based, in part, on proof that defendant used a BB pistol during all of the offenses.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court determined that the evidence was sufficient to support criminal defendant's convictions. The appellate court held that it was proper for the jury to find that the BB pistol was a dangerous or deadly weapon where defendant's words and actions implied that the device was dangerous or deadly, irrespective of the fact that the device was not normally dangerous or deadly when used in its ordinary and usual manner and was not, at the time of the offenses, not dangerous or deadly due to its unloaded condition, which could not have been observed by the victims. The appellate court noted that various witnesses had testified that they thought that the BB pistol was a real firearm and that defendant had carried and used the weapon as if it were loaded and had himself referred to the BB pistol as a "weapon" or "gun." The appellate court upheld the limited reliance upon a reasonable victim's perspective regarding the likelihood of injury and affirmed, noting that nothing visible to any victim in the case would have led a rational person to concluded that the BB pistol was not a loaded and operable, deadly or dangerous weapon.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the criminal convictions, finding that it was appropriate for the jury to have found that the BB pistol used by criminal defendant during all of the charged offenses was a dangerous or deadly weapon where defendant's actions and words implied that the device was a dangerous or deadly weapon, and a reasonable victim's perspective indicated a likelihood of injury resulting from defendant's proposed use of the device.

House v. State


CASE NO. 97-1024


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


696 So. 2d 515; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 7733; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1689



July 8, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of order denying rule 3.850 motion from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Barry E. Goldstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 92-16097CF.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, sentenced as an habitual offender after originally having been sentenced to community control with a consecutive term of probation, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which denied his application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant originally pled nolo contendere to the charge of issuing a worthless check, a third-degree felony. Defendant received a guidelines sentence, within the statutory maximum, followed by a term of probation. Defendant subsequently violated his community control, and the trial court revoked his community control and imposed a habitual offender sentence of imprisonment. Defendant did not directly appeal this sentence, but after the time for appeal lapsed he brought a collateral attack, arguing that the habitual offender sentence, imposed after revocation of his community control, was both unauthorized and illegal pursuant to precedent. The trial court denied collateral relief. On appeal, a state appellate court reversed. The court opined that the precedent cited by defendant, under which habitual offender sentences were prohibited in the situation faced by defendant, was retroactively applicable. Accordingly, defendant's sentence was vacated pursuant to that precedent.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order denying defendant's application for post-conviction relief was reversed. The court's precedent, retroactively applicable to defendant's case, held that offenders in defendant's situation could not be subjected to the habitual offender sentencing statute.

 

734 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cohen


CASE NO. 96-2085


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


696 So. 2d 435; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 7512; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1622



July 2, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; John E. Fennelly, Judge; L.T. Case No. 95-370 CFA.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), which dismissed the three counts of the information against criminal defendant that alleged his violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(5) (1995) for possessing pornographic computer images of an actual child.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court reversed the trial court's decision to dismiss the counts of the indictment that charged criminal defendant with violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(5) (1995) for his possession of pornographic images of an actual child. The appellate court determined that a computer image constituted a "representation or other presentation" under the statute, noting that the pornographic images also could qualify under Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(5) as copies of photographs. The appellate court then found that under the doctrine of ejusdem generis, the term "representation or other presentation" included computer images as items that were similar in nature to a photograph or motion picture, noting that the trial court's usage of qualifying terms that were not found in the statutory language served to rewrite the law and to limit its terms in a manner contrary to its plain language. The appellate court concluded by holding that there was no inherent conflict between Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(5) and Fla. Stat. ch. 827.0135, as the trial court had determined, given that a review of the two statutes indicated that each contained an element not present in the other.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the dismissal of the counts of the information that had arisen from the state criminal statute which had prohibited possession of a photograph, representation, or other representation of a photographic image of an actual child, holding that possession of a pornographic computer image of an actual child constituted an offense under the law and remanding with directions to reinstate the dismissed counts.

 

735 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Vazquez v. State


CASE NO. 96-0072


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


700 So. 2d 5; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 7502; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1630



July 2, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing, Clarification and Rehearing En Banc Denied and Question Certified September 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 10712. Released for Publication October 24, 1997. Rehearing Opinion of September 24, 1997, Reported at: 700 So. 2d 5 at 14.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Carole Y. Taylor, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-21177CF10A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which convicted defendant for trafficking in cocaine. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in excluding certain evidence, and erred in its instruction to the jury on the defense of entrapment.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed defendant's conviction for trafficking in cocaine, because the court found that the lower court erred in refusing to reopen cross-examination of the prosecution's key witness. The court found that the lower court should have allowed defendant to reopen cross-examination of appellee's lead detective for the purpose of introducing into evidence additional tape recordings of conversations between defendant and appellee's informant. The court found that it was fatal error for the lower court to deny defense counsel the right of cross-examination for the purpose of laying a predicate for impeachment. Further, the court held that, because appellee had introduced a portion of the tape recorded conversations, defendant should have been allowed to introduce other relevant portions, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 90.108 (1995). In respect to the lower court's instruction regarding entrapment, the court held that the lower court should have used the most current jury instruction available and advised the court to do so on remand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for trafficking in cocaine. The court found that the lower court should have allowed defendant to reopen cross-examination of appellee's lead detective for the purpose of introducing into evidence additional tape recordings of conversations between defendant and appellee's informant, and that the lower court's failure to do so was reversible error. Defendant was granted a new trial.

Smith v. Board of Regents ex rel. Florida A&M Univ.


CASE NO. 96-2244


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


701 So. 2d 348; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 7203; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1573



June 25, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Re-released for Publication December 2, 1997. Clarification Granted December 15, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 13998.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Charles D. McClure, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant professor sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which dismissed the counts of his complaint alleging civil theft and negligence against appellees, state board of regents, bank, and state comptroller.


OVERVIEW: Appellant professor had received authorization from his employer for paid annual leave. The paycheck for this annual leave was deposited into his bank account and then withdrawn without his permission from that same account. Appellant brought a cause of action claiming civil theft and negligence against appellees, state board of regents, bank, state comptroller, and university president. The trial court dismissed the claims against appellees, state board of regents, bank, and state comptroller. The appellate court affirmed, holding that appellant failed to allege facts that appellees, state board of regents, bank, and state comptroller, harbored evil intent as to their actions or that they had knowledge that appellant was entitled to the payment of annual leave. Furthermore, appellees, state board of regents and state comptroller, were immune from the action because of sovereign immunity. The court also ruled that the negligence action against appellees, state board of regents and bank, was precluded by the economic loss rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint against appellees, state board of regents, bank, and state comptroller. The court found that appellant professor's claims of civil theft and negligence for the withdrawal of his annual leave pay from his bank account did not allege facts to sustain the cause of action against appellees, and that appellant's claims were precluded by sovereign immunity and the economic loss rule.

 

738 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. State


CASE NO. 96-266, CASE NO. 96-1502


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


698 So. 2d 551; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 6557; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1498



June 17, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Peter J. Fryefield, Judge; and

An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Nancy Gilliam, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), which denied his motion to correct his sentence brought under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of aggravated assault that arose from a single criminal episode. Appellant was sentenced to ten years imprisonment on count one and six years on count two. Appellant moved the court to correct his sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a), and contended that the sentence was illegal because the maximum allowed for aggravated assault was ten years imprisonment. The court denied appellant's motion because the sentence did not exceed the statutory maximum and was thus, not illegal under rule 3.800(a). On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. A sentence was not illegal within the meaning of rule 3.800(a), if it did not exceed the maximum period allowed by law. A single sentence for aggravated assault could not exceed ten years and neither of appellant's single sentences exceeded ten years. Appellant's sentence was not illegal, so he was not entitle to relief under rule 3.800(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying appellant's motion. Appellant was not entitled to post-conviction relief because his sentence was not illegal. Appellant's sentence did not exceed the maximum provided by law because it did not exceed the ten years maximum allowed for aggravated assault.

 

739 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Communications Workers, Local 3170 v. City of Gainesville


CASE NO. 96-1878


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 167; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 6562; 157 L.R.R.M. 2243; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1493



June 17, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1997. Released for Publication August 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Public Employees Relations Commission.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order of the Public Employees Relations Commission (Florida), which dismissed appellant's action against appellee on the grounds that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the unfair labor charges because it would have to decide whether appellee violated state and federal constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellee voted to accept a drug-testing program, including proposals concerning random drug testing, notice or no notice and immediate dismissals. Appellant filed unfair labor practice charges against appellee, alleging appellee breached its duty to bargain in good faith in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 447.501(1)(a), (c) and claimed appellee infringed on certain of employees' state and federal constitutional rights. The court reversed and remanded the commission's decision to dismiss appellant's case for lack of jurisdiction. The commission had the jurisdiction, authority, and responsibility to decide the merits of appellant's unfair labor practice charges. Consideration of appellant's unfair labor practice charges did not require the commission to adjudicate the constitutionality of any statute or rule. The commission was not free to ignore statutory and constitutional rights simply because it would have to consider statutes and issues beyond its expertise. The commission's clear authority to decide unfair labor practices occurred did not disappear when it was required to consider constitutional dictates on order to make that determination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the commission's decision to dismiss appellants' action against appellee, and held that the commission did have jurisdiction to hear appellants' unfair labor charges. The commission's authority to decide unfair labor practices did not vanish when it was required to consider whether constitutional rights were violated in order to make that determination.

Monroe County v. Garcia


CASE NO. 96-2787


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


695 So. 2d 823; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 6254; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1427



June 11, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Wayne Miller, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 93-239.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted, order quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought review, by way of certiorari, of an order of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Florida) that granted respondent attorney's motion for fees in excess of the limitation on attorney fees for court-appointed counsel set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036(2)(c).


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney was appointed to represent an indigent defendant individual in a sexual battery case. OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner county's request for a writ of certiorari, quashed the order that granted respondent attorney's motion, and remanded for an evidentiary hearing because there was no support in the record for the finding that an award of attorney fees to respondent in excess of the statutory cap was warranted.

M.C. v. State


CASE NO. 96-1986


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


695 So. 2d 477; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 6256; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1429



June 11, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 27, 1997. Review Denied October 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1819.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 96-2965.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a delinquency adjudication in the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), that found her guilty of violating Fla. Stat. ch. 877.13 (1995), which makes it unlawful for anyone to knowingly disrupt the lawful functions of an educational facility. Appellant challenged the statute as violative of U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: After her brother's arrest at school, appellant juvenile, along with several other students, stormed into the main office yelling obscenities at the arresting officer. Appellant waved her arms in a threatening manner as if to incite the other students and went to an area off limits to students. The office functions were temporarily halted by appellant's conduct. Appellant was charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 877.13(1995), which makes it unlawful for anyone to knowingly disrupt or interfere with the lawful administration or functions of an educational institution. Appellant was found guilty and challenged the statute as facially unconstitutional. The court affirmed appellant's delinquency order. The court held that ch. 877.13 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I because only conduct that materially disrupted normal school functions was proscribed. The court found that the statute was not overly broad because the prohibited disturbances were easily measured by their impact on school activities. The court held that ch. 877.13 was not vague because the plain meaning of the statute prohibited acts that were intended to stop normal school functions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant juvenile's delinquency order for violating a statute that made it unlawful to knowingly disrupt or interfere with the lawful administration or functions of an educational institution. The court upheld the statute's constitutionality because it was not overly broad or vague in violation of the First Amendment, as its intended purpose was to prevent only activity that materially disrupted school functions.

 

743 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Monroe County v. Whispering Pines Assocs.


CASE NO. 96-1435


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


697 So. 2d 873; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 6271; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1434



June 11, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 20, 1997. Released for Publication August 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Richard G. Payne, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 94-10083.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, and remanded with instructions. Trial court's order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Florida) which reversed appellant's determination of a code violation and the imposed fine against appellee mobile home park, who cross-appealed on the basis that appellant was not authorize to hold appellee liable for a past landowner's code violation, and because the law did not authorize such liability, the imposed fine was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment that appellee mobile home park violated code requirements, but reversed the judgment which reversed appellant board's determination of appellee's code violation and imposed fines against appellee. One of the lots in appellee's park was not zoned to permit placement of mobile homes on the lot. For several years prior to appellee owning the park, the park was in violation of zoning codes because mobile homes had been placed on the lot, and such practice continued after ownership of the park transferred to appellee. The court held that under Fla. Stat. ch. 162.09 (1995), code violations run with and the land, and therefore, appellee, as a subsequent purchaser of the park, could be held responsible for bringing the property up to code. The court held that 162.09 was not unconstitutional by requiring the party who has the power to bring the land into code compliance to do so. The court found that a hearing was held pursuant to 162.09, and appellee was given time to obtain the necessary permit or variance, and where appellee failed to do so, it was properly fined each day for its noncompliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that appellee mobile home park violated the code, but reversed the judgment which reversed appellant board's determination of appellee's code violation and which imposed fines, because code violations run with the land under the law, and appellee, a subsequent purchaser of the park, could be held responsible for bringing the property up to code, and appellee could be fined where it failed to do so.

State v. Ellis


CASE NO. 96-3143O


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


722 So. 2d 824; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 5612; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1298



May 22, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Certiorari - Original Jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, seeking review of the determination of the trial court (Florida) that Fla. Stat. ch. 837.011(3) was unconstitutional in describing the issue of materiality in a perjury prosecution as a "question of law" so as to remove the issue from the jury.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner state government sought a writ of certiorari to challenge the trial court's determination that Fla. Stat. ch. 837.011(3) unconstitutionally described the issue of materiality in a perjury prosecution as a "question of law," which removed the issue from jury consideration. Respondent was charged with perjury and moved to dismiss the charge on the grounds that she was constitutionally entitled to a jury determination on the issue of materiality. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss the perjury charge but ruled that materiality was an issue to be determined by a jury. In so doing, the trial court struck as unconstitutional the last sentence of the statute, which provided that in perjury prosecutions materiality was a question of law to be determined by the court. The appellate court denied the petition, holding that although Fla. Stat. ch. 837.011(3) provided a definition of materiality in perjury prosecutions and stated that whether a matter was material in a given factual situation was a question of law, the recitation did not remove the issue from the jury. The appellate court held that the lower court correctly determined that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied because state case law had acknowledged that materiality was an element of the crime of perjury, and because materiality was an element of the crime, the lower court correctly determined that petitioner was entitled to have the issue submitted to the jury and correctly determined that the state statute was unconstitutional.

State v. De La Llana


Case No. 96-04260


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


693 So. 2d 1075; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 5389; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1248



May 16, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court for Hillsborough County; Ronald W. Ficarrotta, County Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the order of the County Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), that dismissed the charge against appellee bar manager on the basis that Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(7)(a)(5) (1995), which formed the basis for the charge, was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state charged appellee bar manager with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(7)(a)(5) (1995), which made it unlawful for any person to keep or maintain a place of business where drug use and drug trafficking occurred. In his motion to dismiss, appellee alleged that the statute was impermissibly vague and overbroad because it failed to define the terms "keep or maintain" and individuals of common intelligence would need to guess the meaning of the terms and their application. The trial court granted the motion and found that the statute violated equal protection and resulted in an unconstitutional deprivation of due process. Appellant challenged that ruling. The court held that drug use or trafficking was not a protected conduct for which one was constitutionally entitled to privacy. The court held that "overbroad" and "vague" were not one the same, but were separate and distinct doctrines of constitutional rights. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the plain meaning of the words "keep" or "maintain" was sufficiently clear and contemplated conducting a business enterprise such as that maintained by appellee to put him on notice that he violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which found the statute that forbade "keeping or maintaining" a place of business where drug trafficking occurred unconstitutional, and remanded for further proceedings. The court concluded that the statute was facially constitutional because, even though the terms "keeping and maintaining" were not defined in the statute, the plain meaning of the language was clear.

K.D. v. Department of Juvenile Justice


CASE NO. 96-4051


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


694 So. 2d 817; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 5158; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1214



May 14, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1997. Released for Publication June 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Hubert R. Lindsey, Judge; L.T. Case No. CJ95-7066 JL.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), in which the court entered judgment confining appellant pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.0517(2) to restore her competency.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a juvenile, was charged with possession and exhibition of a firearm on school property. Appellant was subsequently committed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.0517(2) following a hearing to determine her competency to stand trial. On review, appellant challenged the constitutionality of section 39.0517(2) and whether there was sufficient evidence to support the court's order of confinement. The appeals court affirmed the judgment. First, the appeals court held that the statute was constitutional and that the statute did not require the court to appoint a psychiatrist before it could commit appellant. Moreover, the appeals court held that appellant was treated the same as adult incompetent defendants for purposes of determining competency. The appeals court held that the rules pertaining to adult defendants did not require a psychiatrist. The appeals court then held that there was sufficient evidence to support the lower court's order. According to the appeals court, the appellate task on reviewing a trial court's finding based on clear and convincing evidence was not to reweigh the testimony and evidence or to substitute the court's judgment for that of the trier of fact.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment confining appellant to restore her competency because the statute under which appellant was confined was constitutional and because there was sufficient evidence to support the lower court's order.

 

748 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brigham


Case No. 96-01837


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


694 So. 2d 793; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4902; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1174



May 7, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 5, 1997. Released for Publication June 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court for Sarasota County; Preston DeVilbiss, Jr., County Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a nonfinal order from the County Court for Sarasota County (Florida), which granted a motion in limine in four consolidated driving while under the influence cases and suppressed breath alcohol evidence provided by an Intoxilyzer 5000 breath test instrument in order to require the effective the dismissal of all charges against appellee suspects alleging a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(1)(b) (1995).


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court reversed the suppression orders, holding that the phrase "breath alcohol level of 0.08 percent or higher" in Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(1)(b) (1995) was to be interpreted as meaning "grams per 210 liters of breath" instead of the asserted mathematical definition. The appellate court found that practical information about the Intoxilyzer 500 and other breath test instruments indicated that the term "percent" on that equipment referred to the universal 1:2100 ratio of alcohol in human blood to alcohol in that person's breath. The appellate court further noted that once the state legislature had been made aware of the manufacturer's change of the readout of its equipment, in recognition of the confusion surrounding the term "percent," it had updated the statute to replace "percent" with "grams per 210 liters." The appellate court concluded by remanding the consolidated cases for new trials, finding that criminal defendants' erroneous calculations of blood alcohol content, under their interpretation of the statute, were not sustainable because they resulted in an absurd interpretation of the charging statute, which was to be avoided.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision granting the motions in limine to suppress breath alcohol evidence and remanded criminal defendants' driving while under the influence cases for trial, finding that, in order to avoid an absurd interpretation of the charging statute, the phrase "breath alcohol level of 0.08 percent or higher" was to be interpreted to mean "breath alcohol level of 0.08 grams per 210 liters of breath or higher."

Stat. ch. 39.061, which proscribed escape from various juvenile facilities. Appellant specifically argued that the trial court should have dismissed the petition alleging that she had committed a delinquent act because ch. 39.061 did not proscribe escape from low-risk residential commitment facilities as defined by Fla. Stat. ch. 39.061(59)(b). Alternatively, appellant argued, if the statute did proscribe escape from such facilities, its terms were unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's adjudication of appellant as a delinquent child. OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's adjudication of appellant juvenile as a delinquent child after appellant escaped from a low-risk residential commitment facility. The appellate court held that the relevant statute was not so vague as to fail to provide appellant adequate notice that leaving a low-risk residential facility was a delinquent act.

 

751 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Brevard County v. Fla. Power & Light Co.


CASE NO. 96-1666


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


693 So. 2d 77; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4856; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1099



May 2, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 21, 1997. Review Denied September 11, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1651.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, Edward M. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county government challenged a ruling from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which held appellant's ordinance regulating where power companies could place electrical power lines within appellant's jurisdiction invalid, given appellant's contract with appellee power company granting appellee the right to make that decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county government entered into a contractual agreement with appellee power company whereby appellee could provide electrical services in appellant's jurisdiction. The agreement included provisions authorizing appellee to construct transmission lines in appellant's jurisdiction. Thereafter, appellant adopted an ordinance, in response to citizen complaints, giving it the power to regulate where electrical power lines could be placed, notwithstanding the earlier agreement between appellant and appellee permitting appellee to place such power lines where it pleased. A circuit court held that the ordinance was invalid inasmuch as it interfered with appellee's contractual rights. On appeal, a state appellate court affirmed. The court held that controlling precedent required the decision reached by the circuit court, and struck down the ordinance as unreasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment holding invalid appellant county government's ordinance regulating the placement of electrical power lines was affirmed. Appellant's contract with appellee power company was valid, and enforcement of appellant's ordinance would violate appellee's rights under that contract.

State v. Alecia


CASE NO. 96-1752


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


692 So. 2d 263; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4306; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1066



April 25, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 14, 1997. Review Denied September 11, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1649.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, Jere E. Lober, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a ruling from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which declared a portion of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.08 unconstitutional and dismissed a charge of falsely assuming or pretending to be a deputy sheriff.


OVERVIEW: Appellee tried to obtain information about recent suspicious activity in his neighborhood by falsely identifying himself as a deputy sheriff to two of his neighbors. Appellee was charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 843.08 by falsely assuming or pretending to be a deputy sheriff. Appellee moved to declare chapter 843.08 as unconstitutional based on its vagueness and overbreadth and to dismiss the charge against him. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss and appellant state sought review. The court held that chapter 843.08 was not so imprecise as to require individuals to guess at its meaning. The court found that appellee's actions clearly fell within the plain meaning of chapter 843.08 because said chapter prohibited appellee from falsely assuming the persona of a law enforcement officer and acting as such.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the trial court's order declaring the remainder of a statute as constitutional because the statute prohibited appellee from falsely assuming the persona of a law enforcement officer, but reversed in part the trial court's order declaring a portion of said statute unconstitutional because said statute was vague, and remanded the matter.

 

754 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Latham v. Florida Comm'n on Ethics


CASE NO. 96-1224


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


694 So. 2d 83; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4126; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1041



April 23, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 21, 1997. Rehearing Denied May 23, 1997. Released for Publication June 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Commission on Ethics.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public official sought review of an order of the Florida Commission on Ethics, which adopted a hearing officer's findings of fact and conclusion that appellant had violated Fla. Stat. ch. 112.313(6) by engaging in unwanted sexually or romantically oriented behavior toward a subordinate female employee and recommended the imposition of a civil monetary penalty and a public censure and reprimand to remedy appellant's wrongful actions.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court reversed the decision and recommendations from the state ethics commission on the ground that the commission failed to comply with Fla. Stat. ch. 112.317(1)(a) by requiring proof of appellant public official's violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 112.313(6) by clear and convincing evidence before the penalties had been recommended. The appellate court found that the commission had erred in applying the preponderance of evidence standard, noting that the clear and convincing standard was more appropriate because of the penal nature inherent in finding a violation of the state ethics code and because the penalties at stake included the loss of livelihood and professional reputation. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded that the realities of the impact of a state ethics commission proceeding necessitated a reliance on a heightened standard of proof and certified a question of great public importance to the state supreme court regarding the applicability of the clear and convincing standard, noting that the newly adopted burden of proof would impact a potentially large number of cases.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the conclusions and recommendations from the state ethics commission regarding appellant public official's behavior toward a subordinate female employee, finding that a heightened clear and convincing standard of proof should have been applied in light of the penal nature of the commission's proceedings and the reality of the commission's actions resulting in a loss of livelihood.

 

755 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Stevens v. State


CASE NO. 96-2492


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


691 So. 2d 622; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4327; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 1001



April 18, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.850 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County, Mark J. Hill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Question certified to be of great public importance. REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Lake County (Florida) that denied his motion for post-conviction relief from his sentence of life in prison with a mandatory minimum term of 25 years, which was imposed for his conviction for attempted second-degree murder of a law enforcement officer, in accordance with Fla. Stat. chs. 784.07(3), 775.0825 (Supp. 1988).


OVERVIEW: Holding that a change in decisional law that invalidated the imposition of life sentences for the attempted murder of law enforcement officers pursuant to Fla. Stat. chs. 784.07(3), 775.0825 (Supp. 1988), merited retroactive effect, the court reversed the order that denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, and remanded. The court explained that the imposition of life sentences for attempted murder of law enforcement officers had been invalidated because it resulted in greater sentences for attempted murder of officers than for the actual murder of the officers. The court applied a three-part test to determine if that decision had retroactive effect. Because the decision came from the Florida Supreme Court and removed authority from the state to regulate certain conduct or to impose certain penalties, the first and third parts of the test were satisfied. The court found that because the penalty implicated the guarantees of due process and equal protection it was constitutional in nature, which satisfied the second part of the test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, and remanded for resentencing. The court held that a change in decisional law that barred the imposition of life sentences for attempted murder of law enforcement officers was entitled to retroactive effect because it issued from the highest court in the state, was of constitutional dimension, and limited the state's ability to impose a certain criminal penalty.

 

756 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Seminole County v. Coral Gables Fed. S&L Ass'n


CASE NO. 95-3210


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


691 So. 2d 614; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 4345; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 994



April 18, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Seymour Benson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida) that awarded attorney fees to appellee landowner in eminent domain action calculated pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 73.092 (Supp. 1994). Appellant asserted that the chapter, which provided for fees based the difference between final judgment and last offer, was an unconstitutional infringement on the judiciary's power to determine reasonable fees.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed an award of attorney fees to appellee landowner in eminent domain case that was calculated pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch.73.092 (Supp. 1994). That chapter provided that attorney fees should be based on a percentage of the benefit obtained after negotiations and defined benefit as the difference between final judgment and the last written settlement offer. The court rejected appellant county's argument that the statute was unconstitutional because the legislature had infringed on the powers of the judiciary to determine reasonable fees. The court held that when the legislature was silent on the factors it considered important in determining a reasonable fee, courts could look to the criteria enumerated in Fla. Bar R. 4-1.5, but where the legislature specifically set forth the criteria it deemed would result in a reasonable award, only the statutory factors may be considered. The court also rejected appellant's argument that the trial court erred in admitting a settlement offer into evidence in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.408 (Supp.1994) and held that the fee statute prevailed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that awarded fees based on the statute. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that the judiciary could look to criteria to determine a reasonable fee only when the legislature was silent on specific factors or guidance.

Taccariello v. State


CASE NO. 96-1265


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


692 So. 2d 231; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 3942; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 955



April 16, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1997. Released for Publication May 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Virginia Gay Broome, Judge; L.T. Case No. 93-12463CF A02 and 93-8860CF A02.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the sentence imposed by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), after remand from appellant's direct appeal of the conviction and sentence. Appellant contended that the successor trial judge had failed to provide contemporaneous written reasons for the sentence even though the prior trial judge had done so and the successor judge reimposed the original sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court remanded appellant's direct appeal of the conviction and sentence with directions that the trial court dismiss certain charges and resentence appellant on the remaining ones. On remand, the successor trial judge dismissed the appropriate counts and reimposed the original departure sentence without giving oral or written reasons for the departure sentence. Appellant sought review contending that the successor trial judge was required to provide written reasons for the departure even though the prior trial judge had done so upon sentencing appellant the first time and the successor judge indicated an intent to reimpose the original sentence. The court reversed and remanded the action holding that despite the successor judge's expressed intent to impose the original sentence, it was error not to recite or provide written reasons for the departure. The court found it was impossible to determine whether the departure sentence on remand was based on all three of the original reasons, including the invalid reason of premeditation, or whether it was based on only the two remaining, valid reasons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with no possibility of departure from the sentencing guidelines, holding that because of the trial court's failure to provide written reasons for the departure sentence, it was impossible for the court to determine whether the departure sentence on remand was based on all three of the original reasons, including the invalid reason of premeditation, or whether it was based on only the remaining valid reasons.

State v. Duggins


CASE NO. 95-03013


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


691 So. 2d 566; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 3745; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 916



April 11, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Robert Simms, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), which granted appellee's motion to suppress certain evidence seized from him as the result of a pat-down search. Appellee was charged with possession of cannabis in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(6)(a), and obstructing an officer without violence in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.02.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was stopped by a deputy sheriff because he was swerving in and out of the lane in which he was driving. While waiting for a DUI investigator, the deputy started a pat-down search of appellee, but appellee grabbed the deputy's hand and told him to stop. Appellee was then arrested for obstructing an officer without violence, and a search incident to the arrest resulted in the seizure of 31 grams of cannabis. Appellee was charged with possession of cannabis in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(6)(a) and with obstructing an officer without violence in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.02. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the evidence obtained as a result of the pat-down search, and the state filed a timely notice of appeal. The reviewing court reversed the decision of the trial court, stating that appellee was properly stopped, and subsequently arrested, for DUI. The state established that the evidence would have been discovered as a result of a valid search conducted pursuant to appellee's arrest for DUI. Therefore, the evidence should not have been suppressed because of the inevitable discovery rule.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court reversed the decision of the trial court, holding that appellee's motion to suppress the evidence obtained as a result of a pat-down search was granted in error. The state established that the evidence would have been discovered as a result of a valid search conducted pursuant to appellee's arrest for DUI and, therefore, should not have been suppressed.

S.V.E. v. State


CASE NO. 96-2862


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 1283; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 9657; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 799



March 25, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. A.C. Soud, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), which adjudicated appellant delinquent for escaping from a residential commitment facility, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.061 (1995). Appellant claimed the evidence was insufficient to support the lawful custody or escape elements, or that he escaped from a residential treatment facility. Appellant claimed his transfer to another program was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Because statute that authorized child's transfer to residential commitment facility was constitutionally valid, appellant child's delinquency adjudication was properly entered. Appellant was committed to a special intensive group program. Appellant absconded from the program. Appellee state transferred appellant to a moderate-risk residential program, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.021(4) (1995). Appellant was charged with juvenile escape. The trial court adjudicated appellant delinquent for absconding, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 39.061 (1995). Appellant sought review, and claimed there was insufficient evidence to find the elements of lawful custody or escape, or that the facility from which he absconded was a residential commitment facility. Appellant also claimed the transfer statute was facially unconstitutional, because it was a delegation of legislative power to an agency, such delegation violated due process. The reviewing court affirmed, and found that, because appellant failed to preserve the sufficiency of evidence issues, appellate review was precluded. The appellate court also found the constitutionality of the transfer statute issue to be without merit.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's adjudication of appellant child as a delinquent for escaping from a residential commitment facility. The statute that authorized appellant's transfer was facially constitutional, because the statute did not constitute an impermissible delegation of legislative authority to an agency, and the statute did not violate due process.

T.M. v. State


CASE NO. 96-1115


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 443; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 2478; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 706



March 19, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Thomas K. Petersen, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 95-5902.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Juvenile appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida) asserting that Fla. Stat. ch. 790.22(9)(a) (1995), which mandated the imposition of a five day detention period for a juvenile's use or possession of a firearm in any offense, was violative of the equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: Juvenile was convicted of delinquency with carrying a concealed firearm. Pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 790.22(9)(a), the trial court was required to impose a five day detention period in addition to any other penalty permitted by law. Juvenile appealed, claiming the statute violated his rights of equal protection as it did not require the same for adults who were convicted of a crime. The court, in rejecting the argument, held that the juvenile offender and the adult offender were not similarly situated. With adult offenders, the state's primary objective was that of retributive punishment. One of the primary purposes of the Juvenile Justice Act, however, was to ensure the protection of society, by providing punishment and treatment consistent with the specific rehabilitation needs of the child. The court found the statutory classification was rational in light of the escalating numbers of firearms in the hands of juveniles, which the legislature could find posed more of a societal threat by virtue of the juvenile's immaturity.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court did not err in its determination that the statute imposing a mandatory five day detention period of any juvenile who committed an offense using a firearm did not violate the equal protection clause.

Sisto v. Aetna Cas. & Sur. Co.


CASE NO. 96-0133


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 438; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 2517; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 720



March 19, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Harry G. Hinckley, Jr., Judge; L.T. Case No. 91-02317-08.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, who were injured in an automobile accident, appealed from a jury verdict in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit (Florida), which awarded their past medical expenses only.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, who each claimed injuries in an automobile accident, appealed from a jury verdict that awarded their past medical expenses only. The trial court refused to permit any questioning as to whether prospective jurors had preconceived attitudes, opinions, or beliefs concerning damage awards in general, and in particular, non-economic damages, and the court found that the trial court's limitation on the scope of plaintiffs' voir dire interfered with the right of their counsel to conduct a reasonable examination and prevented meaningful voir dire on damages. The court noted that a prospective juror's attitude about personal injury lawsuits was an appropriate subject for inquiry. The fact that the jury limited its award to economic damages established demonstrable prejudice as a result of the trial court's refusal to permit any inquiry of the prospective jurors' views on damages. Thus, the court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial because the trial court abused its discretion by prohibiting plaintiffs' counsel from asking the panel any questions about their views on damages, including non-economic damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which limited plaintiffs' recovery for an automobile accident to past medical damages, and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion by prohibiting plaintiffs' counsel from asking the panel of prospective jurors any questions about their views on damages, including non-economic damages, in plaintiffs' personal injury suit.

Morse v. Moxley


CASE NO.: 97-114


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


691 So. 2d 504; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1899; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 607



March 7, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 15, 1997. Released for Publication May 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition, A Case of Original Jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: Order quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner court clerk filed a petition for a writ of prohibition against respondent circuit court judge who issued an administrative order. The order assigned certain trial clerks to judges, bypassing the power of petitioner court clerk.


OVERVIEW: Respondent circuit court judge entered an order that assigned certain trial court clerks to certain judges. The reason for the reassignment was that the present method of assignment was unacceptable to many of the judges. Petitioner court clerk sought a writ of prohibition against respondent. Petitioner contended that she had the power to fire deputy clerks and assign them to the position deemed most appropriate. Respondent contended that he acted under the authority of Fla. Stat. ch. 42.26 and Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.050(b)(6). Respondent contended that the plain meaning of the statute conferred upon him the power to assign clerks as he deemed appropriate to promote the efficient administration of justice in the courts. The court quashed respondent's order. The court held that the appropriate remedy was writ of certiorari as opposed to a writ of prohibition because prohibition was a preventative, rather than a corrective, remedy. It only acted to prevent the commission of the act, and was not an appropriate remedy to revoke an order already issued. The court concluded that respondent acted in excess of his jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court quashed respondent circuit court judge's order and the court treated the petition as one for certiorari because prohibition was a preventative, rather than a corrective remedy. The court found respondent acted in excess of his jurisdiction.

Murphy v. Tucker


Case No. 96-02359


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 1164; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1820; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 625



March 5, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 8, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Olin W. Shinholser, Acting Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which granted a judgment and attorney fees in favor of appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that a judgment in favor of appellee was improper because the lower court improperly applied Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(3) (1995) to the facts of the case. The reviewing court upheld the judgment on the grounds that the lower court did not err in applying that statute. However, the award of attorney fees to appellee was erroneous. Appellee made an offer of judgment pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 44.102 (1995), which had been declared unconstitutional and did not provide a substantive basis for an award of fees. Her only substantive basis would have been pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 (1995). Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 (1995) required that an offer be in writing and state that it was being made pursuant to this section, which was not done here. Statutes authorizing attorney's fees must be strictly construed.


OUTCOME: A decision that granted a judgment and attorney fees in favor of appellee was affirmed in part and reversed in part because there was no substantive basis for the award of attorney fees.

State v. Ball


CASE NO. 95-3677


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 1157; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1848; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 593



March 5, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1997. Released for Publication April 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Edward Garrison, Judge. L.T. Case No. 94-9722 CF A02.



DISPOSITION: Order granting Appellee's motion stricken, reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and county, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), directing appellants to pay attorneys' fees to appellee, who was acquitted on criminal charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was acquitted on criminal charges, and the trial court ordered appellants state and county to pay appellant's attorneys' fees. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The trial court lacked authority to make the order; no law entitled appellant to recover his expenses. Appellant, a non-indigent, was not a protected class for equal protection purposes, and the state had a rational basis for providing counsel to indigent defendants, who were presumably low-income, and for refusing to do so for non-indigents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order to pay attorneys' fees to appellee and remanded; the trial court did not have authority to direct appellants state and county to do so.

Brown v. State


CASE NO. 95-3997


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 1165; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1857; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 603



March 5, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certification Denied April 8, 1997. Released for Publication April 8, 1997. Petition for Review Denied July 31, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1275.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert S. Zack, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-14044CF10A.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for official misconduct, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 839.25 (1995).


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that defendant, a public employee, filed false time cards in order to obtain overtime pay. Defendant argued that he was not guilty of official misconduct under Fla. Stat. ch. 839.25(1) because a time card was not an official record or official document. The reviewing court disagreed and upheld his conviction. Official records or documents under Fla. Stat. ch. 839.25 (1995) were those used or prepared to carry out the administrative, public, or official business of a public agency. A public servant's time cards were official records within the meaning of the statute.

State v. Efthimiadis


CASE NO. 95-3463


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


690 So. 2d 1320; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1560; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 535



February 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Clarification Granted April 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 3957. Released for Publication May 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; June Johnson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-25814 MM10A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision, by the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida), in favor of appellee ship's captain granting appellee's motion to dismiss and holding Fla. Stat. ch. 327.02(37) (1994) unconstitutional on its face and Fla. Stat. ch. 327.10 (1993) unconstitutional as applied. Appellee had been cited for violating Fla. Stat. ch. 327.10 by charging appellee with operating an unregistered vessel on Florida waters.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted appellee ship captain's motion to dismiss and after the trial court held Fla. Stat. ch. 327.02(37) (1994), was unconstitutional on its face and Fla. Stat. ch. 327.10 (1993) unconstitutional as applied, appellee state sought review. The court held the trial court acted outside of its discretion in determining Fla. Stat. ch. 327.02(37) (1994) was unconstitutional. The trial court concerned itself unnecessarily with the possible constitutional infirmity of the statute's attempt to include the marginal sea and high seas within the jurisdictional purview of the state's regulatory authority. That concern was misplaced because the citation issued to the appellee was for a violation occurring well within the state's inter-coastal waters and well within the territorial limits of the state. It was a fundamental maxim of judicial restraint - ignored by the trial court below - courts were not to decide constitutional issues unnecessarily. The court held the purported selective enforcement of the statute was not unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. The mere failure to prosecute all offenders could not be a ground for a claim of equal protection denial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the motion to dismiss and remanded because the trial court, in concerning itself unnecessarily with the possible constitutional infirmity of the state's attempt to include the marginal high seas within the state's regulatory authority, ignored the fundamental maximum of judicial restrain not to decide constitutional issues unnecessarily.

Banks v. State


CASE NO. 93-0983


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


691 So. 2d 490; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1357; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 467



February 19, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 7, 1997. Rehearing Denied April 23, 1997. Released for Publication April 23, 1997. Review Denied September 11, 1997, Reported at: 699 So. 2d 1371, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1650.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Marvin Mounts, Jr., Judge. L.T. Case No. 92-5250 CFA02.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing En Banc for Withdrawn Opinion of September 13, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Fla. App. LEXIS 9637.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee filed a petition for rehearing and asked the appeals court to reconsider its decision of whether the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida) erred in denying appellant's motion for discharge under the "speedy trial" rule.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with second degree murder, attempted first degree murder, and shooting into a building. A not guilty plea was entered on May 4, 1992, and on that date the defense filed a demand for reciprocal discovery pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.220. The trial was set for May 26, 1992, without objection. Four days before trial, defense counsel requested a continuance on the ground that he had not received full discovery. The trial court granted the request, indicating that the delay would not be chargeable to the state. The trial was subsequently continued again and trial commenced in November, 207 days after appellant's arrest. On appeal, appellant contended that his speedy trial rights were violated. On rehearing, the appeals court withdrew its original opinion and held that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion for discharge under the speedy trial rule. The court reasoned that under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(j), since there were no allegations of state misconduct or other violation of defense discovery rights, appellant waived the 175-day speedy trial time by requesting a continuance. Thus, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion for discharge under the speedy trial rule, because appellant waived the 175-day speedy trial time by requesting a continuance.

The court found that compliance with the refund procedure was not required as a condition of bringing the instant action.

Newsweek, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


CASE NO. 96-1882


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


689 So. 2d 361; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 1125; 25 Media L. Rep. 1632; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 499



February 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1997. Released for Publication March 27, 1997. Petition for Review Denied July 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1234.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Judge William Gary.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff magazine corporation sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which denied its motion for summary judgment and granted the cross-motion for summary judgment of defendant, thereby denying plaintiff's request for a tax refund.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 212.05(1)(i) (1987), the state legislature imposed a sales tax on newspapers and magazines. However, beginning January 1, 1998, the legislature exempted newspapers from the tax. Upon review, the tax scheme was held unconstitutional. Therefore, on December 9, 1990, defendant state department of revenue began taxing both newspapers and magazines. Plaintiff magazine corporation sued claiming a refund of sales tax paid between January 1, 1988, and December 9, 1990. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted final summary judgment to defendant. On appeal, the court found that the trial court correctly ruled that plaintiff was not entitled to a refund under the Due Process Clauses of the United States and Florida Constitutions. The court concluded that the sales tax paid by plaintiff could properly have been contested in a pre-deprivation proceeding pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 72.011 (1987). Accordingly, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order, which denied plaintiff magazine corporation's motion for summary judgment and granted final summary judgment to defendant department, was affirmed because there was no due process violation in the state's failing to provide a refund or other retroactive relief where plaintiff had an adequate pre-deprivation remedy.
