773 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Neal v. State


CASE NO. 96-2939


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


688 So. 2d 392; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 929; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 416



February 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 13, 1997. Released for Publication March 13, 1997. Petition for Review Denied August 7, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1318.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Henry E. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; and REMANDED, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) that convicted him of grand theft auto, ordered him to pay restitution without holding an evidentiary hearing pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.089(7) (1995), ordered him to pay his public defender's fees without holding a hearing, and sentenced him to jail followed by community control. Appellant claimed that the sentence and payment orders were erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of grand theft auto, and the trial court sentenced him to a jail term followed by community control, and ordered him to pay the fees of his public defender and to pay restitution to the victim including lost wages and travel expenses incurred when she testified at trial. On appeal, the court held that although Fla. Stat. ch. 775.089(1)(a) (1995) allowed the victim to be reimbursed for her lost wages and travel expenses, the trial court erred by not holding an evidentiary hearing pursuant to ch. 775.089(7) (1995) on the restitution amount. Because appellant did not object to his sentence at trial, he was precluded by ch. 924.051(3) (1996) from objecting to his sentence on appeal. Because ch. 924.051(3) (1996) was a procedural law, it did not violate the constitutional ex post facto clauses although it became effective after appellant committed his crime. Because the failure of the court to hold a hearing on the public defender's fees was a plain error, appellant did not need to object to it at trial. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment with respect to the payment orders, affirmed it in all other respects, and remanded the case for the proper hearings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with respect to the orders to pay restitution and the public defender's fees, affirmed it in all other respects, and remanded the case for hearings on the restitution amount and public defender's fees, because appellant's failure to object to his sentence at trial precluded him from raising that issue on appeal, but the trial court could not order restitution or payment of public defender fees without a hearing.

 

774 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Sugarmill Woods Civic Ass'n v. Southern States Utils.


CASE NO. 95-425, CASE NO. 95-457


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


687 So. 2d 1346; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 365; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 373



February 4, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 4, 1997. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Florida Public Service Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants civic associations and a municipality sought review of orders from appellee Florida Public Service Commission, which set uniform statewide rates for water and wastewater customers of a utility's systems and set a separate rate for the systems.


OVERVIEW: After several actions between the parties regarding statewide rates for waste and wastewater customers (customers), appellee public service commission (PSC) decided that it had jurisdiction over appellee utility company's facilities throughout the state. In a previous action, PSC set uniform rates for customers. The trial court ruled that PSC exceeded its statutory authority when it approved statewide rates without making the requisite findings of whether the facilities comprised a single system. Based on that ruling, the appellate court reversed the order setting the uniform rates. However, the appellate court held that PSC properly ordered the cost of appellant municipality's bulk wastewater rate because it was supported by competent, substantial evidence. PSC chose the rate from eight alternative rates and selected a fair and reasonable one. The trial court also properly granted PSC's motion to quash subpoenas duces tecum that were served on a large number of its staff. The prehearing officer had discretion to grant the order based on the probability that the requests were a fishing expedition. Orders were affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The order relating to the cost of appellant municipality's bulk wastewater rate and the trial court's grant of appellee public service commission's motion to quash were affirmed. However, the order relating to uniform rates for customers was reversed.

Martin v. Martin


CASE NO. 95-1801


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


687 So. 2d 903; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 301; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 291



January 29, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 27, 1997. Released for Publication February 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; George A. Brescher, Judge; L.T. Case No. 93-17796 (25).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, sons of decedent, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) granting summary judgment for defendant widow in their suit against her for tortious interference with their inheritance rights.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the lower court's grant of summary judgment to defendant widow in an action by plaintiffs, sons of decedent, who claimed that she tortiously interfered with their inheritance rights by causing decedent to reduce over time the amount they would inherit. Defendant was decedent's second wife, who was a beneficiary of decedent's will and revocable trust agreement. Plaintiffs could recover from defendant, because they could not have obtained the relief they were seeking by attacking the will in probate. Because the assets in the inter vivos trust into which the will poured over were not part of the probate estate, they were also not subject to administration. The trust was not incorporated by reference into the will, because the will did not clearly show an intent on the part of the testator to incorporate the trust.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court grant of summary judgment for defendant widow, because the will did not show a clear intent to incorporate the inter vivos trust. Inter vivos trusts were not part of the estate, and could not be subject to administration.

Royal Selections v. Florida Dep't of Revenue


CASE NO. 95-4059


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


687 So. 2d 893; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 306; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 298



January 29, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Thomas E. Sholts, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 95-2658 AG.

This Opinion Substituted on Motion for Rehearing or Clarification for Withdrawn Opinion of September 4, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 9557.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Palm Beach County (Florida), which held that appellant was not entitled to a declaratory judgment as to the authority of appellee tax collector to collect title search fees in connection with the application for a tax deed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation sought review of the trial court's order, which held that appellant's declaratory judgment complaint failed to state a cause of action. The complaint alleged that appellee tax collector's collection of title search fees from a tax deed applicant as part of the tax deed application process was an unlawful and constitutional exercise of legislative authority. The trial court dismissed the complaint on the grounds that such action by appellee was constitutional and that appellant's complaint failed to state a claim. In substituting the instant opinion for its prior decision, the appellate court reversed the trial court's order. The appellate court held that appellant was entitled to have a declaratory determination of the authority by which appellee charged the title search fee because both the validity of statutes and the validity of administrative regulations were proper subjects for declaratory decrees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order of dismissal and remanded for further proceedings. The appellate court held that the validity of administrative regulations were proper subjects for declaratory decrees and concluded that appellant corporation was entitled to a declaratory determination of the power by which appellee tax collector charged a title search fee as part of the tax deed application process.

Bunn v. State


CASE NO. 95-2672


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


687 So. 2d 879; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 200; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 247



January 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; C.E. Smith, Judge; L.T. Case No. 95-298.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a probation order of the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County (Florida), raising three issues concerning his judgment and conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted at trial, raised three issues on appeal. First, appellant argued that the trial court erred by increasing his sentence in violation of the double jeopardy clause of the United States Constitution. The court found no merit to this claim and affirmed the decision of the trial court. Secondly, appellant argued that the written conditions of probation requiring him to submit to random drug testing at his own expense were to be stricken as they were not orally imposed by the trial court at sentencing. The court agreed with appellant and remanded to the trial court in order to strike down the condition, which required appellant to pay for the drug testing. Likewise, the court determined that other special conditions of probation had to be orally pronounced at sentencing and were to be stricken as well for the court's failure to do so. Finally, appellant challenged the constitutionality of Fla. Sat. ch. 948.01(13)(a) (1993), contending that the drug offender probation statute constituted an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to an administrative agency. The court rejected this argument after reviewing applicable case law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to increase appellant's sentence and to uphold the Florida drug offender probation statute as constitutional. The court reversed the trial court's order imposing special conditions upon appellant's probation because the conditions were required to be announced orally at sentencing and the trial court failed to do so.

Nemeth v. Florida Dep't of Revenue


CASE NO. 95-3096


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


686 So. 2d 778; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 201; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 249



January 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; Scott M. Kenney, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-1144 CA 17.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED; QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax payers sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida) which dismissed appellants' complaint with prejudice regarding their action against appellee department of revenue challenging the constitutionality of the Florida Vehicle Impact Fee, Fla. Stat. ch. 320.072(1)(b) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Appellant tax payers sought review of an order by the trial court which dismissed with prejudice their complaint against appellee tax revenue department for failure to file a claim for refund as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 215.26(2) (1994). Appellants' complaint challenged the constitutionality of the Florida Vehicle Impact Fee, Fla. Stat. ch. 320.072(1)(b) (1990) and sought a refund for taxes paid. Appellants argued that the trial court erred in dismissing their complaint and the court upon review agreed. The court addressed a rule of the Florida Supreme Court which held that persons who paid the impact fee pursuant to a statute similar to ch. 320.072(1)(b) had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute and seek a refund for taxes paid. The state argued that appellants lacked standing for failure to comply with the one year filing requirements under ch. 215.26. Following the rule of the supreme court, the court determined that contrary to appellee's argument, appellants need not pay the fee or request a refund as the fact that they faced penalties for failure to pay an alleged unconstitutional tax was sufficient to create standing under state law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the trial court which dismissed appellant taxpayers' claim with prejudice because the fact that appellants potentially faced penalties for failing to pay an allegedly unconstitutional tax was sufficient to create standing under state law and appellants were not required to file an application for refund with appellee tax revenue department to challenge the constitutionality of a tax.

Welborn v. State


CASE NO. 94-3005


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


687 So. 2d 35; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 125; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 215



January 15, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Dwight L. Geiger, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-209CFA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS TO STRIKE CONDITIONS (9), (11), AND (12).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida) sentencing him and placing conditions on his drug offender probation pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13)(a).


OVERVIEW: Following his plea of nolo contendere to possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and use or possession of drug paraphernalia, appellant was sentenced and placed on drug offender probation for two years. On appeal, appellant contended that the conditions of drug offender probation imposed under Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13)(a) were not orally pronounced and should be stricken. The court held that the conditions that were statutorily imposed did not need to be orally pronounced. However, those conditions that were neither statutorily imposed nor listed in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.986(e) were special conditions that had to be orally pronounced. Accordingly, the court reversed appellant's sentence and remanded to the trial court with direction to strike special conditions that were not orally pronounced.


OUTCOME: The order sentencing appellant on drug charges and placing conditions for his drug offender probation was reversed and remanded with direction to strike conditions imposed that were not based on a statute or rule of court and that were not orally pronounced.

State v. Conforti


CASE NOS. 95-0299 and 95-1299


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


688 So. 2d 350; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 73; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 144



January 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 11, 1997. Released for Publication February 11, 1997. Petition for Review Denied June 23, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1158.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Zebedee W. Wright, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 93-9723MM10A and 93-9724MM10A.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, information reinstated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which had dismissed lewdness charges against appellee suspects on the grounds that Fla. Stat. ch. 796.07(1)(b) (1991), which defined lewdness as any indecent or obscene act, was unconstitutional under the U.S. and Florida Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court reversed the dismissal order, finding that the lewd conduct at issue in the instant case was not expressive conduct protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The appellate court further found that the determination that the sexual conduct in question was unprotected under U.S. Const. amend. I also compelled the conclusion that the Miller test regarding expressive material was inapplicable to the instant case, noting that Fla. Stat. ch. 796.07 regulated actual physical conduct. Accordingly, the appellate court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 769.07(1)(b) (1991) was constitutional on its face, rejecting the void for vagueness and overbreadth arguments because the narrowly drawn statute did give people of ordinary intelligence fair notice of what constituted forbidden conduct. The appellate court remanded for a reinstatement of the information against appellee suspects, finding that the lewdness charges did not violate appellees' right to privacy under the state constitution because they had no legitimate expectation of privacy in the conduct performed at a place where the public could patronize.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the dismissal of the lewdness charges against appellee suspects and remanded for reinstatement of the criminal information; the charging statute was facially constitutional, the expressive conduct at issue was not protected under the First Amendment, and appellees' privacy rights were not violated where they had no legitimate expectation of privacy in the conduct which formed the basis of the criminal charges.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer and imposing a sentence that included probation and community control.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer. The jury returned a guilty verdict and a sentence was imposed which included probation and community control. The conviction and the remainder of the sentence were affirmed without comment.

Pompey v. Cochran


CASE NO. 93-3181


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


685 So. 2d 1007; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 87; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 151



January 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus to the Circuit Court of the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County, Estella May Moriarty and John A. Frusciante, Judges, L.T. Case No. 93-6677 38.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus granted. Question of great public importance certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former spouse sought writ of habeas corpus to the Circuit Court of the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which imposed incarceration on petitioner upon a finding of civil contempt for his willful failure to comply with a child support order.


OVERVIEW: Although petitioner former spouse had been released from confinement prior to the decision of the instant court, the court granted the petition for writ of habeas corpus, finding that the significance of the issues regarding the extent of its jurisdiction on habeas corpus relief in civil contempt proceedings, as well as the proper interpretation of the requirements to civil contempt incarceration, necessitated such a review. In support of his request for habeas relief, petitioner contended that his incarceration was illegal because he did not have the ability to pay the purge amount set by the issuing court. The court found that where there was neither an affirmative finding nor evidence in the record that petitioner, at the time of his incarceration for civil contempt, had the ability to pay the purge amount and thus to obtain his release from confinement, the incarceration was unlawful and petition for writ of habeas corpus was to be granted. The court concluded by certifying questions of great public importance to the state Supreme Court regarding the issues involved in imposing incarceration upon a finding of civil contempt in family support cases.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the petition for writ of habeas corpus, holding that where petitioner former spouse was in civil contempt for his failure to pay child support, and the trial court had determined that incarceration was the appropriate method to coerce compliance, the setting of a purge amount without any finding that petitioner had the present ability to pay the purge amount constituted a violation of petitioner's due process rights.

State v. J.A.S.


Case Nos. 95-2261 & 95-2439


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


686 So. 2d 1366; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 26; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 124



January 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Victor J. Musleh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida), which dismissed the charges of statutory rape against appellee juvenile offenders, who engaged in consensual sex with two 12 year-old-girls, because Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04 (1993) unconstitutionally violated appellees' rights to privacy and equal protection under the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee juvenile offenders were two 15-year-old boys, who engaged in "consensual" sex with two 12-year-old girls. Although appellees were charged with violations of Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04 (1993), the girls were not charged. The trial court dismissed the charges and held that the statute was unconstitutional as applied appellees because the statute violated their right to privacy and equal protection under the law. Appellant state produced a record of numerous past referrals and adjudications to indicate why appellees were charged and the girls were not. The court held that whatever rights to privacy minors under 16 had, it did not include a right to engage in recreational sex with a minor also under the age of 16 because the costs and risks to society and the children involved were far too great. The court found that the crime was no less harmful than any other that may have been committed by a minor. The court vacated the dismissal of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings because appellant had a compelling interest in preventing such conduct and its consequences.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's dismissal of the charges of statutory rape against appellee juvenile offenders, and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that the constitutional rights of appellees to privacy and equal protection under the law were not violated because appellant state provided evidence of repeated adjudications for similar offenses by appellees.

 

785 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Washington v. Burk


CASE NO.: 96-1404


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


704 So. 2d 540; 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 32; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 120



January 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition, A Case of Original Jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of prohibition against respondents, circuit court judge and others, to declare that petitioner's impending trial for indirect criminal contempt of court was barred by the speedy trial rule of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that the speedy trial rule of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191 should have been applied to her indirect contempt proceeding. The county had declined criminal prosecution and the state had later filed an indirect criminal contempt action. The court granted petitioner's writ of prohibition against respondents, circuit court judge and others. The court overruled the previous case law that held that the speedy trial rule did not apply to indirect criminal contempt prosecution. The court found that certain legislative changes made the premises behind the previous case law outdated. The court also found that indirect criminal contempt was a criminal proceeding, and that pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.010, the rules applied to indirect criminal contempt. Finally, the court determined that the speedy trial time began to run from the time of petitioner's arrest and not with the subsequent service of a show cause order.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's writ of prohibition against respondents, circuit court judge and others, because the speedy trial rule applied to an indirect contempt proceeding against petitioner. The court held that petitioner's speedy trial time began to run from her arrest and not from the service of a show cause order.

Tory v. State


CASE NO. 94-2085


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


686 So. 2d 689; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 13402; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 89



December 26, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County; James B. Balsiger, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-432.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded with directions to strike conditions (10), (12) and (13) and to clarify the sentencing order to resolve conflict between the written order and oral pronouncement.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of convictions from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Indian River County, (Florida) of possession of cocaine, possession of less than 20 grams of cannabis, driving while license suspended, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Appellant argued, inter alia, the written sentence did not comport with oral pronouncement and Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13)(a)(1993) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of conviction of possession of cocaine, possession of cannabis, driving while license suspended, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Appellant contended the trial court's written sentence did not comport with the oral pronouncement. The appellate concluded that absent concession by the prosecution, a conflict between the written order and the oral pronouncement required a factual resolution by the trial court. Appellant argued the trial court erred by imposing standard conditions of probation provided in Fla. Stat. ch. 948.03(1), which were not orally pronounced at sentencing. The court concluded that certain conditions should have been orally pronounced and must be stricken. Appellant contended Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13)(a), establishing drug offender probation, was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to an administrative agency in violation of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.The appellate court held statutes were not unlawful delegations of legislative power when the power sought to be exercised was a technical issue of implementation and not a fundamental policy decision. The constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13)(a) was upheld.


OUTCOME: In an appeal from criminal convictions, the judgment was affirmed in part and remanded with directions to strike certain conditions of probation and to clarify the sentencing order to resolve conflict between the written order and oral pronouncement. Florida statute establishing drug offender probation was not unconstitutional.

 

788 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. A.R.S.


CASE NO. 96-333


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


684 So. 2d 1383; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 13159; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 29



December 19, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. John Crusoe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order dismissing Counts I and II of the delinquency petition reversed, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which dismissed two counts of a delinquency petition charging appellee juvenile with unlawful sexual acts with a minor, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(2) and (3).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a delinquency petition charging appellee juvenile with unlawful sexual acts with a minor, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(2) and (3). A trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss two counts of the petition on the grounds of equal protection and the right to privacy. On appeal, the court stated that appellee failed to show that others similarly situated were not prosecuted. Appellee also failed to establish that the prosecutor's intent was to discriminate on an improper basis. Therefore, appellee's right to equal protection was not violated. The court also found that Fla. Stat. ch. 827.071(2) and (3) did not violate appellee's right to privacy. The purpose of the statute was to protect minors from exploitation by anyone who induced them to appear in a sexual performance and showed that performance to other people. The purpose applied to adults as well as minors. Appellee violated the statute by videotaping himself and a younger minor female engaged in sexual foreplay and showing the tape to a third person. Therefore, the trial court's order was reversed and the cause remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that dismissed two counts of a delinquency petition against appellee juvenile was reversed and remanded because appellee failed to show that his right to equal protection or his right to privacy was violated when he was charged with unlawful sexual acts with a minor.

Sunshine Key Assocs. Ltd. Pshp. v. Monroe County


CASE NO. 95-1944


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


684 So. 2d 876; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 13140; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 10



December 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Sandra G. Taylor, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 93-267.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant recreational vehicle park operator and owner sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Florida), which entered a judgment in favor of appellee county by upholding the constitutionality of Monroe County, Fla., Code § 9.5-4. Appellant had filed suit against appellee seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, and damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county determined that certain park models of recreational vehicles were no longer allowed in land-use districts designated for recreational vehicles. Appellee began proceedings against appellant recreational vehicle park operator and owner. Appellee filed an administrative appeal, arguing the classification of park models as mobile homes was arbitrary and without reason. The appeal was heard and denied. Appellant sought review of the denial from the board of county commissioner, but the board denied the appeal. Appellant then filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, and damages. The lower court entered judgment in appellee's favor. The appellate court reversed and remanded for further proceedings, holding that appellant's constitutional claim was not barred by the doctrine of administrative res judicata. The appellate court further held that to the extent Monroe County, Fla., Code § 9.5-4 defined recreational vehicles as not exceeding eight feet in width, the regulation was arbitrary, and therefore unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The decision from the lower court which entered judgment in favor of appellee county by upholding the validity of an ordinance regulating recreational vehicles was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The appellate court determined that the width distinction in the regulation defining recreational vehicles was arbitrary and, as such, unenforceable.

 

790 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Verdi v. Metropolitan Dade County


CASE NO. 95-3416


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


684 So. 2d 870; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 13142; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 8



December 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 3, 1997. Petition for Review Denied May 23, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 792.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Philip Bloom, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 94-20256.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a final order from the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which dismissed an amended class action complaint against appellee municipality on the ground that it was barred by the doctrine of res judicata. A motion for rehearing was also denied. Appellant contended that he had not been given the opportunity to contest civil fines assessed for violations of the county code.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty and fined for violations of a municipal code. He instituted an action against appellee municipality on behalf of himself and others similarly situated who had been fined by appellee for violations of the code but who had not been given the opportunity to contest them in a municipal court. The trial court dismissed the action, ruling that it was barred by the doctrine of res judicata because appellant did not directly appeal a hearing officer's findings that appellant violated the municipal code. On appeal, the court determined that appellee had statutory authority to enforce its municipal code. Appellee was also permitted to adopt, by ordinance, a completely alternative code enforcement system to permit either a code enforcement board or an administrative hearing officer to conduct hearings and assess fines for code violations. The hearing's officers findings and imposition of fines and costs against appellant were not void and did not violate the separation of powers provisions of the state constitution. The code enforcement proceedings were quasi-judicial in nature and were therefore constitutionally authorized. Therefore, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's final order that dismissed an amended class action complaint and denied a motion for rehearing was affirmed. Appellant's action was barred by the doctrine of res judicata, appellee municipality had statutory authority to enforce its municipal code, and the quasi-judicial code enforcement proceedings were constitutional.

Busbee v. Division of Retirement


CASE NO. 96-1131


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


685 So. 2d 914; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 13594; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 45



December 17, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Department of Management Services, Division of Retirement.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of an order from the Department of Management Services, Division of Retirement (Florida), which determined that appellant forfeited his right to receive benefits under the State of Florida Retirement System as a result of his plea of guilty to the charge of accepting a bribe in connection with his employment.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Division of Retirement determined that appellant claimant forfeited his right to receive benefits under the state of Florida Retirement System (FRS) as a result of his plea of guilty in federal court to the charge of accepting a bribe in connection with his employment. On review, appellant argued that the forfeiture of his pension rights unconstitutionally retroactively took his vested property rights and violated the prohibitions in the state and federal constitutions against the impairment of contracts because he did not commit his crime until after his rights to his pension had vested. The court found no merit in appellant's arguments because, when he voluntarily elected to become a member of the FRS, the governing statutes contained the express provision that conviction for bribery in connection with one's employment resulted in forfeiture of pension rights. Therefore, the forfeiture provision was a part of the pension contract between appellant and appellee state, and to the extent that his rights vested after 10 years of service, they vested subject to this provision. Accordingly, the order, which denied appellant benefits, was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order, which determined that appellant claimant forfeited his right to receive retirement benefits, was affirmed because there was no merit in appellant's arguments that such forfeiture was unconstitutional. The forfeiture provision was part of the pension contract when entered into and appellant's rights vested subject to that provision.

Metro. Dade County v. Fonte


CASE NO. 96-1647


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


683 So. 2d 1117; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 12818; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2615



December 11, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 27, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Milton Friedman, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 93-9070.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county and appellee gas station owners challenged a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which assessed a $ 10,000 fine against appellees for violating a settlement agreement in an action to correct ground water pollution.


OVERVIEW: In an action to correct ground water pollution, appellant county and appellee gas station owners mediated a settlement agreement in which appellees agreed to pay a fine of $ 10,000 if they complied with a plan to remedy pollution and $ 30,000 if they did not. Appellees did not comply with the plan, but the trial judge ordered appellees to pay only $ 10,000. The court reversed and found that there was no doubt that, by eliminating their exposure to far greater liability in the lawsuit, appellees received ample consideration for the settlement agreement and could not equitably be permitted to repudiate it. The court held that because there was no question of appellees' violation or the consequences, the payment of $ 30,000, which resulted from the breach, the trial court was required to enter judgment accordingly. The court directed the trial court to increase the amount that appellees were required to pay from $ 10,000 to $ 30,000.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that assessed a smaller fine against appellee gas station owners and held that the trial court was required to enter judgment for a fine of $ 30,000. The court noted that there was no question of appellees' violation of a settlement agreement or of the consequences that resulted from the breach. The court directed the trial court to increase the amount of appellees' fine from $ 10,000 to $ 30,000.

Ward v. Dibble


CASE NO. 95-2480


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


683 So. 2d 666; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 14335; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2587



December 6, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Citrus County, Hale R. Stancil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father and widower appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Citrus County (Florida) awarding appellee grandmother, mother of appellant's deceased spouse, visitation with his children pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 752.01(1) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant father and widower appealed an order of the lower court awarding appellee grandmother, mother of his deceased spouse, visitation with his children, asserting that visitation was not shown to be in the best interests of the children. Appellee had filed a petition pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 752.01(1) (1993) for an order allowing her specified visitation with the grandchildren at appellee's home in New York. Appellant was willing to allow visitation at his home in Florida, but objected to visitation at appellee's home in New York because of his poor relationship with appellee. The visitation order was granted. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erroneously presumed that visitation between a grandparent and grandchild was in the children's best interests, shifting the burden to appellant to justify his decision against visitation with appellee. Appellee bore the burden of establishing by competent evidence that visitation with her was in the best interests of each of her grandchildren. The court reversed the order and remanded the case; the determination was unsupported by substantial, competent evidence that visitation was in each grandchild's best interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order and remanded the case, holding that there was no competent evidence that the order compelling appellant father to allow appellee grandmother visitation with his children in appellee's state of residence was in the children's best interests.

Strohm v. Hertz Corp./Hertz Claim Mgmt.


CASE NO. 95-3233


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


685 So. 2d 37; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 12762; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2570



December 5, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims Judith Nelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an insured employee, challenged an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims (Florida) which allowed appellees, an insurer and employer, to deauthorize chiropractic care for appellant under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(2)(a) (Supp. 1994). Appellant argued that the statute unconstitutionally violated his right of access to courts under the Fla. Const. art. I, § 21 and denied him due process and equal protection under the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an insured employee, suffered injury in a workplace accident. Appellees, an insurer and employer, authorized chiropractic care. Upon appellees' request to deauthorize that care under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(2)(a) (Supp. 1994), a judge of compensation claims entered such an order. Appellant challenged that determination by arguing that ch. 440.13(2)(a) unconstitutionally violated his right of access to the courts under the Fla. Const. art. I, § 21 and denied him due process and equal protection under the law. The court found that appellant failed to assert or show that he had a common law right to chiropractic care prior to the adoption of the Florida Constitution and ruled that ch. 440.13(2)(a) did not restrict his right to proper treatment. Therefore, the court held that this statute did not eliminate a common law right of action. The court held that ch. 440.13(2)(a) did not deny due process because appellant was allowed a fair hearing. The court held that this statute did not deny equal protection of the law because it was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and did not create an improper classification. The court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the judge of compensation claims which deauthorized chiropractic care from appellees, an insurer and employer, for appellant, an insured employee, under a Florida statute. The court held that the statute was constitutional because it allowed court access under the Florida Constitution, afforded due process, and was rationally related to a legitimate state interest without having any improper classifications.

Rucker v. City of Ocala


CASE NO. 95-3224


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


684 So. 2d 836; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 12761; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2567



December 5, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1997. Released for Publication January 10, 1997. Petition for Review February 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 358.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims Jonathan D. Ohlman.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee, a claimant for worker's compensation benefits, sought review of an order of the judge of compensation claims (Florida), which granted the request to exclude appellant's proferred medical expert's testimony under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(5)(e) (Supp. 1994) and then, in a formal order, denied appellant's petition for benefits.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court rejected appellant employee's argument that the interpretation of the term "authorized treating provider" in Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(5)(e) (Supp. 1994) to exclude his medical expert's testimony was error, finding that the term was properly interpreted as meaning treating providers authorized by appellee employer/servicing agent. The court then found that the statute's application did not cause a procedural due process violation, noting that although appellant was somewhat limited in the medical opinions he could have used, he had not been completely denied the right to present evidence. The court also found that the statute did not violate appellant's right of access to the courts because his cause of action, despite being restricted in the range of medical witnesses available to prove entitlement to worker's compensation benefits, had not been eliminated. The court affirmed, rejecting the contention that the statute was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection guarantees because appellant failed to show that any classificatory scheme created by the statute could not have rationally advanced a legitimate governmental objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant employee's request for worker's compensation benefits following the refusal to allow the admission of appellant's medical witness' testimony; the challenged statute, although limiting in its effect on appellant's ability to use medical opinions to support his claim, was constitutional, given that it did not violate appellant's due process or equal protection rights or his right of access to the courts.

State v. Barnes


Case No. 96-01047


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


686 So. 2d 633; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 12463; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2515



November 27, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 17, 1997. Released for Publication February 5, 1997. Petition for Review Denied May 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 813.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Robert A. Young, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2) (1995) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the lower court's holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(2) (1995) was unconstitutionally vague. The statute, which prohibited fleeing or attempting to elude a police officer, was found to be constitutional, including the disputed section. Under a portion of the statute there was an enhanced penalty for engaging in a high-speed chase with police. The lower court struck down this portion of the statute. On appeal by appellant state, the court held that appellee's vagueness challenge to the statute should have been examined in light of the specific facts of his case and not under standards applied to freedoms protected by the U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found that the statute, especially the contested portion, was not void for vagueness because appellee could reasonably understand that his contemplated conduct was proscribed. The court held that appellee failed to show that the statute was facially unconstitutional in that there existed no set of circumstances in which it could be constitutionally applied. Because appellee failed in this heavy burden, the case was reversed in favor of appellant state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's holding that a statute prohibiting fleeing and eluding a police officer by means of a high-speed chase, was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that appellee was unable to show that the statute was facially void and that there existed no set of circumstances in which it could be constitutionally applied.

Rodriguez v. Chiles


CASE NO. 96-739


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


694 So. 2d 53; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 12434; 22 Fla. L. Weekly D 628



November 26, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected on Denial of Rehearing March 5, 1997. Released for Publication March 21, 1997. Petition for Review Denied June 26, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1140. Certiorari Denied November 3, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6649.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Philip J. Padovano, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) that affirmed the denial of his clemency request, arguing that amended procedural rules violated the ex post facto clause in application.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an inmate in a state correctional system, filed a clemency request, which was denied based upon rules 5 and 8 of the Rules of Executive Clemency, which precluded appellant from applying for a commutation of an active sentence without waiver of the rules. He challenged the denial, arguing that the amended rules, which required a waiver not previously mandated, violated the ex post facto clause in application to him. The circuit court affirmed the denial, and appellant sought further review. The appellate court affirmed the circuit court judgment, concluding that the challenged rule amendment did not impose a constitutionally objectionable condition on appellant's access to consideration by the Board of Executive Clemency. Appellant had been considered for clemency during the waiver proceedings, and the parole commission and the state's governor had reviewed the merits of his case prior to the denial. The rule amendment was simply a procedural change and did not diminish appellant's substantive rights.


OUTCOME: The circuit court order affirming the denial of appellant's clemency request was affirmed, because the amendment of the rules applicable to clemency requests did not impose a constitutionally objectionable condition on appellant's access to consideration for clemency and did not diminish appellant's substantive rights but simply reflected a procedural change.

State v. Raleigh


CASE NO. 95-2832 & 95-3173


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


686 So. 2d 621; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 11973; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2458



November 15, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1997. Released for Publication January 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Certiorari Review of Order from the Circuit Court for Brevard County. Jere E. Lober, Judge.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought certiorari to quash orders of the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) which allowed respondent criminal defendant to assert consent of victim minors as a defense to charges of lewd assault, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04.


OVERVIEW: Respondent criminal defendant was between sixteen and seventeen years old when he was charged with lewd assault involving some victims who were aged fifteen. Respondent raised consent of the victims as a defense. He moved to dismiss the charges, asserting that Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04, under which he was charged, was unconstitutional as applied to him because it precluded his raising as defense the consent of the victims. The trial court allowed respondent to assert the defense. The state petitioned, seeking certiorari to quash orders of the lower court. The court granted the writ and quashed the orders. The court held that the interest of the state in protecting children was more compelling than a minor's right to privacy. It ruled that the disallowance of consent of the victims as a defense did not render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of certiorari sought by the state to quash orders allowing respondent to assert consent as a defense to charges of lewd assault because the state's compelling interest in protecting children outweighed respondent's right to privacy.

M.C.L. v. State


CASE NO. 95-3409; 95-4544


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


682 So. 2d 1209; 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 11916; 21 Fla. L. Weekly D 2445



November 13, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. McCarthy Crenshaw Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for consistent proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and his parents challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), which adjudicated appellant delinquent, committed appellant to high-risk juvenile detention, imposed immediate conditions regarding moral and spiritual training and media interviews, and ordered restitution.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge adjudicated appellant delinquent, committed him to high-risk juvenile detention, imposed conditions regarding moral and spiritual training and media interviews, and ordered restitution. Appellant and his parents appealed the terms of the order. The court affirmed all the terms except restitution. The court held that the moral training program was valid under both the state and federal constitutions. However, it modified the condition by deleting the words "and spiritual." The court held the ban on media interviews was valid as well because the condition bore a relationship to appellant's crimes. The court held that the court-imposed participation by appellant's mother was also valid because the trial court acted within the dispositional power expressly granted to it by the statute. The court reversed the order of restitution holding that since the hearing on the matter of restitution was held after appellant's notice of appeal was filed, the order imposing restitution was without effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the order imposing conditions regarding moral training and media interviews. The court deleted that part of the order regarding spiritual training however. The court reversed that part of the order regarding restitution and remanded for further proceedings.
